DEDICATION
This year’s book is dedicated to the generation born with Pluto in Leo and Neptune in Libra. This 
includes many of the so-called “baby boomers.” What sets this generation apart? Why has it been so 
maligned by others? And why dedicate this year’s book to the Pluto-in-Leo, Neptune-in-Libra gen-
eration (i.e., my generation)? 
First, with Pluto in Leo, you gave new importance to the values of fun and happiness. I don’t 
see any other generation in my lifetime enjoying life as much as we have. Sure, we have been self-
centered, which may disturb those who think we have not cared about future generations—but that is 
not entirely true. We have been colorful, discovered ways to live longer and healthier, and seem never 
to end the quest for happiness! In the words of Bob Dylan, this generation believes in being “Forever 
Young,” regardless of chronological age.
Second, with Neptune in Libra, this generation has lived the altruistic quest for both world peace 
and love. They have sought romance and the experience of an active, mobile life. This generation typi-
cally sees the best in others, starting relationships with trust until proven otherwise. There is a quality of 
innocence and playful joy in interacting with others. There is an uplifting delight and a sense of freedom 
in dancing and music. The music of this generation has transformed cultures around the world. Musi-
cians have been this generation’s philosophers, stimulating revolutionary thinking that has brought its 
population together in a communal bond of shared values, even if unconventional at times.
Through the relentless search for truth, this generation’s exploration of studies such as astrology, 
metaphysics, meditation, and Far Eastern philosophies has opened up new areas of understanding and 
ways to cope with the monumental changes that have occurred in our lifetime. This generation has 
truly led humankind into a new consciousness. You have been the leaders of the modern-day astrol-
ogy movement! And so, this year’s book is dedicated to all members of that generation who continue 
to uphold these ideals.

 MARKET TERMINOLOGY USED IN THIS BOOK
The following are terms that the reader will find throughout this book, especially in the Financial 
Markets sections.
Cycle: A measurable phenomenon that recurs consistently at regular intervals of time. In markets, 
cycles are measured from trough (lowest point) to trough unless specified otherwise.
Trough: A low in price; the bottom of a cycle, where the cycle ends and begins.
Crest: The peak of a cycle; the highest price between the troughs that define the cycle.
Phase: A sub-cycle within each cycle. Each cycle is composed of two or three sub-cycles, or phases, 
which are approximately one-half or one-third of the greater cycle’s length.
Cycle pattern: There are three common cycle patterns: 
•	
The classical three-phase pattern, in which there are three sub-cycles (or phases) of approxi-
mately one-third the greater cycle length
•	
The classical two-phase pattern, consisting of two sub-cycles (or phases) of approximately 
one-half the greater cycle length
•	
A combination pattern, which has sub-cycles at both the one-half and one-third intervals of 
the greater cycle
Bull market: Consecutive higher crests and higher troughs of the same cycle type; often associated 
with right translation patterns of primary cycles. Right translation means the crest occurs in the 
second half of the cycle, past its midpoint.
Bear market: Consecutive lower troughs and lower crests of the same cycle type; often associated 
with left translation patterns of primary cycles. Left translation means the crest occurs in the first 
half of the cycle.
Trend: Either bullish or bearish, depending on the cycle being studied. The first phase of a cycle is 
always bullish, and the last is usually bearish.
Support: An area below the current market price where prices are expected to hold on declines—a 
“floor” for prices.
Resistance: An area above the current market price where prices are expected to hold on rallies—a 
“ceiling” for prices.
Treasury values: In the chapter on T-Notes and Interest Rates, prices for T-Notes are quoted in 
values of 1/32 of a point. For instance, a value of 130/25 means 130 and 25/32 of a point. This is 
the standard quoting convention for Treasuries.
For further information on understanding market and cycle terminology, the reader is advised to 
consult the author’s work entitled Merriman on Market Cycles: The Basics.
## Page 7

3
 GEOCOSMIC TERMINOLOGY USED IN THIS BOOK
Conjunction: An aspect that occurs when two planets are in the same sign and degree of the zodiac. 
They appear to be together. A conjunction marks the starting point of a cycle involving those 
two planets. 
Opposition: An aspect that occurs when two planets are in opposite signs and degrees of the zodiac. 
They appear to be on opposite sides of the sky—when one sets in the west, the other rises in the 
east. An opposition represents the halfway point of a cycle involving those two planets. It marks 
the culmination of the themes, or the peak of the cycle, which began with their conjunction.
Square: An aspect that occurs when two planets are 90 degrees apart in the zodiac. They appear to 
be at a right angle—perpendicular to one another. A square represents the first (opening) and last 
(closing) quarter phases of a cycle involving those two planets.
Trine: An aspect that occurs when two planets are 120 degrees apart in the zodiac. A trine represents 
the first-third and last-third phases of a cycle involving those two planets. Trines are considered 
soft or harmonious aspects, along with the sextile (60 degrees, or one-sixth of the zodiac circle).
Hard aspects: The conjunction, square, and opposition are considered the hard aspects in astrology. 
They are challenging and difficult, representing the urge to force conflicting dynamics to work 
together.
T-square: A pattern in which two planets are in opposition, with both square to a third planet.
Grand square: A pattern in which four planets form consecutive squares to one another. It consists 
of two pairs of oppositions, with each pair also square to the other pair.
Grand trine: A pattern in which three planets form consecutive trines to one another. It appears 
as an equilateral triangle in the heavens and is considered the most fortunate of all planetary 
configurations.
Cardinal signs: Every third sign, starting with Aries, followed by Cancer, Libra, and Capricorn. 
Cardinal signs mark the beginning of each season and are associated with action and initiation.
Fixed signs: Every third sign, starting with Taurus, followed by Leo, Scorpio, and Aquarius. Fixed 
signs occupy the middle of each season. They stabilize and maintain the energy initiated by car-
dinal signs and are said to be steadfast, persistent, and sometimes stubborn.
Mutable signs: Every third sign, starting with Gemini, followed by Virgo, Sagittarius, and Pisces. 
Mutable signs close each season and represent change, adaptability, and flexibility.

 ABOUT THE 2026 FRONT COVER
This year’s Forecast 2026 book cover is the work of creative graphic designers Kat Powell of 
Denver, Colorado, and Antonia Langsdorf-Merriman of Cologne, Germany (now Miami, Florida). 
The design is symbolic of the past, present, and future.
Notice the book the children are reading. It represents a compilation of the past 50 years during 
which this annual Forecast book has been published. That’s right—we are celebrating the 50th year 
of publishing our Forecast books! The book in the children’s hands symbolizes these 50 years, a 
period during which we have identified the major cosmic events of each year and shown how they 
likely correlated with collective psychology and human activity in the spheres of global and national 
economics, politics, sociopolitical trends, and financial markets.
The children themselves represent the future. They are the youth who will determine the course 
humankind takes in the years ahead. Note their diversity: they are of different sexes and nationali-
ties. Yet there are no barriers preventing them from being fully engaged with one another. This is the 
future of the world in which racial and gender differences become meaningless as a basis for interac-
tion. The politics of polarization and propaganda that have divided the world over the past 50 years 
will eventually come to an end—and will, in fact, have come to an end—as humankind grows into 
this “New Aira,” identified in the annual Forecast books as unfolding between 2020 and 2032. 
The backdrop of this image shows a red-colored nebula lighting up the heavens. This celestial 
phenomenon symbolizes the “Aries Vortex” of 2025-2027, which culminates on February 20, 2026. 
It also reflects the present state of our solar system, marked by the unusually rare configuration of 
Uranus and Pluto in a favorable trine aspect. The midpoint of this trine is 0° Aries, the degree where 
Saturn and Neptune join together in 2025-2026. Aries, ruled by Mars—the “red planet” of war and 
conflict—is also the sign of new beginnings. It signifies a time of epic change, transformation, and 
turbulence. For this reason, it is depicted as a whirling mass of red activity above the otherwise 
peaceful and beautiful Earth. In the background, the innocent children are shown without social or 
meaningless barriers, united in their quest to understand the present and future by reading the books 
of the past. 
The children (the future) are surrounded by books. A home with a library symbolizes security and 
stability, as well as the importance of family, which in astrology is one of the themes associated with 
Jupiter in Cancer, a combination in effect from mid-2025 through mid-2026. It is meant to evoke a 
Cancerian sense of nostalgia and connection to the past.
The dream of owning a home and raising a family has been a significant challenge this decade for 
younger adults. The peak of this challenge—and the height of polarization among different classes 
and demographics in society, divided by age, race, gender, nationality, and political leanings—may 
very well be taking place right now, during the Aries Vortex and at the midpoint of the New Aira. The 
symbolism of this year’s book cover, therefore, conveys hope for the future: the creation of a new 
foundation of normalcy that offers the next generation the opportunity to live a fruitful, peaceful, and 
secure life.

 ABOUT THE 2026 INSIDE FRONT COVER
This design was created by Kat Powell. It is titled “How Much Time?”
Here, you see a crust of the universe cracking open. The universe is beautiful, but it also conveys 
an image of coldness—an Ice Age, perhaps even the warming of the Earth and the melting of its sur-
face. The crack in the surface, however, reveals an entirely new reality of beauty: another universe 
altogether, radiant with splendor.
This is like our MMA concept of cycles within cycles. Every cycle is part of a larger cycle, and 
within every cycle, there are smaller sub-cycles. Here we have our “known universe,” which turns out 
to be only an appearance—an illusion—that contains yet another larger and more infinite universe. It 
is one that we are only just beginning to experience and comprehend. Our whole model of reality, of 
life as we have known it, is thus transforming as we enter this “New Aira” of knowledge and under-
standing about our world, our universe, and even our universes (plural).
In a way, the transition of the front cover—illustrating the past, present, and future—is meant to 
flow into an even deeper aspect of the unknown future being revealed to us as we are teleported into 
the middle of this New Aira. It is especially crucial right now during the 2025-2026 “Aries Vortex,” 
which is a funnel involving all four outermost planets (Saturn, Uranus, Neptune, and Pluto) in a con-
figuration that focuses on the vernal equinox point of 0° Aries. This celestial phenomenon has never 
before been experienced by our planet Earth. 
It reveals an entirely new reality, direction, and way forward for humanity. We know something 
huge is underway, but we don’t yet know quite how it will turn out. The “opening” shown in this 
image illustrates that it is only beginning to be revealed to us. There is still more of the future to 
unfold, or “open up” to us as the image suggests. 
“How much time” will it take before it opens enough and we finally “see the way”?
That is the challenge of our annual Forecast books. This year’s edition begins to reveal the nature 
and purpose of the Aries Vortex, within the greater period of this New Aira—a term coined in 2020 
by the artist featured here, Kat Powell. 
As you read the following pages, may you begin to understand where we are and where we are 
headed. Enjoy this year’s journey back to—and into—the future.

 THE TRADITION OF THE ANNUAL Forecast BOOK
The first Forecast book I wrote was in 1975, for the year 1976. Thus, Forecast 2026 represents 
a historic personal milestone: the 50th consecutive year of this annual almanac! Who would have 
guessed this would be the case when I started in 1976? Never underestimate the endurance of one 
with both the Sun and Moon in Capricorn!
When I began, I was unaware of any other annual astrological almanacs being written. There may 
have been, but if so, they were not well known. In fact, in 1975-1976, I was not very well-known 
either. I hadn’t even experienced my first Saturn return. But all that changed by the end of 1976.
Today, thousands of copies of the annual Forecast book are distributed each year in several dif-
ferent languages. But the historical tradition of an annual astrological almanac is even more remark-
able. I had no knowledge of this tradition until I spoke with Dr. Christof Niederwieser of Rottweil, 
Germany, who now lives in Switzerland. In my opinion, Christof is one of the world’s foremost 
mundane astrologers. He is also a noted astrological scholar, researcher, and historian. From 2018 to 
2020, he was invited to serve as a visiting fellow at the University of Erlangen, where he wrote two 
prognostication books of his own. In his research, he uncovered a wealth of scientific literature on the 
history of astrology—specifically, the history of astrological almanacs.
He notes that shortly after Johannes Gutenberg invented the printing press in 1454, interest in 
astrology exploded. This was largely due to the popularity of annual almanacs, which continued to 
grow and peaked between 1580 and 1610. The most popular of these almanacs achieved print runs 
of up to 50,000 copies a year! 
Afterward, a slow decline set in. The fall of astrology was largely due to the many sensational 
but incorrect predictions made by astrologers in prior decades to boost sales with spectacular head-
lines of impending cataclysms. This had been exaggerated, especially during the Thirty Years’ War 
(1618-1648). The major event that made the public very skeptical of astrology was the solar eclipse 
of August 1654. Astrologers debated whether this eclipse would be a full or a partial one. People 
concluded: if astrologers could not even distinguish between a total and partial eclipse, how could 
they predict wars, famines, weather, and the like based on celestial factors like an eclipse? It didn’t 
help that many predicted a great flood that would wipe out vast parts of Europe—a flood that never 
occurred. Thus began the decline of astrology and the annual astrological almanacs in Europe. How-
ever, the tradition was rekindled several years later in other countries, including England and the 
United States. Benjamin Franklin, for example, wrote a yearly almanac that became very popular.
So here we are, more than 200 years later, reviving this ancient tradition in astrology—hopefully 
in a meaningful and ethical way, with a better outcome than what our ancestors devolved into in the 
mid-1600s. To quote Niederwieser in a personal e-mail on the subject: “Yes, you are definitely in an 
honorable tradition with the yearly almanacs!”
## Page 11

7
 ACCURACY AND PRECISION: LIMITS TO FORECASTING
An astrologer, or one who uses the study of astrology to make forecasts or even predictions, is not 
the same as a psychic or clairvoyant, despite often being lumped together by those who do not under-
stand the difference. One uses objective means to make forecasts, while the other relies on subjective 
means. An astrologer is capable of providing probabilities for forecasts based on historical facts and 
frequencies of occurrence, while a psychic or clairvoyant is not. Both may at times make forecasts 
or predictions based on personal observations and experiences, but that is not the same as providing 
evidence-based studies supporting probabilities derived from past frequencies of repetitive patterns.
An astrologer examines the relationship of the planets to one another. Planets are also analyzed 
according to their relationship to the equinoxes and solstices. The vernal and autumnal equinoxes 
mark the beginnings of the signs Aries and Libra (spring and autumn as measured by the Earth’s orbit 
around the Sun). The solstices are identified as 0° Cancer and 0º Capricorn, or the start of summer and 
winter, based on the Earth’s orbital cycle. These are the points by which seasons are measured, which 
is also how much of human activity is organized. When a planet—or the Sun, in the case of a geo-
centric perspective—crosses one of these points, it begins a “cardinal sign” (Aries, Cancer, Libra, or 
Capricorn) for approximately the next 30 degrees of spatial arc. In the case of the Sun, it will remain 
in that cardinal sign for approximately 30 days. The next 30 degrees represent the “fixed signs,” or in 
the case of the Sun, the middle of the season. The last 30 degrees represent the “mutable signs,” or in 
the case of the Sun, the change of the seasons.
Each of these planets and signs has different dynamics. They relate to different themes and dif-
ferent aspects of human experience or nature. For instance, some planets, including the Sun and 
Mars, are “hot.” Hence, the signs they rule—Leo and Aries—are also “hot.” They are known as “fire 
signs.” Thus, when “fire signs” are activated, there is much energy on Earth, but tempers can also 
flare, which in turn can lead to conflicts and threats of war. This can also correlate with hotter-than-
normal temperatures, which may lead to droughts and famine. Now, a psychic might be able to claim 
to know which influence would dominate under a gathering of several planets in fire signs—war or 
droughts. But an astrologer, at best, might forecast one or the other, or perhaps state something like: 
“These placements can suggest the possibility of either a drought or war.” The astrologer cannot be 
certain exactly which type of event will unfold, but can suggest with confidence the themes involved 
and the types of events that may correlate with those themes. 
Furthermore, the astrologer can accurately identify “when” these themes and possible events are 
most likely to occur. A psychic or clairvoyant cannot consistently do this, although some may claim 
they can. Without astrology, their subjective vision of the future often lacks accuracy in predicting 
the timing of events. 
This brings up another difference between the two often-confused practices. An astrologer 
observes outer cosmic movements. It is an objective study in its own right. The interpretation of 
those movements may be subjective, but the timing is objective. This is not the case with psychics or 
clairvoyants, whose analysis is purely subjective, based on a “feeling” or “vision” they experience 
when in the presence of a client.
## Page 12

8
In many cases, an astrological delineation of a chart may be misunderstood by those who 
think astrology, or the astrologer, “missed something” or was inaccurate because a specific event 
suggested did not happen. In other words, the narrower or more specific an astrologer’s inter-
pretation of a geocosmic signature, or even its timing, the more likely it will appear inaccurate. 
Astrology, in its purest interpretation, must allow for a wide range of possibilities to accurately 
reflect the meaning of a particular signature. This is important because the highest role of an 
astrologer is to help the client better understand the possibilities before them, so they (the client) 
can make informed choices in their life. The broader the communication of the themes and dynam-
ics involved, and the wider the timing of possible events under those themes and dynamics, the 
more accurate the astrologer will be. For instance, if an astrologer forecasted that between 2020 
and 2025 the price of Bitcoin would be higher, that forecast would have been 100% accurate. But 
that is a very wide time band and would have missed the 80% price decline from November 2021 
through November 2022. If that astrologer had said the price of Bitcoin would be higher every 
year between 2020 and 2025, the prediction would be inaccurate because of the collapse in 2022. 
The same would be true with stocks. One might say that stock indices will be higher every 
ten years. That is, if you invest in a stock market index at any time, the value of that index 
would be higher ten years later. That prediction is often used by salespeople of financial funds 
and would be correct—except after the high of 1929, when it took more than 20 years for stock 
markets to regain their value from the September 1929 peak. Is this type of prediction, with very 
broad and ten-year time bands, helpful? Perhaps it is for one who is very patient. Or would it be 
more helpful—and profitable—to know that during a certain year or period, the stock market has 
a high historical frequency of dropping at least 20%, or even 35% or more, according to histori-
cal evidence? An investor might be better off waiting for such a decline before investing in the 
stock market when it is making a new all-time high. There are arguments to support both sides 
of this question.
However, the point is that there are limits to the degree of accuracy an astrologer can provide, 
especially when dealing with something as volatile as a financial market or a political trend. The 
best one can do is share the research—historical studies based on evidence that can yield prob-
abilities about the future, drawn from what has transpired in the past under the same or similar 
geocosmic signatures or cyclical time bands, especially when they overlap—and then make a 
projection of what that indicator suggests about the present or future. If the forecaster provides 
evidence of past correlations, and the market does not repeat this time as it did in the past, does 
that mean the astrologer or market timer was wrong? Or does that simply mean this was one of the 
fewer than 20% of instances in which a particular cycle didn’t happen as it had before?
This is what an ethical astrologer can do: provide historical evidence and make a projection 
based on that evidence when the same indicators appear again. The examples above illustrate the 
limits of forecasting accuracy. The more specific the forecast is in terms of an event rather than 
a theme, the more likely the astrologer is to miss other dynamics that could unfold according to 
astrological principles. The more specific and narrower one is in forecasting a turn in a long-term 
market trend—a turn with a wide time band relative to the length of the cycle being examined—
the more likely one is to miss it. A financial astrologer can, for instance, demonstrate that an 
18-year U.S. stock market cycle has occurred 100% of the time within a 13- to 21-year interval 
since the market was founded in 1792. However, if the astrologer states unequivocally that it will 
happen in a specific year—say, 2026—that prediction has only a 12.5% chance of being exact (if 
## Page 13

9
given in 2021). In fact, every year in that 8-year time band has a 12.5% probability of being the 
exact year of the cycle. If one allows the entire time band to represent a possible 18-year cycle 
low, there is an excellent chance of being correct, as this has occurred in all cases so far. But as 
one tries to narrow that time band down to a single year, the odds of being correct begin to decline.
How do we address those odds in an effort to narrow the time band down for such a long-term 
cycle’s culmination? We do this by overlapping smaller cycles, sub-cycles, or “phases” of the 
longer-term cycle. For example, an 18-year cycle might be composed of three 6-year sub-cycles 
or phases that have a normal range of 5-7 years. When the second phase is completed, we add 
5-7 years to that date and see where it overlaps the 18-year cycle. For instance, if the last 18-year 
cycle in the U.S. stock market occurred in March 2009, then the odds are high that the next one 
will occur between 2022 and 2030. If we know that the last 6-year cycle ended in 2022, and in 
over 80% of historical cases this sub-cycle has occurred every 5-7 years, we can project that it is 
next due in 2028 +/– 1 year, overlapping the 18-year cycle time band. This is where the probabili-
ties, based on historical studies, are greatest. But the 6-year cycle is not 100% reliable—it is just 
over 80%. So, if the cycle low does not happen in 2028 +/– 1 year, but instead happens in, say, 
2026 or 2030—still within the 100% historical time band for the 18-year cycle, are we wrong? Or 
is this simply a case of the event happening slightly outside the 80% window? This illustrates the 
limits of accuracy in forecasting. The broader the interpretation and timing, the more accurate it 
will be. However, the broader and wider the timing of the event, the less useful it becomes for the 
reader to benefit from—or profit by.
Efforts to narrow the time band and accuracy of a possible event do not end with cycle over-
laps. This is what distinguishes MMA from most market analysts. We also use geocosmic cycles 
that correlate with historical events and market culminations. The basic rule is this: the longer 
the planetary cycle that is unfolding, the more likely it will coincide with the end of a long-term 
market trend and the beginning of a new one. Likewise, the closer a long-term market cycle is to 
being due, the more likely a long-term planetary cycle will also be in effect. 
Given that the Aries Vortex, for example, is in effect in 2025-2026, and that it is the rarest 
celestial configuration of our lifetime, there is reason to think the all-time highs (the crest of the 
18-year cycle) may be happening now. The crest is due at any time, as is the 18-year cycle trough, 
which is expected sometime before 2030. And since 35-65% declines tend to occur after such a 
long-term bullish trend ends, what should the prediction be? 
More importantly, what should a stock market investor’s strategy be over the next couple of 
years? That question not only illustrates the limits of forecasting but also the value of applying 
these timing methods with an understanding of their odds and importance. If you can avoid buy-
ing when a market is making an all-time high and instead wait for a 37-63% decline that is due 
before entering, which offers a better possibility of long-term profits?
This is why market timing, when used effectively, gives an investor better odds of success. 
You don’t have to be exact in your timing, but it is helpful to know the limits and probabilities. 
Knowledge of cycle studies combined with geocosmics provides this “edge.” It is an edge that all 
traders and investors seek.

 BRIEF NOTE TO INVESTORS AND TRADERS IN 2026
This year’s note is directed more to investors than to traders. The reason is that an important long-
term planetary cycle is in force: the 36-year Saturn–Neptune conjunction on February 20, 2026. Long-
term planetary cycles most often correlate with the completion of long-term market cycles. Further-
more, predicting the exact turn of such cycles within a narrow time band is never easy when a long-term 
planetary cycle is unfolding. There are many possibilities within the orb of influence of such a cycle.
The historical orb of influence for a long-term stock market cycle connected to the Saturn–Nep-
tune conjunction is eleven months. The conjunction is exact on February 20, 2026, which means a 
long-term cycle crest or trough (or both) is due between March 2025 and February 2027. However, 
this can be narrowed down because, in all but one case, the range was eight months or less. This sug-
gests the highest probability for a long-term cycle to end lies between June 2025 and October 2026.
We may be able to reduce this further if we take into account that in July 2025, these two outer 
planets came within just 13′ of their exact conjunction. If that counts, then allowing an 8-month orb 
from that time yields a range of November 2024 to March 2026. The overlap of March 2025 to March 
2026 would stand out as a potential long-term trend change. But it may expand to eight months 
beyond the exact conjunction in February 2026 as well.
What type of long-term stock market cycle is due? As stated in The Ultimate Book on Stock Mar-
ket Timing: Geocosmic Correlations to Investment Cycles: 
The Saturn–Neptune conjunction has a definite correlation to long-term cycle crests. In some 
cases, these cycles were 18-year crests, and in others, they were simply phases of the 18-year 
cycle. Investors may use this signature as an opportunity to take profits on long-term holdings 
if the market is rallying into it, for the probabilities are great that a 4-year cycle will top out 
within the central time band, or close by.
The U.S. stock market is in the time band for its 18-year cycle crest and trough, which extends 
from 2025 through 2030 in the case of the trough, with the crest due before that. But it could also be in 
the time band for a 4-year cycle crest and trough, measured from the low of September 2022. In the case 
of a 4-year cycle, we would anticipate a decline from the high of at least 16%. In the case of an 18-year 
cycle crest, we would anticipate a decline of 35-65%. Since the 18-year cycle will be starting its 17th 
year from the low of 2009, and bull runs to the crest of the next 18-year cycle have historically lasted 
9-20 years, one can see that it is getting very late for the 18-year cycle crest to be completed.
With this in mind, our advice to investors is very simple: start looking for signs to scale back on 
long-term equity holdings or to hedge them in the event that a severe decline is approaching. You may 
also want to begin adjusting your portfolio with the idea that cash will soon be king again. But even 
that is a concern, because the Aries Vortex suggests that the Dollar may continue its decline relative 
to other currencies over the next three years. 
For this reason, investors are advised to consider diversifying their portfolios away from solely 
U.S. dollar-denominated assets and into those backed by other currencies, especially those of neutral 
countries, countries with economies heavily supported by commodities, and stable Asian currencies. 
Once the U.S. stock market declines 37-63%, consider moving back into U.S. equities.

12
It is possible, but not likely, that each of these cycles will end and begin in 2026. My view, how-
ever, is that investors are well advised to consider protecting their portfolios against a severe decline 
that could very well begin from a high forming within the orb of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction 
crest described above.
I also have a specific period for traders to concentrate on in 2026. This would be in the latter 
half of July (July 15-25), when the transit of Jupiter will form a sextile to Uranus, trine to Neptune, 
and opposition to Pluto. Uranus will also form a sextile to Neptune and a trine to Pluto. These are 
intermediate- and long-term planetary cycles, so they require an orb of up to four months to manifest 
as an intermediate or long-term cycle in various financial markets. But in many cases, such a cycle 
could very well happen within three weeks of this period. Traders are advised to watch for reversals 
in markets that are making new yearly highs or lows, or double tops and/or double bottoms.

 CHANGING OF THE GUARD:
TRANSITION OF LEADERSHIP UNDER THE ARIES VORTEX

From the west unto the east.

Worry and anxiety are only a matter of the time it takes us to adjust to the Truth. 
—Damien Simpson and Ray Merriman interview, Universal Mind Science, Hollywood, 
California, early 1980s
I have never lived in a time when the U.S. was not the world’s dominant superpower. 
I have never lived in a world where the U.S. Dollar was not the dominant standard world currency. 
I have never lived during a period when the U.S. did not have strong allies throughout the world 
who trusted it to be the leader of world order and global security. 
However, that is all changing as we enter the midpoint of the “New Aira” of 2020– 2032, which 
just happens to coincide with the “Aries Vortex” of 2025–2026.
What is this “New Aira”? What exactly constitutes an “Aries Vortex”? And what correlation do 
these two extremely rare cosmic developments have with great changes in the world order? Can any-
thing be done to affect how these changes unfold?
Let’s review the larger New Aira cycle first. On December 21, 2020, Jupiter and Saturn conjoined 
at 0° Aquarius. This synodic cycle occurs approximately every 20 years. For roughly 200 years, those 
conjunctions take place in signs of the same element, with slight distortions near the beginning and 
end of each 200-year interval, when the series crosses the boundaries between elements. Between 
1802 and 2000, for example, the conjunctions occurred mostly in earth signs, except in 1821, when 
the cycle reverted briefly to late Aries, and in 1980–81, when it leaped forward to the air sign of 
Libra. In 2000, the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn returned for one final occurrence in the earth 
sign of Capricorn. 
The air-sign era is now underway with the Jupiter–Saturn conjunction in Aquarius on December 
21, 2020. From 2020 through 2199, eight of the next nine Jupiter–Saturn conjunctions will occur 
in air signs. The air element of this synodic cycle has not been dominant since the 13th century, or 
approximately 800 years ago. Thus, as coined by market analyst and astrologer Kat Powell, we are 
now entering the “New Aira” cycle of the “Great Chronocrator,” a term often used to refer to the 
Jupiter–Saturn cycle.
## Page 18

14
Of greatest importance right now is the first 12 years of the New Aira, or 2020–2032. This is the 
interval of time that it will take Jupiter to return to 0° Aquarius, the point from which the New Aira 
began. These 12 years will unfold as a sub-cycle within a greater cycle. It will likely take that long for 
humankind to begin to fully understand the New Aira transformation it is undergoing. It will take that 
long before the application of these new understandings registers in a meaningful, transformative, 
and enduring way—one that elevates human consciousness and clarifies the direction of the human 
experience. Until then, we are still learning what it means and how to use this new knowledge wisely.
We already have a glimpse of the New Aira that is emerging and how it might manifest over 
time. Aquarius rules innovation, particularly in technology. One of the major themes associated with 
Aquarius is revolution and renaissance. In the past several Forecast books, it was noted that this 
would be a period of technological renaissance—and indeed it is. Yet we do not know quite yet how 
it will ultimately affect life on this planet. We see incredible possibilities. But there are also fears 
that it may lead to an ominous, even destructive, outcome for humanity. Will we be able to harness 
the power of this technological renaissance and use it constructively to improve life as we know it? 
Or will world leaders and other bad actors harness it first to control or destroy those they perceive 
as enemies? Answers to these questions during this first 12-year sub-cycle of the 200-year New Aira 
should begin to emerge as we continue through this period of transition.
Sub-cycles are also known as phases. Just as this 12-year period is a sub-cycle, or phase, of 
the greater 200-year New Aira cycle, so too does the 12-year sub-cycle divide into two 6-year half-
cycles. And half-cycles can be very dramatic, for they represent turning points in the pendulum swing 
of the greater cycle. 
It so happens that the midpoint of this first 12-year phase coincides with another powerful celestial 
configuration known as the “Aries Vortex.” The course of human activity and leadership is shifting. 
The pendulum of world leadership is swinging from the West back to the East. America’s standing as 
the world’s leader is vulnerable to being replaced by leadership from the opposite hemisphere—to a 
degree never experienced before by most people alive today. Will this change actually take place? Or 
is this just a temporary threat to the status of the U.S. that will reverse shortly? Will its currency, the 
U.S. dollar, survive this threat as the de facto global currency used for most world trade? If so, how 
will the U.S. regain its economic leadership? If not, where will that lead the U.S. and other nations of 
the world? Who will emerge as the new leader?
These are the questions—even the challenges—that the U.S. and the world face as we enter the 
midpoint of the first 12-year phase of the New Aira. These are the realities coming to light as we 
enter the Aries Vortex. Nothing is quite the same. The world in this New Aira is filled with danger and 
uncertainty—a classical representation of Saturn conjunct Neptune in Aries. Yet it also offers incred-
ible opportunities. Where there is fear, there is also opportunity for those who are alert and able to act 
in accordance with the changes signified by these times.
For investors, this is a time to consider broadening one’s perspective—and one’s portfolio—to 
include the rise of new world leadership and assets backed by the currencies of these emerging world 
powers. In fact, the currencies themselves may change significantly, shifting from paper fiat to something 
more representative of this New Aira that began with the Jupiter–Saturn conjunction at 0° Aquarius. 
This is a techno-renaissance—and its currency is digital. It’s only a matter of time before we all 
need to adjust.

History is seasonal and winter is here. 
—Neil Howe, “The Fourth Turning is Here,” Simon and Schuster, 2023.
Welcome to “Crazy Times 2026.” 
This is the time of the long-anticipated “Aries Vortex,” an extremely rare celestial configuration 
centered on—and linked to—the Saturn–Neptune conjunction in the very first degree of Aries. Aries 
itself is the very first of 12 signs and marks the beginning of the world cycle according to astrology, 
the world’s oldest discipline exploring the correlation between cycles in the cosmos and cycles in 
human activity.
Why are these “Crazy Times”? Because Saturn and Neptune correspond to more terms used in 
abnormal psychology than any other two planets. They represent very opposite dynamics, such as 
fear and hope, guilt and forgiveness, delusions of grandeur and persecution, certainty and disillusion-
ment, mania and depression, irrational exuberance and panic. And in the first degree of Aries, this 
setup indicates a monumental shift from the end of one long-term cycle (Pisces) to the beginning of 
a new one (Aries). That is, Neptune only crosses into Aries every 164 years. Saturn does the same 
approximately every 29 years. The two planets conjoin one another every 36 years. But how often do 
these two planets conjoin one another right at the end and beginning of the 12 signs? Our database 
only goes back to about 4000 BC, and there are no instances of this same cosmic feat during that time. 
Some astrologers have suggested that this cosmic configuration happened at some point between 
4000 and 8000 BC, but I cannot confirm that.
To understand why the Aries Vortex of 2025–2026 is akin to “crazy times,” consider two things: 
(1) what is happening today, and (2) the principles associated with Saturn and Neptune, combined 
with the classic principles of Aries versus Pisces, the beginning of the cycle of signs versus the end 
of that cycle. In this case, it is not just an ordinary cycle but a very, very long one—over 4000 years 
in duration, at least. 
## Page 20

16
We must also take into account that the other two outermost planets—Uranus and Pluto—are 
in a favorable trine aspect, with their midpoint also crossing back and forth over 0° Aries, the very 
point of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction. These may seem like “crazy times” because they are 
unfolding under a geocosmic configuration that humanity has never before seen or experienced. 
Cosmic patterns this rare will usher in global changes of great magnitude, and life may seem so 
different that it feels a bit “crazy.”
As we consider what has transpired already during the “orb of influence,” which began in 
early 2025 (when Saturn and Neptune entered Aries, followed by Uranus entering Gemini, and 
shortly Pluto finally entering Aquarius in November 2024), it is apparent that vast transforma-
tions are underway across multiple sectors of human activity. Figuratively speaking, everything 
that is supposed to be up has turned down, and everything that would normally be expected to 
turn down has instead turned up. What was previously regarded as diplomacy in the pursuit of 
world peace and global order has instead become driven by coercion and land- or money-grab-
bing, with little regard for consent or fairness toward those affected. The belief that “might is 
right,” and therefore entitles one to dictate the course of civilization rather than cooperate toward 
win-win outcomes and mutual benefit, has become the “new normal” of global leadership. This 
reflects one of the many expressions of Saturn in Aries (“the bully”), which will remain largely 
in effect through April 13, 2028. 
On a more positive note, Saturn in Aries can also represent superhuman efforts to build sys-
tems and structures that stand the test of time. However, this process is unlikely to unfold without 
resistance and struggle. Hence, there is often a challenge to authority and dominance. And without 
mutual respect among all parties involved, this can lead to conflict, or even the threat of war, where 
those with the most “might” can claim superiority and the mantle of power.
Yet it is not just Saturn in Aries that indicates the harsh challenges that many experience today, 
especially those who find it difficult to adjust to this new reality (Aries). It is also Neptune, the 
planet of ideals, altruism, and the search for beauty and truth. Those guiding life principles are also 
being challenged. Even those who hold such fundamental religious beliefs as salvation in an after-
life for virtuous deeds committed in this life may find their belief systems challenged.
One example of this cosmic dichotomy between Saturn and Neptune is the very simple con-
flict between hope and fear. Neptune represents hope, or the wish for a “better life,” even a perfect 
life—which, of course, is an illusion that can never be fully manifested on this plane. Yet it is a 
concept that can be imagined and moderated to mean simply a “better life” than the one currently 
being lived. Everyone has Neptune in their chart. Everyone has hope for a better life, a better 
world. For many, this belief is what keeps them going. It is supported by practices such as prayer 
and meditation, which are among the activities associated with Neptune.
And then there is Saturn, the opposite counterpart to Neptune, representing fear or the reality 
that life is not perfect and, in many cases, not even fair. Where Neptune is idealistic and guilty of 
wishful thinking, Saturn is realistic, skeptical, controlling, and guilty of ... well, just plain guilt, 
either personally, for failing to do or attain something, or projecting (blaming) that “failure” onto 
others. Saturn represents boundaries, laws, and rules—the very things that help structure society 
into orderly collective behavior when built wisely and according to a sensible, well-thought-out 
plan. If one violates these boundaries, there is usually a consequence, a punishment, that follows. 
Or at least, that’s the way it used to be before the influence of the Aries Vortex began. Now the 
## Page 21

17
Aries Vortex (especially with Saturn in Aries) wants to return to those basic principles, ensuring 
that everyone is “staying in one’s lane” and not crossing boundaries without harsh reprisals.
Thus, bringing together the two planets ruling “hope and fear” results either in a battle for 
dominance or in a pathway that patiently seeks to integrate the two dynamics in a way that encour-
ages and supports hope while at the same time minimizing the fear (Saturn) of going into the 
unknown (Neptune) or the new (Aries). Everybody wants change (Aries), but nobody wants to 
sacrifice security or the hope for a better future. Everyone wants change to move in a direction 
that is clear, understandable, and easy to adjust, one that provides a sense of self-control and self-
determination. Without these latter qualities, a general sense of confusion arises: a feeling of being 
lost, even helpless, about future prospects. 
This is the downside of Neptune when it struggles to work constructively with Saturn, 
who demands both a realistic goal and an organized plan to achieve it. Without that possibility 
or belief, Neptune’s existence is in danger of falling into a state of hopelessness. One is then 
tempted to give up, surrender, or seek solace in altered states of consciousness. Hence, the rise 
in mental illness and substance abuse to escape (Neptune) the fears generated by the uncertainty 
of reality (Saturn). 
Living in today’s world of epic change is not easy. That is why this period (2026 +/– one year) 
is dubbed “Crazy Times.” 
Yet if one looks at the possibilities of this “New Aira” starting to unfold, one can also train 
the mind to see new possibilities—extraordinary opportunities. Therefore, once Saturn passes by 
as the planet front-running Neptune, the principles of the latter planet will again become visible. 
That is the hope. That is, Saturn is the faster-moving planet and “blocks out” the light of Neptune 
while it approaches and comes into conjunction with Neptune. But after February 20, 2026, Saturn 
begins to separate from Neptune, releasing more of Neptune’s power. Yes, Saturn may still domi-
nate until it finally leaves Aries, the sign also occupied by Neptune, in April 2028. But Neptune’s 
influence grows as Saturn starts its withdrawal from Neptune’s cosmic head and heart. The virtu-
ous Neptunian principle of compassion and care for others begins to express itself again. And as 
Saturn moves from the dominancy of fire-sign Aries into the more comfort- and security-motivated 
sign of Taurus, a return to normalcy—a deportation of “Crazy Times” into something less crazy 
and more humane—is scheduled to commence. In other words, hope about the world and its future 
can and will be re-imagined. A new texture of light, figuratively speaking, will begin to surround 
this planet and its inhabitants.
Let’s now examine various areas of human activity and the possibilities that may be related to 
the Aries Vortex in 2026 and develop an awareness of how to navigate these challenges.

THE FUNNEL OF THE ARIES VORTEX
Figure 1: Aries Vortex, illustrating the Saturn–Neptune conjunction at 0° Aries and the Uranus–Pluto 
trine, whose midpoint is also 0° Aries.
The Aries Vortex is also a funnel, with its apex located at the Earth—specifically, the Earth at its 
vernal equinox point of 0° Aries. 
The broadening sides of this funnel are represented by Uranus and Pluto, which are also in the 
early stages of their ingress into the air signs Gemini and Aquarius. In fact, as they dance across these 
ingress points, they form a 120° trine aspect to one another, which is considered the most favorable 
of all aspects (spatial relationships) between any two planets in the study of astrology. 
The sides of the funnel—Uranus and Pluto—narrow down to their midpoint, which is the apex of 
the funnel: 0° Aries, the beginning of the zodiac, where Saturn and Neptune conjoin in 2025–2026. 
The exact date of their conjunction is February 20, 2026, though they were very close (less than 13′ 
of arc) during the spring and summer of 2025 as well. Thus, to understand the possibilities of this 
historic and unparalleled cosmic arrangement, we need to contemplate the meaning of (1) the Saturn–
Neptune conjunction, (2) the Uranus–Pluto air trine, and (3) the apex of this funnel, which is 0° Aries. 
We start with this last factor. This particular degree, 0° Aries, aligns with the vernal equinox point 
in Earth’s orbit around the Sun. In that orbital cycle, this degree represents the end of winter and the 
beginning of spring (in the Northern Hemisphere, that is—but in either hemisphere, it marks a time 
when day and night are approximately equal in length, just before shifting toward more of one and 
less of the other). Thus, this degree holds great symbolic meaning. 
It is referred to as “the World Degree,” meaning that longer-term cosmic crossings of this point 
represent times of major change on Earth or in the direction of humankind. The longer the geocosmic 
## Page 23

19
cycle involved, the stronger the transition taking place. Therefore, when Saturn crosses from Pisces into 
Aries every 29 years (approximately), it marks an important shift. When Neptune crosses every 164 
years, it symbolizes an even greater one. When both cross this World Degree at the same time, it signi-
fies an enormous shift, as this type of cosmic event has not occurred in more than 4000 years! It is rare 
and therefore very powerful in its capacity to transform the existing order of life as it has been known.
The nature of the shift will reflect the characteristics of the planets involved and of the sign Aries. 
For instance, Saturn in Aries (May 25–September 1, 2025, and then again February 14, 2026–April 
13, 2028) displays a strong drive to build something lasting (Saturn)—a legacy—with a sense of great 
urgency and swift effort (Aries). It wants to accomplish something great in a comparatively short time, 
as if time (Saturn) is running out. There is an underlying sense that “time is one’s greatest enemy.” Yet 
in this rush to get things done, one often encounters great resistance to change and delays in meeting the 
goal (Saturn). It can be frustrating when others do not move as quickly as the builder or initiator of the 
effort would like. The Saturn principle may then come into play, punishing anyone who does not follow 
his or her command or who resists being controlled by the driver of the legacy movement. 
Saturn is the principle of control. Aries is associated with the principle of speed and the sense of 
“me first” or independence. This struggle between control and independence can result in clashes—
even war. Alternatively, it can signify a superhuman feat led by someone who does most of the work 
without relying on others who cannot keep up with the pace needed to complete the project on time. 
In either case, the conjunction of Saturn and Neptune on the World Degree (0° Aries) signals 
that something major is happening. Something on a very large scale is underway, and this change 
will likely come with conflict. Nevertheless, it will probably gather enough momentum to force the 
issue—the change—into something entirely new for humankind to cope with. Perhaps this has to do 
with the technological renaissance now underway, a change in the world’s standard currency, a new 
hierarchy of global leadership, or—most likely—a combination of all of these developments.
The Age of American Exceptionalism may be ending. However, that does not mean the U.S. is 
becoming a “third world” or failed country. It simply means that other nations, such as China and India, 
are growing faster than America and gaining greater status as world leaders. They are advancing more 
rapidly than the U.S. in many areas, but it doesn’t mean the U.S. is declining—only that others are catch-
ing up and, in some cases, surpassing it in their influence over global affairs that for the past century have 
defaulted to America. The question to ask is not whether America is in decline, but rather: Why are other 
countries becoming more and more influential in world affairs? Why are they choosing to trade more 
with one another and less with the U.S.? And why might much of the world’s capital, anchored in U.S. 
dollars, begin to leave the once-secure investment pastures of America for opportunities in other regions? 
The answers, I believe, lie in the nature of basic relationships: trust versus mistrust. When the 
balance of that dynamic is altered in any relationship, the relationship begins to break down. It takes 
a long time to build trust. It takes only a moment—a sudden decision or change of policy—to tear it 
down, and even longer to repair and rebuild it.
We will discuss this further when we examine the chart of the United States and its past and cur-
rent leaders. For now, let us deepen our understanding of this magnificent celestial arrangement, the 
Aries Vortex, and the outer planets that make up its funnel and apex. I will cover the aspects in the 
pages that follow, and Pouyan Zolfagharnia will cover their sign placements as we embark upon this 
remarkable journey into the Aries Vortex of 2026.

 THE SATURN–NEPTUNE CONJUNCTION
Well, we know where we’re goin’,
But we don’t know where we’ve been,
And we know what we’re knowin’,
But we can’t say what we’ve seen.
And we’re not little children,
And we know what we want.
And the future is certain—
Give us time to work it out.
—David Byrne, “Road to Nowhere,” Little Creatures (Talking Heads, 1985), published by WB 
Music Corp.
The synodic cycle of Saturn and Neptune—that is, from conjunction to conjunction—lasts 36 
years. However, the frequency of these two planets conjoining at the first degree of Aries is extremely 
rare, given that there are 360° in each planet’s orbit around the Sun. 
In the next chapters, MMA analyst Pouyan Zolfagharnia will interpret what each planet—Saturn 
and Neptune in Aries, Uranus in Gemini, and Pluto in Aquarius—portends. Here, however, we will 
examine the meaning of and the potential world changes suggested by events that occurred during 
past periods of Saturn–Neptune conjunctions. We will also consider the principles of Saturn and 
Neptune, as known through the study of astrology, and review some historical instances that have 
repeated with similar themes when these two planets have conjoined.
SATURN–NEPTUNE CONJUNCTION OF 1989 
The most recent conjunction of Saturn and Neptune is probably vividly recalled by those who 
were adults 36 years ago. This occurred from March 3 to November 13, 1989, when the two outer 
planets conjoined in a three-passage series due to the retrograde motion of both. The middle cross-
ing took place on June 24. All three passages occurred between 10° and 12° Capricorn. We typically 
allow an orb of approximately one year for events related to a long-term planetary aspect to manifest.
The first event to note during this period was the environmental disaster in Alaska on March 24, 
1989, when 42,000 cubic meters of crude oil leaked from the Exxon Valdez oil tanker. In the world 
of finance, Neptune is one of the planets associated with crude oil and the ocean. Saturn is associated 
with loss, and Capricorn pertains to the earth. Thus, the combination of these principles fits an epic 
environmental disaster such as an oil spill in the ocean off the coast of Alaska. 
Therefore, in 2025–2026, we must be alert to potential environmental and ecological catastrophes. 
These might involve floods (Neptune) that threaten human life or abnormally hot or cold temperatures 
that damage the growing or harvesting cycles of food. They may also indicate freezing (Saturn) of 
citrus or coffee fields, or outbreaks of disease caused by parasites infesting and destroying crops.
Next, we note that Apple launched its first portable computer, the Macintosh Portable, on Sep-
tember 20, 1989. This event sparked new creative applications that would influence both the arts and 
the business world, particularly through advances in advertising and marketing. With the world of 
artificial intelligence opening up today, we can anticipate many new innovations and products—much 
## Page 25

21
like the portable Apple computer—that will drive the technological renaissance currently underway. 
Graphic illustrations are likely to be stunning, both in print and in the digital realm. This creative 
force may also extend into the fields of music and film, which are ruled by Neptune.
However, the most notable event of 1989 was the fall of the Berlin Wall on November 9. This 
was one of the most significant moments in modern history, symbolizing the reunification of East and 
West Germany. It also coincided with the collapse of ideological divisions that had separated Europe 
for decades. This event is highly representative of Saturn and Neptune conjunct in Capricorn, as both 
Saturn and Capricorn rule structures such as walls. They also rule authoritarian systems of govern-
ment in which the state exerts greater control over the lives of its citizens. Neptune’s character is not 
only idealistic but also dissolving—it erodes whatever it touches. In combination with Saturn and 
Capricorn, it dissolved an entire system of government—Russian Communism as it was known at 
the time—and, as a result, the Soviet Union came to an end. Russia’s government imploded as more 
than 300 million new consumers entered the free-market economies of the world.
This event eventually led to a great global economic boom that lasted through the following 
decade, highlighted by the internet revolution that connected people from around the world. It ulti-
mately transformed how business was conducted—from traditional brick-and-mortar retail to the 
emerging world of online commerce. Barriers dissolved.
What barriers and boundaries will dissolve in 2026 and beyond?
THE SATURN–NEPTUNE CONJUNCTION OF 1952–53
This was another three-passage series, starting on November 21, 1952, and ending on July 22, 
1953. The middle crossing took place on May 17, 1953.
It was also another monumental and transformative period that exhibited themes related to Saturn 
and Neptune, which conjoined in the sign of Libra. According to Google’s AI, “In 1952, the United 
Kingdom gained Queen Elizabeth II as monarch, and Britain developed its first atomic bomb. Glob-
ally, the Mau Mau Uprising began in Kenya, while King Farouk was ousted in Egypt by a military 
coup. The Great Smog of London killed thousands, and the U.S. conducted its first hydrogen bomb 
test [on November 1 in the Marshall Islands], which strengthened the international supremacy of the 
United States in terms of weapons capability. The U.S. Supreme Court also declared a steel seizure 
by President Truman illegal.” 
Of particular interest here is the Great Smog of London, which killed thousands, for Neptune is 
the planet of fog and smog. With Neptune, it is hard to see—visibility can be distorted and things 
become blurred, both literally and figuratively. But smog can also be poisonous and hazardous to 
one’s health, and Neptune rules poisons. 
Thus, in 2025–2026, we may see instances of deadly fog or smog, or poisons in the atmosphere 
that threaten people’s health, or toxins in food or medical injections used in attempts to assassinate 
leaders (or their enemies). 
It is also noteworthy that the United States Supreme Court intervened in President Harry Tru-
man’s attempt to seize control of the steel industry and declared his action illegal. Today, there are 
cases before the Supreme Court alleging that President Trump engaged in similar unlawful efforts to 
assert control over segments of U.S. industry and business.

Most of this particular instance of Saturn conjunct Neptune took place in 1952–1953, which is

(2) Vladimir Putin was born (October 7, 1952); and (3) Xi Jinping was born (June 15, 1953). According 
to Google’s AI, the year 1953 also witnessed “… the end of the Korean War, the first Soviet hydrogen 
bomb test, the 1953 coup in Iran, and the execution of the Rosenbergs for espionage in the U.S.”
This Saturn–Neptune conjunction period also witnessed the peak of the “Red Scare,” when Sena-
tor Joseph McCarthy’s brutal tactics, false accusations, and life-ruining trials were unleashed on 
those he accused of being Communist spies. By 1954, he was condemned by Congress for “conduct 
that tends to bring the Senate into dishonor and disrepute.” Does this sound familiar, given current 
events under Saturn conjunct Neptune? This is a time when witch hunts and attempts to ruin the lives 
of well-known people who disagree with those in authority can take place. Today, this is referred to 
as “hate speech.” Saturn and Neptune together can indicate false accusations and scandals, but truth 
eventually comes to the surface, discrediting the aggressors and restoring the reputations of those 
harmed by such attacks. The problem is that until the truth is known—or agreed upon—both sides 
believe they are being attacked unjustly and seek retribution. 
By the way, the American Heritage Dictionary defines “McCarthyism” as “1. The political prac-
tice of publicizing accusations of disloyalty or subversion with insufficient regard for evidence; and 
2. The use of methods of investigation and accusation regarded as unfair in order to suppress opposi-
tion.” In some respects, this Saturn–Neptune of 2025–2026 may seem like 1952–53 all over again in 
the halls of leading world governments.
THE SATURN–NEPTUNE CONJUNCTION OF 1917
1917 was a key year in a crucial decade. This was a decade of change, or, rather, transforma-
tion; of the destruction of what became old orders; and of the replacement of existing currents 
and practices.
— Jeremy Black, “A Nation Must Think Before It Acts,” Foreign Policy Research Insti-
tute, 2017, www.fpri.org.
This was a single-passage event that occurred on August 1, 1917. Therefore, approximately one 
year on either side of this date should be allowed for its influence to manifest in human affairs.
There were three historically significant events in 1917 that relate to themes of today: the Russian 
Revolution, America’s entry into World War I, and the Balfour Declaration with its implications for 
the Middle East.
The Russian Revolution, also known as the Bolshevik Revolution, stands out because it led to 
the birth of Russian Communism. The Russian government imploded as Czar Nicholas II was over-
thrown, followed by a second revolution that put Vladimir Lenin’s Bolsheviks in power and started a 
civil war. According to Google’s AI, “The Bolsheviks, a Marxist faction led by Vladimir Lenin, seized 
power in the October Revolution of 1917, ending czarist rule and creating the world’s first socialist 
republic. The party formally changed its name to the Russian Communist Party in 1918, solidifying 
the link between the revolution and Communism.”
The Balfour Declaration of 1917 was also an important event that relates to what is transpiring 
today. According to Google’s AI, the declaration “…expressed British support for the establishment 
of a ‘national home for the Jewish people’ in Palestine. The declaration also stated that nothing 
## Page 27

23
should be done to prejudice the civil and religious rights of Palestine’s non-Jewish communities. This 
statement is considered a pivotal moment for Zionism and a foundational document for the state of 
Israel, although it also laid the groundwork for decades of conflict in the region.”
In 1918, still under the Saturn–Neptune orb of influence, three more major world events occurred. 
The first was the end of World War I. The second was the eruption of the Spanish flu pandemic, which 
killed 50–100 million people worldwide—the deadliest pandemic in history. In addition, a massive 
liberation movement emerged in Ukraine, seeking to separate from the new Russian Bolshevik gov-
ernment in 1917–1918 and beyond. That struggle for Ukrainian independence from Russia continues 
to this day.
THE SATURN–NEPTUNE CONJUNCTION OF 1882
The Chinese Exclusion Act was approved on May 6, 1882. It was the first significant law 
restricting immigration into the United States. 
—National Archives, www.archives.gov. 
This was another single-passage conjunction, occurring on May 12, 1882. Therefore, it also

Once again, the Russian government was in a state of turmoil when Emperor Alexander II was 
killed by a bomb near his palace in March 1881—an act falsely blamed on Russian Jews. Pogroms 
then broke out, inflicting suffering on Russian Jewry not seen since the 17th century. The pogroms 
came suddenly and unexpectedly. 
This period exhibited several themes related to what is unfolding in 2026—especially concerning 
Israel and the Jewish people—as well as tensions between China and the United States and restrictive 
immigration policies in the U.S.
SUMMARY AND COMMENTS
The basic themes suggested by the principles of Saturn and Neptune have manifested strikingly 
well in world events under their 36-year conjunction cycle throughout history, as exemplified by the 
last four instances. It is remarkable how history has, in a very impressive manner, closely repeated 
these themes—not only in the nature of events but also in the specific locations and regions of the 
world where they occurred.
Let’s briefly review these recurring themes and consider how they are once again emerging in 
today’s world as Saturn conjoins Neptune from mid-2025 through early 2026.
•	
Health and possible epidemics/pandemics: A study I conducted and published in Forecast 
2021 revealed that the dominant geocosmic correlation to the ten deadliest pandemics in his-
tory involved major signatures between Saturn and Neptune. In 1918, this aspect coincided 
with the Spanish flu—the deadliest pandemic in human history. Saturn will conjoin Neptune 
again soon. Thus, it is crucial for the world’s population to closely monitor the development 
of any diseases or viruses that may attack the immune system of a large segment of the global 
population. Individuals with weakened immune systems must take extra precautions, such as 
avoiding gatherings where contagion may spread quickly and making lifestyle choices that 
strengthen rather than stress the immune system (for example, taking nutritional supplements 
and getting extra rest). This aspect can also indicate blood disorders or the growth of tumors 
if not addressed in time.
## Page 28

24
•	
Propaganda and the quest for truth: This challenge has been ongoing for the past several 
years, even as Saturn transited Pisces, the sign ruled by Neptune, from 2023 through to early 
2026. Saturn represents the quest for facts, evidence, and, ultimately, truth. Neptune repre-
sents the search for a higher truth, yet it can also symbolize a conscious choice to avoid the 
truth and even to intentionally misstate, misdirect, or avoid relevant facts in order to create a 
false narrative. It can also involve withholding information and evading disclosures that oth-
ers need in order to make intelligent and well-informed choices. In short, this combination 
can be highly manipulative—even to the point of outright deception—to gain an advantage at 
the expense of others, including the collective, which may ultimately suffer as a result. It can 
foster rumors or false narratives that lead to serious problems of trust. It can also be accusatory 
and ruinous to the reputations of innocent people, as seen during the early 1950s under the 
“Red Scare” led by Senator Joseph McCarthy. Here, fear comes into conflict with hope, and 
a pervasive sense of paranoia can grip a nation—or even the world—convincing people that 
the future is bleak and cannot be changed except by following the advice of the propagandists. 
Today, the world is awash in propaganda and false narratives to the point that knowing 
the truth has become a difficult challenge. 
•	
Errors in data and numbers: Saturn represents data and evidence-based facts and figures. 
Neptune represents errors and omissions regarding hard data. It is therefore not surprising that 
many reports containing detailed “estimates” or calculations have been found to be incorrect 
under this signature. For instance, the U.S. Labor Department announced in August 2025 that 
it had overestimated the number of people employed over several months—via the monthly 
payroll figures—by reporting a whopping 900,000 jobs that didn’t exist! Expect more of these 
types of inaccuracies where numerical data are involved. The result is a misrepresentation of 
reality—another common theme under Saturn–Neptune hard aspects—that challenges inves-
tors to make wise long-term planning decisions that are based on accurate data points.
•	
Trust and distrust leading to the dissolution of partnerships and loss of allies:
When the terms of an understanding between allies change without the willing consent 
of the other party, trust turns to mistrust, and the foundation of the relationship begins to dis-
solve. It takes a long time to regain what has been lost through a perceived violation of trust. 
The U.S. has unilaterally changed the terms of its long-standing agreements with other 
nations—including its closest allies—in matters of trade (tariffs) and military support. This may 
be a major reason why many of America’s former allies are beginning to lose faith in the U.S. 
as the moral leader of the free world. The era of American exceptionalism is faltering, in part 
because of policy changes that affect allies without their willing consent. These relationships are 
no longer perceived as “win–win” and mutually beneficial. Instead, they are seen as win–lose, 
where those who do not comply with such unilateral decisions are the “losers.” Since no one 
wants to be a loser, several former allies of the U.S. now seek to strengthen ties with other nations 
that offer better terms—without new or higher tariffs. Hence, there is a loss of America’s standing 
as the world’s moral and trusted leader. This represents one of the downsides of Saturn conjunct 
Neptune in Aries, forming a hard square aspect to the natal position of Venus in the U.S. chart.
•	
Immigration restrictions and isolationism: People wish to enter the U.S. and other nations, 
usually in hopes of a better life and to escape persecution or hardship under the authoritarian 
leadership of their native country. Neptune represents that hope for a better life. But with 
## Page 29

25
Saturn, new laws are often enacted that restrict immigration or make the process of entering 
or remaining in a country extremely difficult. This occurred with the Chinese Exclusion Act 
of 1882 in the U.S., and it appears to be happening again in late 2025 as the U.S. and other 
nations contemplate new and restrictive immigration laws.
•	
Kidnappings, poisonings, and assassinations of political or financial opponents: These 
events often increase under hard aspects between Saturn and Neptune. People simply “dis-

is responsible for their disappearance. Assassination attempts have already been increasing 
during the current Saturn–Neptune conjunction period, a trend that may continue into 2026.

Oil spills and ecological disasters or calamities: Neptune rules water, oceans, and oil. 
Saturn represents loss resulting from catastrophes in these areas. Floods and oil spills can 
cause major losses, both financial and environmental. This pattern has been observed during 
previous Saturn–Neptune conjunctions, most notably with the Exxon Valdez oil spill of 1989.
•	
Attacks and persecution of Jews: For some reason, Jews have often been blamed for societal 
problems during Saturn–Neptune conjunctions, subsequently suffering greatly at the hands of 
their oppressors. These acts are the equivalent of “hate crimes,” and once again, the blaming of 
Jews is increasing across many parts of the world. In 2025, Jews are being accused of commit-
ting genocide against Palestinians in Gaza. Polls show that majorities of both Jews in Israel and 
Palestinians in Gaza believe the other side is engaged in genocide. Yet there is no evidence that 
the majority of either group actually supports genocide against the other.
•	
Crisis on the seas: Neptune rules the oceans and seas, while Saturn pertains to government. 
Together, they can signify naval or maritime incidents that require government intervention. This 
may be reflected in challenges involving China and Taiwan, or in China’s activities in Cambodia 
and along shipping routes in the South China Sea, where its navy is actively engaged in building 
projects and ports that could be perceived as threats to the U.S. and its allies in the region.
•	
Implosion of the Russian government: In the last four instances of Saturn conjunct Neptune, 
the Russian government has undergone major changes within one year. Something similar 
could therefore repeat, with the Russian government falling into turmoil and a new leader 
emerging. If this cycle repeats, it suggests the end of Vladimir Putin’s rule in Russia by 2027.
Overall, Saturn–Neptune conjunction periods have coincided with times of hysteria, paranoia, 
and fear about an uncertain future. Propaganda has been widespread and has distorted the truth. 
Scapegoats have been blamed and reputations ruined for failures in government and business to 
uphold the moral high ground. Corruption has been rampant, and trust between allies and partners 
has often been damaged to the point that these relationships dissolve. False narratives have led to 
greater polarization and division within societies, even escalating into hate crimes. These are the 
negative ways in which events have unfolded during previous Saturn–Neptune conjunction periods. 
Yet humanity has always recovered from these difficult times, beginning a period of rebuilding that 
led to a decade of peace and prosperity afterwards. 
Can humanity—facing similar Saturn–Neptune challenges today as it has in the past—recover 
from the current dark period of polarity, division, and fear of an uncertain future? Yes. The Uranus–
Pluto trine that defines the boundary of the Aries Vortex funnel supports this possibility.
