CREATIVE DESTRUCTION VIA TECHNOLOGICAL RENAISSANCE
By Raymond Merriman, with research assistance from Daniel Gordon
Jeff Bezos presented an audacious vision to confront one of artificial intelligence’s most press-
ing challenges: its insatiable energy demands. This proposal, “…which outlines the develop-
ment of gigawatt-scale, solar-powered data centers in space within the next 10 to 20 years, 
marks a significant conceptual leap in sustainable infrastructure for the burgeoning AI indus-
try. Bezos’s plan not only offers a potential remedy for the environmental strain imposed by 
current AI operations but also provides a fascinating glimpse into the future of humanity’s tech-
nological expansion beyond Earth. Bezos’s core message underscored the urgent need for a 
paradigm shift, asserting that the exponential growth of AI is rapidly pushing terrestrial energy 
grids and environmental resources to their breaking point. He highlighted the escalating issues 
of pollution, water scarcity, and increased electricity prices stemming from the construction of 
colossal, ground-based AI data centers.”
—“From Earth to Orbit: Jeff Bezos Unveils Radical Space-Based Solution to AI’s 
Looming Energy Crisis,” TokenRing AI, via FinancialContent / WRALTechWire, Octo-
ber 6, 2025, www.financialcontent.com.
The translator [between Xi Jinping and Vladimir Putin, caught on a hot mic] added, after an 
inaudible passage: “Human organs can be continuously transplanted. The longer you live, the 
younger you become, and (you can) even achieve immortality.”
—“Hot Mic Picks Up Putin and Xi Discussing Organ Transplants and Immortality,” 
Reuters (Beijing Newsroom), September 3, 2025.
INTRODUCTION
The universe works in mysterious ways. 
This is a concept—actually, more of a belief—held by students of metaphysics and mysticism for 
centuries. It often defies science and logic when the course of human civilization shifts in ways that 
no one could have foreseen in their specifics. As astrologers, we know when such transformational 
changes can take place, but we don’t always know exactly what form they will take or what will cause 
them. For example, during the Capricorn stellium of early 2020—when Jupiter, Saturn, and Pluto 
were joined by Mars in mid-February, all gathering in late Capricorn by mid-March—many mundane 
astrologers forecasted a powerful turning point in global socio-economic and financial conditions. 
Many predicted a recession and economic downturn, which indeed occurred. Some anticipated assas-
sinations of powerful world leaders or threats of major wars—and those, too, came to pass. However, 
to this writer’s knowledge, only one astrologer forecast a deadly generational pandemic that could 
kill millions in 2020. That was André Barbault, who, in 2012, wrote the following:
“Going back to the pandemics and going back to the past century, the four crises of 1918, 1954, 
1968, and 1982 are obvious, the two considerable being the first, the famous ‘Spanish flu,’ which 
is said to have claimed 25 million lives, and the last one marked by AIDS, which is even more 
devastating and continues to be deadly. We may well be in serious danger of a new pandemic at 
the 2020–2021 mark, at the lowest peak of the cyclical index of the 21st century, with the quintet 
## Page 31

27
of outer planets gathered over a hundred degrees, a conjunction Jupiter–Saturn-Pluto can more 
specifically, and even specifically, lend itself to the ‘tissue’ of this imbalance.” 2
The Aries Vortex is a rare and powerful configuration, first formally introduced in my Forecast 
2023 book, though I initially presented this epochal event to subscribers in 2021. It is expected to 
coincide with a profound and monumental shift in human activity during 2025–2027. As discussed in 
those annual books, this would likely mark the height of conflict, polarity, and division among people 
worldwide over differing beliefs and ideologies, possibly leading to wars. It would also be a time 
when the corruption of truth through propaganda by world leaders could control the narrative to such 
a degree that few would know what was real or false, or where this deception was leading humanity. 
At the same time, inventions and innovations in technology would usher in a new renaissance—a 
technological renaissance—as we had forecast. Humanity would face two parallel realities: one of 
wars and destruction, caused by ruthless leaders seeking to maintain power and control through 
coercion, and another of an incredible new future and work environment, spurred by discoveries and 
applications in technology—what we now recognize as artificial intelligence (AI).
It would be a time of great stress, division, and even hopelessness about the future felt by the 
masses. However, we also pointed out that 2026 +/− one year would mark the bottom of this abyss, 
after which the arc of division and polarity would begin to bend back toward unity and healing. 
These reflections offered an optimistic vision of the future, based on the approach and subsequent 
separation of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction, the apex of the Aries Vortex. This was a vision—a 
forecast—presented at a time when few believed that the tide of war, polarity, and division could ever 
turn or improve again.
This worrisome direction was amplified by the election of Donald Trump as U.S. president in 
November 2024. His first term had been polarizing for American citizens as well as for the allies of 
the United States around the world. And his 2024 campaign did very little to assure people that he 
would suddenly change and become a unifying force, either nationally or globally. It was hard to 
imagine how the nation and the world could heal under his presidency, given the extreme divisions 
that his rhetoric—including the vilification of anyone who challenged or resisted him—had only 
intensified. Yet, as stated at the start of this chapter, the universe works in mysterious ways.
 The cosmos had a message for Earthlings, but they were neither seeing nor hearing it through 
the first three quarters of 2025. Yet the cosmic message was still there. As we wrote in last year’s 
Forecast 2025 book:
For whatever reason many may not understand, Americans have chosen Donald Trump to 
return to the White House and to be the leader of this movement into—and then out of—the 
Aries Vortex. In astrology, it doesn’t matter who the individual leader is. What matters is that 
the nation and world see a path to a successful outcome that eventually brings humanity into a 
greater sense of unity. That is the promise of the Aries Vortex. 
There are two interesting chart patterns. One is a grand air trine between the Sun, Uranus, 
and Pluto, indicating great discoveries and applications in technology. The other is a peculiar 
Yod formation (“Hand of God”) in this and the previous ingress charts. This “Hand of God” 
signature indicates that fate, or karma, may be unfolding, and the destinies of the U.S. and 
other nations are being carried out as a result of (1) its prior actions and (2) the reaction to the 
results of those prior activities. If handled maturely and with a degree of accountability and

can finally be addressed, and the parties can move forward together in a spirit of greater trust. 
It sounds unlikely and perhaps impossible. But the cosmos moves in mysterious ways and offers 
opportunities like this during such rare celestial patterns. 
Then, in October 2025—completely unexpected by anyone entering the year—the historic Gaza

So, let us now examine the properties of the Aries Vortex further—and, in particular, the boundar-
ies that make up the funnel of the Aries Vortex, which are Uranus and Pluto in Gemini and Aquarius, 
respectively. As stated before, these two superpowers are in a 120° waxing (opening) trine aspect 
to one another, which by itself represents a long-term planetary-pair cycle ranging from 112 to 142 
years in duration, due to Pluto’s erratic orbit. Yet what makes this Aries Vortex funnel so remarkable 
is that, at the midpoint of its Uranus–Pluto boundaries lies the Saturn–Neptune conjunction serving 
as the apex of the vortex, which in turn forms a double sextile to both Uranus and Pluto, as shown 
in Figure 1 (in the Aries Vortex section of this book). So far, we have focused mainly on the Saturn–
Neptune conjunction, but equally important is the Uranus–Pluto trine, the midpoint of which is also 
the 0° Aries world point, occupied by Saturn and Neptune.
How rare is this planetary configuration involving the four outermost planets of our solar system 
in such an aspect formation? We have no record of it ever having occurred before. Therefore, we 
will explore what it portends by (1) applying basic astrological principles to both planets (Uranus 
and Pluto), as well as to their aspect (waxing trine) and the fact that they are in air signs, and (2) 
examining parts of this configuration that have occurred in the past to see whether any themes relate 
to current times while also opening up ideas about future possibilities. Specifically, we will examine 
historical periods when either Saturn or Neptune was at the midpoint of a Uranus–Pluto trine, since 
there are no instances when both were at the midpoint. In this matter, astrological researcher Daniel 
M. H. Gordon1 of Oregon (xstarian@gmail.com) conducted a special in-depth study at our request. 
We will share many of his fascinating findings in this chapter.
THE ASTROLOGY OF URANUS AND PLUTO
Uranus and Pluto share many themes in common. For instance, both are strongly correlated with 
major changes and disruptions in life. The difference lies in the pace of that change. With Uranus, 
it is usually sudden and unexpected—spreading like wildfire, suddenly out of control. In the case of 
Pluto, however, the pace of change is much slower, gradually building over time until the collective 
realizes that circumstances must change. The old ways become obsolete and no longer serve a valued 
purpose as they once did. 
One may think of Uranus as revolutionary and new—indicative of a dramatic change that is 
likely to be resisted by those in control. Change comes too quickly for the masses to adjust easily. It 
## Page 33

29
is like a storm appearing out of nowhere and wreaking havoc. With Pluto, the process is more like 
rolling thunder—darkening clouds gathering on the horizon and slowly moving closer and closer. 
You sense something powerful is building, readying to unleash its force.
Whereas the motivation behind Uranus is often revolution, the impulse behind Pluto is reform 
or transformation. With Uranus, there is a thrust toward something totally new and different, often 
driven by an urge for greater freedom and liberation from real or perceived oppression. In the case of 
Pluto, the desire is not so much for something new as it is to remove or terminate something old. Its 
time has come to an end. It is time to move on and build something different, more functional, or at 
least repair that which is no longer working as it should or once did. In this distinction, Uranus rep-
resents something young—perhaps even experimental or original. Pluto, on the other hand, pertains 
to something old, even obsolete, that has reached the point of decline and diminishing returns for the 
well-being of the masses.
MMA Market Analyst Gianni Di Poce likes to refer to the integration of these two principles as 
a force of “creative destruction.” This is an apt description because, in many ways, Uranus is indeed 
creative. At the very least, it is innovative and original. But to get there—with Pluto involved—also 
requires an act of destruction or termination. Through a process of elimination and release, the need 
arises to create something new and more relevant.
Pluto is driven to dismantle that which is no longer functioning well. Perhaps it pertains to some-
thing that has rotted or been allowed to decay—such as an old house, building, or even a system of 
governance. Yet if the powers in control refuse to let it go and insist there is still value in the old ways, 
a natural conflict arises between the young (Uranus) and the old (Pluto, in this case). It becomes a 
generational struggle for power (Pluto) that requires a revolution to overthrow and pave the way for 
a new vision and future to emerge (Uranus). Thus, under the favorable trine aspect, this may involve 
innovation and new discoveries that overwhelm existing systems to such an extent that it becomes 
obvious that new ways must be established. There arises an awareness that there is a much better way 
to do things than before—an organic process of change.
This is the nature of creative destruction. It is also the driving force behind what becomes a 
technological renaissance. We see this unfolding today with the explosion of AI, which has quickly 
reached a level of development where it can now perform many of the routines once carried out by 
the labor force. The work environment is a perfect example of the creative destruction taking place 
across societies worldwide—an evolution that is giving rise to the technological renaissance we 
have been alerting readers to over the past five years. It has been well underway since Pluto entered 
Aquarius in March 2023, though it is still in its early stages.
As a side note, this Uranus–Pluto trine can also provide a cosmic basis for healing the genera-
tional wounds that have persisted since the Uranus–Pluto square of 2012–2015. It was around that 
time that younger generations rebelled (sometimes violently) against older generations, in what later 
came to be called “cancel culture.” In this way, the younger generation refused to allow their elders 
to share experience or wisdom that might temper their disruptive activities. If a speaker from an older 
generation appeared on a college campus, students might force the speaker off the stage, canceling 
the event they deemed offensive based on generational identity or other aspects of “identity politics” 
they opposed. This was a major contributing factor to the polarity and division that led the world 
into the abyss of today’s Aries Vortex. But these wounds can now be addressed and healed now that 
Uranus and Pluto have moved beyond their difficult waxing square into a more harmonious trine. 
## Page 34

30
There are other sectors of human activity that are likely to be affected by the themes associated 
with both Uranus and Pluto, as well as by the air signs they are just entering. The signs are important 
because Uranus rules Aquarius and therefore disposes Pluto, which now occupies Aquarius through 
2043. Thus, the sign Aquarius—and its ruler Uranus—will stand out for several years. In fact, Uranus 
will be in Gemini, another air sign compatible with Aquarius, through 2032. Therefore, the period 
2025–2032 will be especially characterized by themes of renaissance, technology, innovation, dis-
covery, and revolution. However, there are other themes to consider related to Uranus and Aquarius, 
colored by Pluto’s presence—especially with both planets in air signs, an element associated with 
knowledge and original thought.
Consider that Uranus and Aquarius are both connected with outer space, the realm beyond Earth. 
The importance of exploring and finding applications for outer space is about to explode, largely 
because of the “environmental strain imposed by current AI operations,” as outlined by Jeff Bezos. 
The energy demands required to develop new data centers on Earth have grown as “the exponential 
growth of AI is rapidly pushing terrestrial energy grids and environmental resources to their breaking 
point.” This development complements the concept of creative destruction, which leads to the next 
level of today’s technological renaissance. 
The next step in humanity’s evolution and survival will involve the exploration—and eventually 
the mastery—of outer space, one step at a time. Each step will usher in new discoveries, innovations, 
and insights into this vast realm. With Uranus in Gemini and trine to Pluto in Aquarius, this configu-
ration can guide humanity into a new world of discovery, as illustrated on the inside front cover of 
this year’s book. It will stimulate learning how to utilize outer space more constructively in the next 
stage of humanity’s growth. Becoming an astronaut, or participating in the exploration of outer space 
through commercial or governmental ventures, may rapidly become an exciting profession in which 
demand and compensation could grow immensely over the next six years. This is also an area likely 
to offer excellent investment opportunities. 
As humans expand into outer space to address their burgeoning energy needs, efforts will also 
intensify to extend life itself. Here we have Pluto, the planet of death and rebirth, combining with 
Uranus, the planet of youth and technology, uniting their forces to explore the possibility of immor-
tality. Our current tech visionaries believe the human body is a flawed mechanism in need of a tech-
nological upgrade. Why should it decay, grow old, and die in physical pain? The idea that humans 
can live longer and better through technological advances—such as artificial limbs and decoding the 
human genome to eliminate diseases—is a core tenet of the modern intellectual and cultural move-
ment known as transhumanism. According to Gemini AI, “This perspective is driven by the desire to 
use technology to overcome human limitations, particularly aging and mortality.” This is also a per-
fect illustration of how the themes of Uranus and Pluto in an air trine can operate. Uranus and Pluto 
represent not only the process of creative destruction but also the impulse to discover and invent new 
processes that extend life and enhance well-being as humanity ages.

URANUS–PLUTO TRINES IN HISTORY
The forthcoming Uranus–Pluto trine will unfold in a five-passage series of exact waxing trines 
on July 18, 2026; November 29, 2026; June 15, 2027; January 13, 2028; and May 10, 2028. It should 
also be noted that Uranus and Pluto came within 7′ of one degree of an exact trine in September 2025, 
which is close enough to generate a cosmic influence. Thus, one can assume that the orb of influence 
of this remarkable outer-planet aspect will be in effect from 2025 through 2028. 
For reference, the last time these two planets were in an opening trine was during the three-
passage series from November 9, 1884, through September 21, 1885. It is interesting to note that in 
that instance, both planets were also in the early degrees of air signs (Uranus in Libra and Pluto in 
Gemini). According to Daniel Gordon’s research, “In 1884, the United States was in a period of its 
‘long depression,’ and yet this led to the Second Industrial Revolution. This also coincided with the 
rise of industrial Japan, accompanied by social change. Meanwhile, at the Berlin Conference, the 
European powers carved up Africa into colonies under their rule, developing new trade routes and 
new trading conditions, which led to an immediate economic addition to the asset sheet of the king.” 
## Page 36

32
The time before that was a seven-passage series spanning from August 11, 1770, to April 
29, 1773. This instance involved earth signs (Taurus and Capricorn), which are relevant to the 
masses rebelling against governments whose policies of control were viewed as oppressive. In the 
American colonies, early settlers protested corrupt officials, heavy taxes, and unfair fees. The con-
flict—and the subsequent executions of several Regulators—highlighted the growing tensions and 
resistance to British authority in the colonies. In 1773 America, for instance, the major event was 
the Boston Tea Party, when, according to Gemini AI, “Colonists dumped British tea into Boston 
Harbor to protest the Tea Act, a British law that granted a tea monopoly to the East India Com-
pany and imposed a tax on tea without colonial representation.” This is another classic instance 
combining themes related to Uranus (rebellion, disruption, desire for equality, and independence 
from authority) and Pluto (taxation). “Taxation without representation” remains a rallying cry for 
citizens protesting taxation initiatives by the U.S. government without the vote of its citizenry. It is 
likely a theme that will come to the forefront in the 2026 midterm elections—assuming elections 
take place as scheduled.
There are many prior examples of Uranus in a waxing trine to Pluto, several of which demon-
strate major conflicts between coercion, oppression, and the drive of the masses to free themselves 
from tyrannical forces through rebellion. One such example is the nine-passage series from 1514 
through 1518, which resulted in sweeping transformations across culture, government, and religion 
in Europe. Once again, according to AI, “The period from 1514 to 1518 was a time of significant 
military conflict, the start of the Protestant Reformation, and continued European exploration. Key 
events included the start of the Ottoman-Mamluk War and Martin Luther’s posting of the Ninety-
five Theses.” 
Uranus–Pluto trine periods have also brought forth important inventions that have had a positive, 
transformational effect on societies throughout the world, as one would expect from a trine (favor-
able) aspect. 
In his insightful research, in which he also analyzed the waning (closing) trine of Uranus and 
Pluto, Gordon identified many recurring themes that astrology would ascribe to these two planets, 
especially when both are in air signs. He notes the following: 
There is a disrupted central authority in each of these periods, whether dynastic, papal, or 
imperial. 
Social relationships through economic behavior show that trade routes and economic systems 
change and adapt to new conditions in a positive way. 
These are often crisis periods of change to social institutions and the social contract. In many 
instances, this is a form of war because those with money and power do not willingly give it up. The 
social contract changes when the government changes. 
Taxation, monetary systems, and trade routes all change during these time bands.
 Currency debasement and the collapse of monetary systems raise questions about where to store 
wealth. 
Each time, there seems to be a generational change from the old way of doing things to a new 
way because of economic forces. 
## Page 37

33
In this reshaping and change of power, there is often a military element, the success of which is 
based upon technological advancement. Some people preach separateness, and some preach one-
ness. Those preaching separateness become the dysfunctional ones.
Do any of these themes during Uranus–Pluto trine periods sound familiar today? Gordon also 
points out, “An interesting side note is that from 740 until the coming 2026, there has been only one 
instance when the air trine between Uranus and Pluto (including both waxing and waning) did not 
involve the sign of Aquarius. That was when Uranus in Libra was trine to Pluto in Gemini in 1884–
85. All other times, the sign of Aquarius held either Uranus or Pluto.” 
Indeed, if history is not repeating itself under Uranus–Pluto trines in air signs, it sure sounds like 
it rhymes.
SATURN AT THE MIDPOINT OF URANUS AND PLUTO
Now comes a very interesting study related to Gordon’s research on historical periods when Sat-
urn, and then Neptune, were at the midpoint of the Uranus–Pluto trine. 
In the current alignment, Saturn and Neptune are both at the midpoint of the Uranus–Pluto trine, 
but we have no historical instances to draw from in which both planets were in a double sextile simul-
taneously. Still, studying those periods when either Saturn or Neptune was at the midpoint between 
Uranus and Pluto provides very interesting insights that relate to current times. 
Saturn was posited at the midpoint of Uranus and Pluto, while sextile to each, in 482, 543, 
618, 907, 1255, and will be again in 2025–2026. During these periods, Gordon observed, “…old 
government systems were weakening and collapsing, and new systems were rising but fragmented. 
Laws were being reformed, reordered, and rewritten, and new laws were passed after a period of 
chaos. Money and the economy were usually disrupted because the trade networks and routes col-
lapsed and needed rebuilding. The disruption to human society was noted as a turning point when 
old systems were hanging onto new systems, but the old systems could not remain and were reborn 
into the new system.” 
Once again, this aligns with many of today’s global themes as we enter 2026. Saturn rules laws 
and governments. With Pluto, new rules (laws) are reordered and rewritten in an effort to end chaos 
(Uranus). Trade routes could very well be disrupted, as we see today through the use of tariffs as 
weapons to pressure other nations into meeting specific demands. And yet today we also see the 
advent of new technologies (Uranus) forcing out old systems of governance and practice as new 
systems are created. It has happened before, according to Gordon, and we are seeing it happen again 
today with Saturn at the midpoint of the Uranus–Pluto trine. 
## Page 38

34
Figure 3: Saturn (and Neptune) forming a double sextile to Uranus and Pluto, in effect 
from August 2025 to March 2026. This is an Aries chart set for August 11, 2025. Following 
this period, Saturn begins to separate from its sextiles to Uranus and Pluto, leaving 
Neptune to maintain its double sextile to Uranus and Pluto through 2028.
One point to understand is that, as the midpoint of two other outer planets in a favorable sextile 
to each other, Saturn draws favorable power from both Uranus and Pluto. The government or author-
ity (Saturn), or the entity that controls the situation, receives the combined blessing of power and 
innovation provided by Uranus and Pluto. In today’s case, however, Saturn is in Aries, where it can 
be coercive and demanding, imposing its will over the masses, who do not enjoy that kind of power 
and control. That control could begin to wane as Saturn moves out of the double-sextile formation 
and the collective once subject to its controlling influence begins to regain its power. 
As long as Saturn in Aries (in today’s case) remains at the midpoint of the Uranus–Pluto trine, the 
central authority will have its way—for better or worse. In many cases, conditions in society could 
actually improve if that authority focuses on building enduring structures and systems. Authorities 
may be dominating, but they can also provide many benefits that endure over time.
NEPTUNE AT THE MIDPOINT OF URANUS AND PLUTO
Most relevant to today’s sudden swing toward peace and the end of hostilities in the Middle East 
is Neptune, located at the midpoint of the Uranus–Pluto trine and sextile to each.
## Page 39

35
There have been three historical periods when Neptune was at the midpoint of a Uranus–Pluto 
trine, as examined in Gordon’s study. These were 476–480, 991, and now again, 2023–2027. With 
Saturn, one would expect attention to focus on governance—and indeed, changes in governance were 
pronounced, as shown in the previous paragraphs. But with Neptune, one would expect major transi-
tions involving religion, the arts, and efforts to end wars and usher in prolonged periods of peace.
In Gordon’s words, regarding the highlights of these three periods: “In each of these times in 
history, there was a decline of the dominant power and a rise of local powers with the local actors: a 
trend to decentralization. There arose new social structures, technology, networks, and trade routes, 
even while the old ones collapsed. Knowledge shifted to new physical centers of collection and hold-
ing. There were new art forms developed in cultural crossroad areas built of old traditions and new 
technology. Finally, religion spread during these times of political change and fragmentation.”
The 476–480 period marked the fall of the Roman Empire—one of the greatest military and 
governmental eras in human history—which began around 750 BC. The year AD 476 is often used 
by historians to mark the transition from antiquity to the Middle Ages in Europe. In other words, this 
was a profoundly important turning point in world history. Its themes resonate with today’s possible 
decline of American exceptionalism as the world’s leading power and the concurrent rise of emerging 
leaderships in the Far East, particularly China and India.
The 991 period was also interesting. The “Peace of God” was enacted at the Council of Char-
roux just before then. It was a plan aimed at reducing feudal warfare by limiting private wars to 
certain times of the year and by providing protection for noncombatants. The Peace of God move-
ment relied on the threat of excommunication to enforce its decrees. The Church was all-powerful. 
Also of interest is that in 992 there were notable celestial events: historical records describe major 
auroras observed in Korea, Germany, and Ireland, likely caused by a strong solar event, according to 
Gemini AI. We note that powerful solar storms are erupting now as we leave 2025 and enter 2026. 
Such explosive solar activity tends to correlate with strong changes on Earth—in weather, climate, 
governments, and financial markets alike.
We have only two instances to draw from in the past two millennia. And keep in mind that neither 
Uranus, Neptune, nor Pluto was even known to humans during those times. Yet we can apply our 
understanding of these cosmic themes to what we observe today. Let’s start with Neptune, since it 
is the midpoint between Uranus and Pluto. Furthermore, these are the three outermost planets in our 
solar system, with the longest orbits around the Sun. Thus, we might assume that this could be con-
sidered the most important configuration of all during the lifetime of most people reading this book.
We begin with the idea that Neptune is the planet of peace. Planets represent actions. They are 
more powerful than signs, which represent attitudes and therefore color the actions of the planets 
transiting through them. In this case, Neptune seeks to bring peace to Aries, the sign whose attitude 
is basically “me first” and “I will do what I want, and you won’t stop me.” Aries is ruled by Mars, 
the god of war. So here comes Neptune, the god(dess) of peace, entering the sign ruled by the god of 
war, and saying something like: “I want you to de-escalate your aggression and not be so combative. 
I want you to pull back and use your warrior mentality in the effort to bring peace to the world.” Wars 
that begin—or are underway—when Neptune enters Aries tend to wind down.
## Page 40

36
Figure 4: Neptune forming a double sextile to Uranus and Pluto (2025–2028), as Saturn begins to sepa-
rate. This is an Aries chart constructed for July 25, 2026. Neptune is the planet of peace initiatives.
Wars are high on the agenda today because Saturn is in Aries and at the midpoint of Uranus and 
Pluto, sextile to each. Saturn in Aries—warlike and bullying—is more akin to Uranus (revolution) 
and Pluto (coercion and reform) than to Neptune (withdrawal and the search for peace). Thus, Saturn 
is presently drawing more from its sextiles to Uranus and Pluto than from Neptune. It conveys an 
attitude of “peace through strength” rather than one of diplomacy, trust, and goodwill. 
But what happens when Saturn begins to separate from its double sextile to Uranus and Pluto 
after March 2026, while Neptune remains there for another two years? Neptune then starts to draw the 
benefits of power from its sextiles to Uranus and Pluto. This creates an entirely different dynamic—
one that bodes well for efforts to end wars and attain peace on Earth. This is the cosmic correlation 
to the sudden (Uranus) emergence of peace in the Middle East after eight decades of hostility and 
conflict, along with an effort to rebuild (Pluto) Gaza as a seaside (Neptune) destination for future 
world travelers.
This is the peak of the Aries Vortex, and possibly the nadir of the abyss of hatred and division. 
It symbolizes the pendulum’s swing from discord and conflict to a period of ten years or more of 
relative peace and rebuilding. This is why I have remained optimistic about the Aries Vortex and 
## Page 41

where it will lead humanity. I don’t know how—no one knew how—this would manifest, espe-
cially under the polarizing leadership style of President Donald Trump. But here it is. He gets 
the credit, as it was his individual force of personality, projecting “peace through strength,” that 
brought Hamas and other terrorist organizations to the peace table and started the process of end-
ing the Middle East conflicts over Israel’s right to exist. Love him or hate him, he deserves the 
credit for this manifestation of the positive dynamic underlying the Aries Vortex—something few 
believed possible until now.
SUMMARY
Just as important as the Saturn–Neptune conjunction at 0° Aries in the remarkable Aries Vortex 
configuration is the Uranus–Pluto trine, the midpoint of which is also at 0° Aries. In other words, 
0° Aries forms the apex of both the Uranus–Pluto trine, which defines the boundaries of the funnel, 
and the Saturn–Neptune conjunction, which defines its apex. There has never been a configuration 
like this in recorded history—at least none known to us—involving all four of the outermost planets 
converging at 0° Aries, the starting point of the zodiac, also known as the “world point.” 
When we break down each of these components in terms of their correlation to historical events 
and trends—and attempt to interpret their meaning according to astrological themes and principles—
we find many possible manifestations as we enter 2026. There are so many cosmic dynamics con-
verging within a short period that it can seem overwhelming, both in terms of individual experience 
and in terms of future possibilities for humanity and the planet itself. Nevertheless, the following is 
a partial list of major points that I believe will define human activity over the next year, especially 
those associated with the air trine aspect between Uranus and Pluto:
1.	 Efforts to usher in a new era of peace on Earth lasting at least ten years
2.	 Outer space exploration and development to meet the world’s increasing need for energy, 
which is rapidly approaching overload on Earth
3.	 The quest for immortality and the extension of human life and physical well-being
4.	 New cures for diseases such as various forms of cancer
5.	 Creative destruction leading to the overhaul of obsolete systems and structures
6.	 A technological renaissance transforming the labor market and creating new career opportu-
nities related to outer space
7.	 Decentralization and the collapse of old systems of government
8.	 Revolutions inspired by innovation rather than overthrow or rebellion
9.	 Debasement and transformation of currencies
10.	 Wealth seeking new places to flow, leading to major economic reforms and the creation of 
new trade routes
11.	 Laws reformed, reordered, and rewritten as new legislation follows a period of chaos
12.	 A revival of religion and renewed interest in both traditional and emerging faiths
## Page 42

38
This is truly a “New Aira” humanity is moving into. And the chaos accompanying these vast 
social, cultural, economic, and governmental changes will require flexibility and a willingness to 
adapt. There are parallel realities unfolding: one driven by forces of destruction and resistance to 
change (i.e., wars), and the other by the power of creation and invention through a technological 
renaissance that will eventually lead to an economic boom—though likely following an economic 
bust. The danger of taking on too much risk is great, but the opportunity for success through well-
considered risk-taking is even greater. Uranus represents risk, while Pluto signifies the potential for 
great loss. Yet, they are in a favorable trine aspect, which bodes well for a successful renewal—even 
if a major financial downturn occurs along the way.

 THE CHART OF MODERN MANKIND
Freedom’s just another word 
for nothin’ left to lose.
—Janis Joplin, “Me and Bobby McGee,” written by Kris Kristofferson, 1971.
Last year, we introduced the “Horoscope of Modern Mankind,” which was presented by Claude 
Weiss at the MMA 2024 Investment Retreat, held September 19–22, 2024, in Lake Bled, Slovenia. 
This chart was originally proposed in 1992 by Eric Alan Meese in the magazine Welcome to Planet 
Earth, formerly published by astrologer Mark Lerner. We return to this chart again, as it shows further 
astrological developments supporting our view of the Aries Vortex and its potential for the ongoing 
monumental transformations taking place at this time in the history of humankind.
The chart of Modern Mankind is constructed on the last conjunction of the longest planetary 
synodic cycle known, which is between Neptune and Pluto. This conjunction cycle lasts between 492 
and 496 years and last occurred on April 30, 1892 (the third of three passes). Since the exact moment 
of that conjunction cannot be defined—because Neptune and Pluto move so slowly that they can 
occupy the same degree and minute for days—the new moon that preceded this conjunction is used 
as the starting point. That new moon was also a solar eclipse and thus magnified the importance of 
this cosmic event, which occurred on April 26. 
The time used for the advent of the chart of Modern Mankind is the solar eclipse of April 26, 
1892, at 9:47 PM GMT, just before the third and final passage of Neptune conjunct Pluto. The time 
of this eclipse is known to the exact minute and hence serves the purpose of a timed chart very well. 
The location chosen for this chart is Greenwich, England, since it serves as the prime meridian and 
reference point for world time (GMT). However, the chart could be relocated to any other location 
and the angles adjusted accordingly, which might be useful when identifying regions over which the 
outer planets transit the chart’s angles over time. For our purposes here, we will stay with GMT.
Note that at the time of the solar eclipse on April 26, 1892, the Sun and Moon (i.e., new moon) 
were in early Taurus, in opposition to Uranus in early Scorpio (see the chart below). This is important 
because Pluto will be transiting in a T-square to the natal Uranus and the Sun–Moon opposition in this 
chart from February 8, 2026, to February 6, 2028. 
With transits of Pluto, we have one basic rule: no one escapes unscathed under a hard Pluto 
transit to a natal point. In this case, the transit of Pluto relates to a global need to address a difficult 
situation confronting humankind. It won’t be easy. Something has to end in order for something 
new and better to begin. A major transformation for humanity—or the Earth itself—is called for, as 
threats to its existence, the lives of many people, or its basic economic or social stability may be at 
risk. This could be due to a natural calamity such as an earthquake, tsunami, hurricane, or volcanic 
eruption. It could be due to some kind of advancing existential threat, perhaps related to global warm-
ing or climate change. It could be in the form of a threat to humankind from a powerful leader who 
has the capability to put the lives of millions at risk. Or it could be a financial crisis, given that Pluto 
(planet of debt, deficits, downgrades, and defaults) is in the second house of finances, while the natal 
Moon—which rules the eighth house (financial crisis and debt) of this chart—is also involved. With 
natal Uranus activated, it indicates that the masses of humanity are in a mood to rebel or revolt in 
## Page 44

40
order to gain greater freedoms, rights, and even power. But it could also indicate that a world leader 
“loses his mind” and simply detaches from reality, putting others at great risk through a terrorist act. 
In other words, this can portend a very dangerous cosmic development, and it would be wise for 
leaders of the world to recognize when such a person or situation might present an existential threat 
to the world. 
Figure 5: Chart of Modern Mankind, “born” April 26, 1892, when Neptune conjoined Pluto, 
as seen from London, UK. Note: not only did Neptune conjoin Pluto on the Descendant, but 
the solar eclipse preceding this date (when the Sun and Moon conjoined at 7° Taurus) was 
also in opposition to Uranus at 3° Scorpio. 
With Pluto as the transiting planet, there may be an advance warning before an event erupts. 
Pluto events do not happen suddenly, although Uranus transits do, and both planets will be high-
lighted during the next two years. Readers must understand that with any powerful transit like this 
one involving Pluto, there are many ways an event may actually unfold. And if specific dangers are 
recognized before a major crisis erupts, changes can usually be made to prevent or minimize their 
impact. Pluto (and all planets) is an indicator of potential events, such as threats, but these do not 
necessarily manifest if conscious choices are made to express the positive potentials of the cosmic 
signatures involved. Instead of an actual crisis, Pluto can symbolize an awareness to make a major 
change in behavior before further troubles arise. Let’s hope our world leaders are astute and wise 
enough to spot a major threat to the masses if it arises, as indicated by this chart, and do something 
## Page 45

41
about it before any calamity occurs. Our duty as astrologers is to point out the timing of such pos-
sibilities, both positive and negative, but with the understanding that one can transform into the other. 
The outcome depends as much, if not more, on the choices humans make as it does on geocosmic 
aspects being causal. They correlate with human activity but are not to be considered purely causal.
Figure 6: Transits of August 11, 2026, to the chart of Mankind. Note the transit of Pluto forming a 
T-square with Uranus opposite the Sun–Moon conjunction in the natal chart, while transiting Uranus 
conjoins the natal Descendant, Neptune, and Pluto, and forms a trine to transiting Pluto. 
It would be enough to warrant our attention if Pluto were the only outer-planet transit active dur-
ing the next two years. However, that is not the case. All the outermost planets will be activated in 
2026 and even into 2027–2028. Uranus, for example, will be in early Gemini, transiting the Descen-
dant as well as the Neptune–Pluto conjunctions in the seventh house. This is quite fascinating because 
as Uranus, the disruptor, conjoins this powerful natal angular point, and also Neptune and Pluto, from 
July 24, 2026, through April 17, 2028, it will be forming a trine to Pluto in the skies. That is, transiting 
Uranus will conjoin Mankind’s Neptune and Pluto, while transiting Pluto will also be in a trine aspect 
with Neptune and Pluto in the Mankind chart. So, this is not a harbinger of total destruction or annihi-
lation but rather a symbol of death and rebirth. Once again, it is the theme of creative destruction—
the possibility that long-established directions and traditions of the human experience are ending, but 
as a result of something new being created (Uranus). We may think we have a clear vision of what 
this means, but with Uranus, we don’t really, for Uranus pertains to the unexpected and something 
## Page 46

42
completely new. But as with Uranus, the natal planet, the transit of Uranus also relates to the drive of 
the masses to attain freedom and new rights. With Uranus, the theme in an individual’s chart is that 
of a new lifestyle. But in this case, it is a new direction (lifestyle) for humanity as a whole, not just 
for certain individuals. One idea that comes to mind again is the exploration—and maybe even the 
settlement—somewhere outside of Earth, in outer space.
Transiting Saturn and Neptune will also be important in early 2026, as both will transit over the 
I.C. (bottom) of this chart. Saturn is especially noteworthy, for as it crosses the nadir (I.C.) of a chart, 
it symbolizes the end and beginning of a new cycle in the life of the entity. Generally speaking, this 
represents the bottom of the external part of one’s existence and the uphill climb to greater success 
and accomplishment over the next 17 years, until Saturn reaches the midpoint between the M.C. and 
Ascendant (around the middle of the eleventh house). This also bodes well for the future once Saturn 
crosses that threshold of Mankind’s nadir. 
In the final analysis, though, it is the transits of Pluto and Uranus that seem most critical to under-
stand and prepare for. It may be helpful to review some of our thoughts about this Chart of Mankind, 
as given last year, in order to further grasp the significance of what is about to be disrupted, brought 
to an end, and then reborn. As stated in Forecast 2025, “Another factor of the Chart of Modern Man-
kind that commands attention is the Solar Eclipse at 7° Taurus, in opposition to Uranus at 3° Scor-
pio. This represents a conflict between the wish for security and peace (Taurus) as well as financial 
opportunity (also Taurus) against the presence of strong forces of chaos and revolution (Uranus) that 
can put the lives of many in physical or financial danger (Scorpio). Taurus wants to build and enjoy 
security. But Scorpio (with Uranus involved) has an urge to tear down and rebuild all over again. 
Traditions (Taurus) can be upended by these revolutions and can disregard norms and customs that 
hold societies together.” This is the dynamic of human activity and civilization up until this point that 
Pluto is about to transform.

 PLUTO IN AQUARIUS: REVOLUTIONARY CHANGE
by Pouyan Zolfagharnia, MMA Analyst
Pluto’s slow, shadowed journey at the edge of our solar system mirrors its power to shape the 
deep currents of collective change. The farther a planet lies from the Sun, the greater its impact 
on mundane affairs. After fifteen years in Capricorn, Pluto began its twenty-year passage through 
Aquarius in March 2023. With a 248-year orbit, Pluto’s movements are rare markers of civilizational 
turning points. Where data cannot reach, astrology becomes our lens for interpreting how this shift 
may reverberate through markets and society alike.
Pluto governs transformation, regeneration, and power—the unseen forces behind debt, taxation, 
interest rates, and the mechanisms through which governments and central banks wield control. It 
is the planet of change, separation, death and rebirth, inheritance, windfall gains, destruction, and 
renewal. Ray calls it the planet of the four D’s: debt, deficits, downgrades, and defaults. Its energy is 
immense, catalytic, and often explosive. I consider it the higher octave of Mars; therefore, warfare 
and destruction usually accompany its initial ingress into a new sign (as seen with Russia–Ukraine 
and Israel–Hamas). 
Aquarius, by contrast, embodies humanity, equality, intellect, invention, and revolt. It is the sign 
of discovery, exploration, electricity, uranium, technology, forceful intervention, revolution, and the 
collective will. It represents the masses—the 99% of the population that controls 1% of the world’s 
wealth (in opposition to Leo, the 1% that controls 99% of global capital). With Jupiter in Leo form-
ing an opposition to Pluto in Aquarius in the summer of 2026, we could see this theme of financial 
polarization and social redistribution surface.
When Pluto enters Aquarius, the deepest forces of metamorphosis infiltrate the sign of the water 
bearer, carrying not the chalice of the individual soul but the amphora of collective life. As Pluto 
transits Aquarius, the unconscious energies of transformation tunnel through the latticework of col-
lective thought, shaking the very fabric of civilization. We stand at the threshold of profound social 
and structural transformation—a reconfiguration of power, technology, and belief that may alter the 
very foundations of our world.
Pluto first entered Aquarius on March 23, 2023, and after a couple of retrogrades back into Capri-
corn, it made its final ingress on November 19, 2024. It will remain in Aquarius until its final exit on 
January 19, 2044. This twenty-year arc echoes three previous transits upon which I based my study: 
April 1777 to December 1798; February 1532 to December 1553; and March 1286 to November 
1308. These are not fleeting influences but epochs that ushered in structural revolutions in belief, 
governance, science, and human self-conception. Each previous Pluto-in-Aquarius cycle coincided 
with tectonic global transformations whose consequences cascaded far beyond their own time. This 
one is no exception, as we have already seen with the advent of artificial intelligence and the trans-
formation it is creating.
When Pluto last entered Aquarius in 1777, the American colonies were in open revolt against 
monarchical rule. Within a year, France would recognize the nascent United States, and the world 
would witness the first modern democracy born of Enlightenment ideals embodied in the Declaration 
## Page 48

44
of Independence. Not long after, in 1789, the French Revolution would erupt, dismantling centuries 
of feudalism, aristocracy, and divine right. It was as though the axis of power (Pluto) shifted from 
Capricorn (the king and aristocracy) to Aquarius (the people). Amid the chaos, the Rights of Man 
were proclaimed and the metric system invented—symbols both of egalitarian vision and rational 
order. The old regimes, long upheld by religion and inherited privilege, cracked under the pressure 
of new ideologies. The guillotine’s blade was both literal and symbolic: it severed the head from the 
body politic, and the old world from the new. Yet even these revolutions carried their shadows: the 
French “Reign of Terror,” the rise of Napoleon, the American Revolutionary War, and the ironies 
of liberty built on the backs of enslaved people. Still, the structures of power had been irrevocably 
altered.
Numerous advances in science occurred in the years leading to Pluto’s 1777 ingress into 
Aquarius (an air sign). Chemist Carl Wilhelm Scheele made several breakthroughs in chemistry, 
discovering oxygen (1771), barium (1772), chlorine (1774), manganese (1774), and molybdenum 
(1778). In 1778, Scottish scientist Daniel Rutherford isolated nitrogen gas from the air. These 
discoveries paved the way for the invention of the hot-air balloon by the Montgolfier brothers. 
Advancements in science go hand in hand with the development of technology. How fitting, then, 
that the Industrial Revolution is said to have begun during Pluto’s transit through Aquarius in the 
1780s. Are we on the cusp of a technological—or perhaps cyber—revolution? With Uranus (arti-
ficial, technological, electrical) ingressing into Gemini (intelligence, mind, networks, vehicles), 
we are already witnessing groundbreaking progress in artificial intelligence, quantum computing, 
electric vehicles, and genetic technologies.
A cycle earlier, from 1532 to 1553, the Reformation tore through Europe. Luther’s challenge to 
Rome, ignited in 1517, had by this time become a conflagration of national and spiritual self-defi-
nition. In England, Henry VIII severed the Church of England from papal authority, solidifying the 
Protestant Reformation and setting the stage for the Industrial Revolution during Pluto’s next transit 
through Aquarius. Across Europe, Protestants and Catholics waged both ideological and military war, 
and the question of conscience (Aquarius) versus authority (Capricorn) came to define the age. Dur-
ing the same span, Copernicus’s heliocentric model was published, quietly dismantling the geocentric 
cosmos and elevating human reason as a force capable of dethroning dogma. These were not merely 
religious or scientific shifts—they were existential realignments of humanity’s place in the universe, 
orchestrated through Pluto’s invisible hand moving behind Aquarius’s crystalline lattice of ideas.
Reaching further back, the 1286–1308 transit marked the waning of the Crusades, the final fall of 
Acre in 1291, and the subsequent retreat of Christendom from the Holy Land. In Europe, the Mongol 
Empire fractured into khanates, and the Ottoman state was born faintly and quietly in Anatolia, yet 
destined to dominate the region for centuries. In Scotland, resistance to English rule culminated in 
the rise of Robert the Bruce, setting in motion a centuries-long national identity. These were stirrings 
of future empires, ideological partitions, and nationalist awakenings. Even in these less illuminated 
centuries, Pluto’s Aquarian pulse could be felt in the collective rearrangement of power and meaning.
Taken together, these epochs teach that Pluto in Aquarius does not merely transform govern-
ments or spark innovation—it rewires the circuitry of the collective mind. It is a time when invis-
ible convictions become visible architectures. Systems once thought immutable (divine right, papal 
authority, hereditary class, and egocentricity) collapse beneath the weight of new logic. This logic 
may be scientific, democratic, or spiritual, but it is always systemic. Aquarius does not tinker; it reen-
gineers. It does not evolve; it revolts. 
## Page 49

45
As we now enter the 2023–2044 transit, we do so already midstream in a sea of metamorphosis. 
The world is reeling from a pandemic that altered human interaction at every level (social, economic, 
and spiritual). Artificial intelligence, once the domain of speculative fiction, now crafts art, writes 
essays, and challenges our sense of creativity and authorship. Climate change is no longer a future 
threat but a present reality, compelling a reimagination of energy, consumption, and planetary stew-
ardship. Political systems are fraying under the weight of hyperpolarization, and the question of 
governance itself—who decides, how, and why—is under renewed scrutiny. These are not random 
disruptions; they are the signature of Pluto moving through Aquarius—a time when the infrastruc-
tures of thought and the blueprints of society are subject to collapse and renewal.
As Pluto shifts its axis of power from Capricorn into Aquarius, we may be standing at the thresh-
old of a profound change in the global monetary order. The age of the petrodollar—a distinctly Capri-
cornian symbol of control, structure, and authority—may be giving way to a new financial paradigm 
rooted in decentralization and digital innovation. This could manifest through the rise of cryptocur-
rencies or perhaps through a future reserve system anchored in blockchain technology, reflecting the 
Aquarian ideals of transparency, equality, and collective empowerment.
In much the same way, the centers of worldly influence appear to be shifting from the traditional 
sphere of politicians and institutions, shaped by Capricorn’s discipline and hierarchy, toward the 
visionary realm of technology leaders and digital pioneers. The Kissingers of old are being replaced 
by the Zuckerbergs and Jensen Huangs of the new—figures who shape global dynamics not through 
diplomacy and statecraft but through data, platforms, and artificial intelligence. One need only look 
at President Trump’s inner circle to see this transition unfolding, as the engines of political power 
become increasingly intertwined with the architecture of technology and the ambitions of a new kind 
of elite.
Aquarius, being fixed air, is the principle of ideational structure. It governs constitutions, tech-
nologies, collectives, and the unseen patterns that bind individual minds into societal order. When 
Pluto moves through this terrain, it brings the underworld’s depth to bear upon the sky’s abstraction. 
In practical terms, this may mean the exposure of corruption within institutions, the dissolution of 
dysfunctional systems, and the obsessive pursuit of new paradigms. Yet such changes are rarely 
smooth, as we have seen with the cuts implemented by the Department of Government Efficiency 
(DOGE). The last time this transit occurred, liberty and terror walked hand in hand; before that, reli-
gious freedom gave way to inquisitions and wars. Pluto brings to light that which must decay—not to 
destroy for destruction’s sake, but to compost the soil of civilization for future growth.
In the years ahead, we may witness the reshaping of global alliances, the redefinition of rights in 
the digital and biological realms, and the rise of new forms of identity that transcend nation, gender, 
and tradition. Aquarius speaks of the group, but Pluto asks: at what cost? Surveillance technologies, 
biometric data, and algorithmic governance may promise efficiency yet threaten the very freedoms 
they aim to protect. The paradox of Aquarius is that its utopian impulse can, under Pluto’s pressure, 
veer into dystopia. What begins as collective liberation may end in technocratic control—unless tem-
pered by wisdom and ethical clarity.
Yet history shows that these are also times of extraordinary human brilliance. When the old world 
breaks, the new world becomes possible. The heliocentric model was heresy before it was astronomy. 
Democracy was treason before it became a principle. In each case, the seeds were sown during 
Pluto’s passage through Aquarius. 
## Page 50

46
In summary, these are the key recurring patterns identified from studying prior transits of 
Pluto through Aquarius. They represent the overarching undertone of mundane activity over 
the coming two decades:
•	
Revolution and rebellion: Political change in the structure of governance
•	
Major power transition: The fall of the old empire and the rise of the new
•	
Technological transformation: Intellectual progress through innovation
•	
Social reform and collective ideals: Expansion of rights and establishment of new social 
contracts
•	
Polarization and persecution: The “us vs. them” mentality taken to extremes
•	
Paradigm shift: Re-evaluation of fundamental truths and organizing principles 
•	
Exploration: Transformation in our understanding of the world and our place within it

 NEPTUNE IN ARIES: THE DAWN OF NEW DREAMS
by Pouyan Zolfagharnia, MMA Analyst
When Neptune crosses the fiery threshold of Aries, the collective dream meets the first sign of the 
zodiac—the spark of beginnings, the will to incarnate, the courage to act. Neptune, planet of vision, 
dissolution, and transcendent imagination, moves with an almost unimaginable slowness, circling the 
Sun once every 165 years and spending approximately 14 years in each sign. It governs the tides of 
human consciousness, the rise and fall of ideals, the blurring of boundaries between what is seen and 
what is intuited. 
Aries, by contrast, is the archetype of emergence: cardinal fire, ruled by Mars—the pulse of ini-
tiative, the assertion of individuality. When the oceanic depth of Neptune enters the furnace of Aries, 
humanity is asked to dream not in abstraction but in motion, to translate longing into action, and to 
awaken through the heat of new beginnings. This meeting will define the years from March 30, 2025, 
when Neptune first entered Aries, to March 24, 2039, when it departs the sign for the final time. Nep-
tune will ignite the first degrees of the zodiac, closing the long Piscean era of surrender and faith and 
ushering in a cycle of spiritual confrontation and renewal. I have reviewed the prior three instances of 
Neptune in Aries—1533–1548, 1697–1712, and 1861–1875—each marked by revolution, invention, 
and a burning sense that the world was beginning again.
In the spring of 1533, when Neptune last blazed into Aries at the dawn of the modern age, Europe 
was splitting along lines of belief and power. Henry VIII’s break with Rome, John Calvin’s new the-
ology, and the first stirrings of the Council of Trent transformed religion from a single edifice into a 
battlefield of conscience. The Reformation tore the veil of medieval unity and authority, and behind it 
rose the sovereign state and the free (Aries) mind (Neptune). At the same time, Copernicus prepared 
De revolutionibus, shifting the cosmos itself: the Sun, not the Earth, at the center—an idea as radical 
then as the notion of artificial intelligence or space colonization is now. The conquistadors crossed 
oceans; the Jesuits crossed continents. The human spirit, intoxicated by its own potential, burned to 
claim and to know. As Neptune left Pisces for Aries, faith (Pisces) was transmuted into struggle, and 
revelation into discovery (Aries). The world’s map was redrawn, its heavens reimagined, and human-
ity stood—dazzled—on the brink of its modern identity and place in the cosmos. A paradigm shift 
had occurred.
A century and a half later, in 1697, Neptune again entered Aries beneath a sky of gunpowder and 
invention. Europe convulsed in the War of the Spanish Succession, while in the north Peter the Great’s 
armies shattered Sweden’s power and founded St. Petersburg on the Baltic marshes. These were wars 
not merely of territory but of principle: who would define the shape of empire, who would claim 
divine right, and who would harness the newborn engines of science. Newton’s Opticks appeared in 
1704, revealing that light consists of particles rather than waves—a paradox befitting Neptune’s mys-
tic symbolism. Locke’s empiricism and the first murmurs of Enlightenment reason spread through 
coffeehouses and pamphlets. Even the machines began to stir: Thomas Newcomen’s steam engine 
was built in 1712—a modest contraption pumping water from a mine, yet in it the Industrial Age took 
its first breath. Once again, Neptune’s mist met Aries’ flame, and out of the smoke rose a new vision 
of human power—the capacity to shape the material world through the imagination of the mind.
## Page 52

48
Then came 1861, and with it a thunderous repetition of the same motif on a planetary scale. 
This transit is particularly important, as it also found Uranus in Gemini and Jupiter in Leo—three of 
the five outer planets in the same signs where we find them again in 2026. The American Civil War 
erupted as Neptune entered Aries’ early degrees, a baptism of blood that forced a nation to reconcile 
its ideals with its deeds. In Europe, Garibaldi’s Redshirts marched for Italian unity, and Prussian can-
nons forged the German Empire. Across continents, the principle of nationhood, of collective identity 
born from struggle, seized humanity with martial fervor. The serfs of Russia were emancipated, slav-
ery was abolished in America, and new ideologies of socialism, feminism, and scientific humanism 
challenged the old order. The telegraph stitched oceans together, the Suez Canal joined seas, and the 
United States completed its first transcontinental railroad in 1869, uniting the two coasts. Mendeleev 
dreamed (Neptune) of the periodic table; Pasteur revealed the germ (Aries) theory (Neptune); and the 
descendants of the first practical steam (Neptune) engine (Aries) reshaped the rhythm of daily life as 
the world reached the height of the Second Industrial Revolution. Every realm of existence quick-
ened. It was as if the planet itself inhaled, braced, and charged forward, believing it could master 
destiny. Yet behind the triumphs lay the same Neptunian shadow: illusions of progress, the seductions 
of nationalism, the dream that machinery could redeem humanity. Out of these contradictions rose 
the modern world we still inhabit.
Now, once more, the tide returns. In 2025, Neptune entered Aries, and for the first time in living 
memory the collective imagination is being asked to start anew. We stand at the frontier of crises and 
possibilities that echo those earlier epochs, but on a scale their architects could not have conceived. 
The old Piscean age of faith, media saturation, and global diffusion is dissolving; the new age demands 
action, courage, and embodiment. The wars of religion have been replaced by battles of ideology and 
information, the Copernican revolution by the algorithmic one. Just as Copernicus displaced Earth from 
the center, artificial intelligence may soon displace humanity from the center of cognition. The question 
is not whether this will happen, but how consciously we will shape its unfolding.
Every prior Neptune-in-Aries generation has faced the same paradox: the promise of freedom 
and the peril of zeal. When the ocean (Neptune) enters the forge (Aries), the steam obscures as much 
as it reveals. The sixteenth century’s wars of faith cloaked ambition in piety; the eighteenth century’s 
Enlightenment hid conquest within reason; and the nineteenth century’s nationalism carried liberation 
and domination in the same breath. Our own age is poised between salvation and self-annihilation 
in equally Neptunian fashion. Climate change, the exhaustion of resources, and the digital coloniza-
tion of consciousness expose how thin the boundary has become between dream and delusion. Aries, 
impatient and absolute, demands decision. Neptune blurs every line. Together they create the atmo-
sphere of a holy war of the future—a moral urgency to act on visions that may or may not be true.
Yet from this tension arises the possibility of renaissance. The youth of the world—those born 
into climate anxiety and algorithmic life—may become new spiritual warriors, their rebellion not of 
territory but of meaning. As in 1533, when the word of God shifted from Latin pulpits to vernacu-
lar tongues, knowledge today is democratizing through digital networks. Voices long silenced find 
global amplification. Ideals of equality, ecological stewardship, and collective imagination surge 
across borders—sometimes chaotic, sometimes profound. Neptune in Aries tends to inflame the col-
lective heart; revolutions of conscience, such as the response to the Palestinian genocide, are its 
signature. We may see movements that combine technology with mysticism, activism with artistry—
arising from a generation seeking not escape but embodiment, replacing despair with the courage to 
attempt the impossible.
## Page 53

49
Technologically, the parallels are uncanny. Just as the 1700s cycle birthed the steam engine and 
the 1860s brought the telegraph and industrial expansion, this transit unfolds amid revolutions of 
comparable magnitude. Artificial intelligence, genetic engineering, and renewable energy are today’s 
steam engines—tools that can either liberate or enslave, depending on the ideals guiding them. Aries 
insists on mastery; Neptune reminds us that mastery without meaning is illusion. Humanity’s chal-
lenge in these years is to wield innovation with conscience, to transform invention into stewardship. 
The coming decades will test whether our species has matured enough to fuse technological fire with 
spiritual humility.
Politically, Neptune in Aries coincides with the fragmentation of empires and the birth of new 
alignments. The sixteenth century saw monarchs wrest power from the papacy; the early eighteenth 
redefined the balance of Europe; the nineteenth forged nation-states from feudal ashes. In our time, 
globalization itself is fraying. Supply chains recoil inward, currencies digitize, and regions assert 
sovereignty over distant systems. Aries thrives on independence; Neptune erodes boundaries. Their 
meeting may produce both secession and synthesis—nations dissolving into networks, while net-
works harden into nations. The dream of unity may survive only through a higher form of diversity: 
a federation of consciousness rather than of commerce. Out of turbulence could emerge a new plan-
etary identity, forged not by empire but by shared vulnerability to climate, data, and destiny.
Economically, this cycle reveals a recurring theme: political turbulence exerting a direct impact 
on markets and financial structures, especially at the onset of the ingress. Historical patterns show that 
the first two to three years after Neptune enters Aries consistently mark a period of financial upheaval, 
speculative innovation, inflation, and structural revaluation. In each of the past three ingresses, old 
monetary or political systems broke down, giving rise to new instruments of credit, trade, and state 
power. The years 1533 to 1536 saw a massive reallocation of capital from the Church to private 
hands, resulting in a property boom followed by inflation and currency debasement in England. The 
years 1697 to 1700 brought financial innovation and the rise of public debt markets—initially under 
the newly founded Bank of England, but soon expanding into more speculative ventures such as the 
South Sea and Mississippi Companies, which ultimately led to a financial crash. The period from 
1861 to 1864 introduced fiat currency (the first paper “greenbacks”) and speculative industrial expan-
sion amid global conflict. Gold and silver prices soared, then collapsed as confidence fluctuated.
Each cycle began with dislocation and exuberance, as faith or ideology shifted and old systems or 
currencies broke down, forcing the creation of new instruments of credit and trade. It is worth noting 
that the current Bretton Woods system—with the U.S. dollar as the world’s reserve currency—is cur-
rently in tatters. On one side lies an unsustainable degree of national debt, driven by decades of budget 
deficits in the global North; on the other, the confiscation of approximately $640 billion in Russian 
national reserves frozen in 2022 in response to the invasion of Ukraine. Combined, these forces have 
significantly eroded trust in the system, spurring the global South, led by the BRICS nations, toward 
the Chinese yuan as they attempt to anchor it to gold through the so-called “gold corridor”—a global 
network of vaults facilitating the conversion of U.S. Treasuries into gold. It is also worth noting that 
the Federal Reserve is really going to struggle to retain control over the economy if it faces a market 
crash and high inflation simultaneously. Both scenarios are on the table over the next three years.
The prior cycles were also accompanied by speculative surges, as optimism outran fundamen-
tals and capital chased new “frontiers” (religious reform, colonial expansion, industrial technol-
ogy, or postwar rebuilding). We are currently seeing similar speculation and a potential bubble 
## Page 54

50
forming around technology stocks and AI (see the boom–bust cycle discussed in the Uranus-in-
Gemini section).
History also warns that every birth of vision carries its delirium. The Reformation begot inquisi-
tions; the Enlightenment, colonialism; nationalism, world wars. The next danger may be ideologi-
cal absolutism disguised as moral clarity. Digital tribes already wage crusades across screens; truth 
becomes fluid, belief weaponized. Neptune clouds, Aries polarizes—and together they form a dan-
gerous combination. The task for the wise is to see through both illusions: to act without fanaticism, 
to dream without escape. 
As the transit deepens through the 2030s, we may see breakthroughs in fusion energy, space 
exploration, and consciousness studies. Humanity may extend its reach beyond Earth even as it con-
fronts the limits of its own habitat. The symbolism is clear: the frontier outside mirrors the frontier 
within. The question is not only how far out we can go, but also how far in. Each prior Neptune-in-
Aries era believed it was entering a new world—one that would mark a paradigm shift.
In summary, these are the key recurring patterns I have identified from studying the last three 
transits of Neptune through Aries. Beneath the overarching undertone set by Pluto, Neptune will cast 
the light through which mundane activity will manifest over the next thirteen years:
• 
War and the birth of new orders: Each transit coincided with major conflicts that 
shattered old structures and ushered in new political orders. 
• 
Ideological and spiritual revolution: Every period witnessed a surge of new ideas, 
ideologies, and mass movements that challenged prevailing orthodoxies.
• 
Technological and scientific breakthroughs: Each transit aligned with game-changing 
innovations that expanded humanity’s capabilities and understanding.
• 
Social upheaval and reform: Each period brought intense social stress and 
transformation, as entrenched orders were challenged and new rights or reforms 
emerged.
• 
Financial upheaval, speculative innovation, inflation, and structural revaluation: 
Each cycle began with dislocation and exuberance, as faith or ideology shifted into 
material enterprise, followed by correction and consolidation that defined the next 
economic era.
## Page 55
