The 3-Year Cycle
The cycle that both the 9-year and 6-year cycles share is the 3-year cycle. Last year’s trading plan 
was built around the 3-year cycle trough that was expected between December 2024 and October 
2025. And indeed, it did culminate within this time band on April 7, 2025, at 14,784 in the NASDAQ. 
It was a sharp and quick decline of 27% from the 3-year cycle crest that formed on December 16, 
2024, at 20,205, and satisfied our criteria for a 3-year cycle low. We are now in the third and final 
3-year cycle phase of the greater 9-year cycle. That same 3-year cycle is also the third and final phase 
within the current 6-year cycle. This means the current 3-year cycle is the last intermediate-term 
cycle phase within the current 18-year cycle. 
November 2025 starts the 8th month of the current 3-year cycle. This is a great example of why 
MMA’s “cycles within cycles” principle is so valuable. By tracking and breaking down the intermedi-
ate-term cycles, we can get a detailed read on the long-term cycles and their development and status.
Since 1980, there have been 16 completed 3-year cycles observed in the NASDAQ. In 80% of 
the instances, the 3-year cycle in the NASDAQ has a normal length of 2.6 years or 31 months with 
a normal range of 26–36 months. Thus, the current 3-year cycle is due to bottom next between June 
2027 and April 2028. This overlaps with the time band of the long-term cycles from June 2027 to 
August 2027, making this a high probability time band for the 18-year cycle trough, where most 
cycles overlap (the “hot zone”).
Historically, in 80% of the cases, 3-year cycles have rallied between 10–37 months to their crest 
with an average of 26 months. As of this writing, the current 3-year cycle has been going up for 7 
months from its start in April 2025 and will enter the time band for its crest to form in 3 months (begin-
ning of 2026). By that time, the 6-year cycle will also have entered the time band for its crest. The 9-year 
cycle will enter the time band for its crest in October 2026, but let’s keep in mind that we are expecting 
a short 9-year cycle in which the crest could happen earlier than the historical time band. 
## Page 117

113
The appreciation of 3-year cycles has been between 55%–122% with an average of 99%. Based 
on these studies, the price target for the 3-year cycle crest is 29,600 with a range of 23,050–33,050. 
This falls right within the price target range for the long-term cycle of 21,700–49,400, narrowing 
down that range. The current 3-year cycle has appreciated over 60% so far from its starting low in 
April 2025 and has already entered the target price range. We can conclude that the 3-year cycle crest 
price target range is the one to focus on for the 18-year cycle crest as well.
Once the crest is in, the historical range of decline from the crest to trough in 3-year cycles has been 
1–14 months with an average of 6 months. The historical depreciation has seen a range of 11%–49% 
with an average of 30%. Moreover, from our studies, we know that the last phase of a greater cycle often 
retests the second phase low. In the case of the 9-year cycle, that would be the low of October 2022, 
which, from the current highs, would represent a 55–60% decline. In case of the 6-year cycle, this would 
be the low of April 2025, which, from the current highs, would represent a 35–40% decline.
The 50-Week Cycle
The 3-year cycle in the NASDAQ further breaks down into three 50-week cycles, when it unfolds in 
a 3-phase pattern. Historically, in 80% of the cases, the 50-week cycle has a normal length of 50 weeks 
with a range of 35–65 weeks. If the 50-week cycles are on the longer side, then a 3-year cycle can also 
break down into two 50-week cycles, as in a 2-phase pattern. Another possibility is a breakdown into a 
combination pattern, in which we would see lows at the 1/3 and 1/2 intervals of the greater 3-year cycle.
Measured from its start in October 2022, the previous 3-year cycle broke down in a 3-phase 
pattern with 50-week cycle lows in October 2023, August 2025, and the third and final low in April 
2025. As of this writing in November 2025, the current 50-week cycle, measured from its start in 
April 2025, has progressed 30 weeks. The next 50-week cycle trough is due in March 2026, with a 
range of January 2026 – May 2026, when a 1/6 orb of the normal length is applied. If the orb of 15 
weeks is applied, the 50-week cycle trough range increases from December 2025 to July 2026.
The current 50-week cycle seems to be breaking down in a 3-phase pattern. Currently, we are 
only in the second phase of the 50-week cycle. Historically, in 80% of the cases, 50-week cycles have 
rallied between 22–65 weeks from trough to crest with an average of 43 weeks. Thus, we are already 
in the range for the crest. However, since this is only the first 50-week cycle in a new 3-year cycle 
and the first 50-week cycle usually exhibits bullish characteristics, I expect the crest to form within 
the second or third phase, which would be December 2025 through March 2026. The appreciation 
from trough to crest has historically ranged from 18%–73% with an average of 39%. Measured from 
the starting trough in April 2025, this gives us a price target range of 17,500–25,700 for the current 
50-week cycle, which has also been achieved as of this writing. 
Once the crest is in, in 80% of the cases, 50-week cycles have declined from the crest to the 
trough for 4–38 weeks with an average of 13 weeks. The historical depreciation from the crest to the 
trough ranges from 8%–34% with an average of 18%. Thus, we anticipate an 8%–34% drop in the 
NASDAQ in the first half of 2026.
GEOCOSMIC INDICATORS
During the years 2026 until 2027, there is an abundance of geocosmic signatures happening that 
have relevance for timing market cycles. I will focus on the overlap period of the identified market 
cycle time bands in the previous section.
## Page 118

114
Let’s first look at the critical reversal dates for 2026 that are specific to the NASDAQ. Critical 
Reversal Dates are high-probability market turning points identified through proprietary algorithms 
by Jonathan Jairaj and Wiebke Held, based on the correlation of market and planetary cycles in the 
NASDAQ for the past 40+ years. The methods to derive the CRDs are built upon The Ultimate Book 
on Stock Market Timing Volume 3: Geocosmic Correlations to Trading Cycles, by Raymond Merri-
man, and have been further enhanced to improve prediction accuracy for the NASDAQ. 
CRDs are ranked by correlation strength, with three-star CRDs signifying the highest probability 
for cycle crests or troughs to form. There are six three-star Critical Reversal Dates (CRDs) in 2026 
for the NASDAQ:
	
January 20 (+/– 4 trading days)
	
March 22–25 (+/– 4 trading days)
	
June 15 (+/– 4 trading days)
	
July 20–25 (+/– 4 trading days)
	
September 15–25 (+/– 4 trading days)
	
October 3–November 14 (Venus Retrograde)
Together with the cycles analysis from the previous sections, these CRDs narrow down the 
time bands for when to expect major turning points in the NASDAQ in 2026. As we expect a 
50-week cycle crest and trough in the first half of 2026, watch for the 50-week cycle crest and/or 
trough culminating around the first three CRDs (January 20, March 22–25, June 15). Even though 
it is not my preferred scenario, we must be open to the possibility that the first 50-week cycle crest 
may also be the greater 18-year cycle crest. This would be supported by the following long-term 
geocosmic signatures:

However, should we see a decline that exceeds 34% within this timeframe, then it is a possibility.

has one of the strongest correlations, if not the strongest, to long-term market cycles in the NASDAQ. 
Readers should be aware that the extended time band for the Saturn–Uranus waning semi-square, 
which has three passages in April 2027, October 2027, and January 2028, starts in July 2026 and 
lasts until October 2028. The central time band is from March 2027 until February 2028 and overlaps 
nicely with the hot zone for the 18-year cycle (June–August 2027).
Thus, my bias is that we will not see the 18-year cycle trough in 2026, but rather in 2027, as there

The “Jupiter Effect” (updated by Pouyan Zolfagharnia and calculated by Sergey Trassov) is

mid-Leo. Jupiter will be in the sign of Leo from June 2026 until July 2027, which overlaps with both 
geocosmic cluster zones in 2026 and 2027 and further supports the outlook of a significant crest and 
trough during that time frame.
And then there is also Venus turning retrograde from October 3, 2026, until November 14, 2026. Dur-
ing the last Venus retrograde period from March 2 until April 13, 2025, the previous 3-year cycle crest was 
tested on February 18, which was only 9 trading days prior to Venus turning retrograde. Only two trading 
days before, on March 2, the market broke below the start of the primary cycle and was rendered bearish 
with a final retest of that structural break on March 3, the first trading day after Venus turned retrograde. 
The 3-year cycle trough culminated on April 7, only four trading days prior to Venus turning direct. 
Thus, in 2026, the Venus retrograde period could correlate again with a crest and/or trough of 
significance. If we don’t see the 18-year cycle crest forming within the June CRD, then watch the 
Venus retrograde period or the September 15–25 CRD closely. Another possibility during this period 
is a retest of the highs, if a crest forms around the June CRD.

116
CONCLUSION
In the longer-term picture, 2026 will likely witness the 18–year cycle crest. The price target range 
is 23,050–33,050, or if this is exceeded, up to 49,400 (extreme target). Once the crest is in, the decline 
into the 18-year cycle trough will start. This decline will likely last between 1–31 months or 1–15, 
if we take the narrower time band from the 18-year cycle phases (9- and 6-year cycles). The highest 
probability is for the 18-year cycle trough to occur in 2027 or 2028, with a narrower time band from 
February through August 2027 and a “hot zone” of June through August 2027.
In the intermediate-term picture, a 50-week cycle crest is due in the first quarter of 2026 (if not 
already formed by December 2025) with a price target of 17,500–25,700. This crest will be followed 
by an 8–34% decline in the NASDAQ into the first 50-week cycle low of the current 3-year cycle. 
The time band for this low is December 2025 through July 2026, with a “hot zone” between January 
and May 2026. Watch the January 20, March 22–25, and June 15 CRDs closely during this time, as 
those deliver the highest probability time windows for the 50-week crest and trough to unfold. 
The 50-week cycle trough will be followed by another rally into the second half of 2026 that will 
likely last 22–65 weeks with an appreciation of 18%–73%, forming the crest of the second 50-week 
cycle in the current 3-year cycle. The July 15–25 CRD is the ideal geocosmic backdrop for this to 
happen. The question is whether this crest will exceed the first 50-week cycle crest or not, as at some 
point the 3-year cycle will likely turn bearish and start the decline into the 18-year cycle trough.
My preferred scenario is that the crest of the second 50-week cycle will retest or slightly exceed 
the crest of the first 50-week cycle, forming a double top formation. This would signal that the 
18-year crest is likely to unfold in Q2 or Q3, depending on how the cycle count develops after the 
first 50-week cycle trough.
However, if the second 50-week cycle crest rises clearly above the first crest and prices continue 
trading higher, then the 18-year cycle crest is more likely to occur at the end of the second 50-week 
cycle. In that case, we would expect a retest by the crest of the third 50-week cycle, and an 18-week 
primary cycle crest would be expected later in 2026 (Q3-Q4). In this scenario, pay close attention 
to the September 15–25 CRD and the Venus retrograde period (October 3–November 14) for a sig-
nificant long-term cycle crest. All scenarios will continue to be reviewed and refined in the monthly 
MMA Tech Report. 
These conditions would represent a textbook long-term cycle crest with a classic double top 
formation formed by intermediate-term cycles. However, it is important to remember that the final 
phases of a greater cycle most often distort, and the pattern may not unfold in a perfect textbook man-
ner. We are currently in the final phases of all long-term cycles, so the intermediate-term cycles may 
be shorter or longer than their normal length and range, or can even be skipped completely. 
Therefore, if we observe a decline greater than 34% in the NASDAQ, that would indicate the 
decline into the 18-year cycle trough is likely underway. In that event, traders and investors should 
be prepared to buy the long-term cycle trough of the 18-year cycle. Additionally, any intermediate-
term cycle crest that develops in late 2025 or 2026 should be viewed as an opportunity for traders and 
investors to reduce exposure to the NASDAQ and the broader US stock market in anticipation of the 
decline into the 18-year cycle low.

 GOLD IN 2026
by Wyatt Fellows, MMA Analyst
REVIEW 
What an incredible year for Gold in 2025! At the time of writing last year’s Forecast 2025 book, 
we were in the time band for an intermediate low when it was written, “Gold is due for a second 10.5-
month cycle low by November 2024. The price target for this low could be between $2350–$2575.” 
Indeed, Gold bottomed out on November 14 at 2541.50. It then exploded to an all-time high of $4398 
on October 20. This was above even our most optimistic price target mentioned last year, which was 
$3743 +/- 411. Since peaking, Gold is now in the process of correcting back into a 50-week and 
31-month cycle low that is due ideally by the end of January 2026. If a bottom forms, then all eyes 
will be on whether or not Gold can eclipse that $4398 high in 2026.
Gold Cycles

October 2029–July 2031

16-YEAR CYCLE
Gold likely has a 16-year long-term cycle, which aligns well with the lengths of long-term cycles 
in other financial and commodity markets. However, since we only have two observed instances of 
this cycle (three if you consider 1968 as a viable low, as I do), it will take many more years of data to 
confirm this. Until that happens, we will operate under the assumption that Gold has a 16-year cycle 
with a historical 2-year orb. It last bottomed in December 2015, placing 2026 in the 11th year of the 
current cycle. It is next due to bottom in 2029–2033. As we are past the halfway point of the long-
term cycle, we need to be aware that a crest could form at any moment. It could even have occurred 
at the October 2025 all-time high of $4398, but this is not our current bias.
What is interesting about the $4398 high is that it was very close to an exact doubling of the 
rise from the preceding 16-year cycle. Measuring from the double bottom lows of 1999–2001 to 
the 16-year crest of September 2011, Gold rallied $1667. If we double that amount and add it to the 
December 2015 16-year bottom of $1045, we get $4379. The October high of $4398 is within $20 
of this price target, which means it needs to be given some serious consideration for being a 16-year 
high. Right now, our bias is that Gold will make further gains in 2026 before ultimately peaking out, 
but if Gold experiences a monthly close below $2541 before making a new all-time high, then the top 
for this 16-year cycle is probably in. Until that happens, the next upside price targets for this 16-year 
cycle are $5016 +/- 467, followed by $5410 +/- 515. 
## Page 122

118
THE 7.8-YEAR CYCLE
All cycles typically break down into two or three sub-cycles of approximately equal length. For 
Gold, the 16-year cycle predominantly breaks down into a two-phase pattern of 7.8-year cycles. This 
7.8-year cycle is 94 months long and has a normal range of 84–104 months. Measuring from the start 
of this current 16-year cycle that bottomed in December 2015, we would have expected the first 7.8-
year cycle phase to bottom sometime between December 2022 and August 2024. Instead, it bottomed 
one month early (83rd month) in November 2022 at $1618. We might now consider the new normal 
range of these cycles to be 83–104 months.
January 2026 will begin the 38th month of the second 7.8-year cycle phase measured from the 
November 2022 bottom. It is next due between October 2029 and July 2031 and will coincide with 
the next 16-year cycle low (notice the nice overlap of the time bands for both lows). The crest will 
happen first, and it was stated last year, “There have been seven 7.8-year cycles since 1968, and not 
one has peaked out before the 34th month. This implies that even higher prices for Gold are in store 
for 2025.” This proved to be even more than correct, with Gold surpassing all upside price targets. 
Last year also stated, “If we look at just the second phase 7.8-year cycles, which we are now in, 
these have topped out in the 35th month twice and also in the 41st month of the cycle. This gives us 
a general time period for a crest between October 2025 and April 2026 at the earliest.” So, we have 
another reason to consider that Gold may have formed a long-term top in October 2025, as this was 
the first month of the time band for when we expected a bearish 7.8-year crest to form. If not, then we 
expect a crest to form by April 2026, but it may spill over into May or June.
Gold has already exploded through all of the normal upside price targets given in last year’s 
forecast. If the rally continues, as we suspect, then Fibonacci extension targets for a 7.8-year crest 
may be $5108 and $5352. These overlap nicely with the price targets given for the 16-year crest 
earlier. There is an even higher price target around $6600 using the highest range of historical per-
centage gains of 7.8–year cycles. But the preferred targets would be in the lower measured price 
target ranges just given. Once this 31-month cycle bottoms, we will then be able to narrow down 
possible upside objectives. 
## Page 123

119
INTERMEDIATE TERM CYCLES
Based on the fact that all cycles break down into two or three sub-cycle phases, the 7.8-year 
cycle could break down into either two 47-month cycles or three 31-month cycles. The predominant 
breakdown has been the three-phase pattern, so we are basing the current forecast on the assumption 
that this 7.8-year cycle will break down in this manner.
January 2026 will begin the 38th month of the first 31-month cycle measured off the start of the 
current 7.8-year cycle in November 2022. With a normal range of 24–38 months, it is due to bottom 
by the end of January 2026 (if it hasn’t bottomed already in November or December). However, there 
is always a chance it could expand by a few months. The crest of this first 31-month cycle phase 
topped on October 20 at a price of $4398. This was a 172% gain and it was in line with the historical 
gains of this cycle. When looking at all 31-month cycle phases that immediately follow a 7.8-year 
low, all but one have been bullish (as this one has been), and they only decline for 1–4 months before 
bottoming. This supports the idea that a significant low in Gold should be in by the end of January, 
with an outside chance of it occurring as late as February 2026.
A normal corrective price target for this coming 31-month low would be $2680–$3336. We would 
also like to see the 16-month moving average tested on the decline (currently around $3200 and rising), 
but given that this has been an extremely bullish cycle, Gold may bottom at a higher level than usual. 
At the very least, a 20% decline could be anticipated, which targets $3500 +/- $100. We would 
also prefer to see prices at least test the 16-month moving average, which stands at about $3200 in 
mid-November 2025 and rises about $100/mo. At whatever price the 31-month cycle ultimately bot-
toms, our bias is that new all-time highs are in store for 2026.
The 31-month cycles can break down into two 16-month half cycles (with a range of 13–20 
months) or three 10.5-month cycles with a range of 9–12 months (sometimes expanding up to 14 
months). The 10.5-month cycle can be referred to as a 50-week cycle that carries an 8-week orb. 
Often, we will get a combination of two- and three-phased patterns. However, the current 31-month 
cycle is breaking down as a classic three-phase pattern of three 50-week cycles. The start of the third 
and final 50-week cycle was November 14, 2024, so it is due to bottom by the end of December 2025 
unless it expands by a few weeks, which is a possibility given that the longer 31-month cycle is also 
due to bottom at the end of this current 50-week cycle.
While the above outlines when, and at what price, we think this first 31-month cycle will bottom 
before ultimately continuing higher into 2026, we need to entertain the possibility that this 7.8-year 
cycle might instead display the less frequent two-phased pattern of two 47-month cycles instead. A 
clue that this might be happening is if Gold fails to even reach the 50-week moving average on this 
decline (currently around $3293 in mid-November 2025 and rising about 30/mo.) or fails to decline 
for even a month before making new highs past December. Such a shallow decline could still be a 
50-week cycle low (47-month cycles contain four 50-week cycles and two 23.5-month half cycles), 
but it would mean that Gold would be rallying in the fourth and final 50-week cycle instead of the 
first 50-week cycle in a new 31-month cycle.
Even in this scenario, we are expecting new all-time highs for Gold in 2026. However, if it is a 
47-month cycle crest that is forming early in 2026, then we could also be looking at an extremely 
steep decline in the coming year as well. This is because a 47-month low would then be due February 
2026–June 2027.	
## Page 124

120
GEOCOSMICS
Saturn in aspect to a planet outside of its orbit has proved to be timely in ushering in a major high 
or low in the Gold market. Specifically, at all but one 7.8-year high or low, Saturn has been aspecting 
Uranus, Neptune, or Pluto within a reasonable orb of time around the occurrence. And, at the one 
instance where Saturn wasn’t making an aspect to Uranus, Neptune, or Pluto (March 2008 high), 
Saturn was still involved, as this was when the last instance of Jupiter in a waxing trine to Saturn 
took place. The reason this is so important for the coming year is that we will have Saturn forming 
a waning sextile to Uranus in January 2026, Saturn conjunct Neptune in February 2026, and Saturn 
forming a waxing sextile to Pluto in March 2026. This makes the first half of 2026 a very good time 
for the current 7.8-year cycle to top out.
First up will be Saturn forming a waning sextile to Uranus, taking place on January 19, 2026. It 
will be the third and final pass of this aspect, with the first two having occurred on April 4, 2025, and 
August 11, 2025. What is interesting is that the previous occurrence of this aspect was in 1979–1980 
and occurred in three passes as well. The first was September 16, 1979, and led to a 10.5-month cycle 
crest three weeks later. The second passage on February 17, 1980, was big for Gold. It coincided with 
a 16-year crest four weeks earlier when Gold hit an all-time high of $873 in January 1980. This high 
remained in place for the next 28 years until it was finally surpassed in 2008. The last pass occurred 
on July 4, 1980, and was followed by a primary cycle crest one week later. Based on historical pre-
cedence, it is within reason that we could see the final 50-week and also 31-month cycle low form 
within 4 weeks of January 19, 2026.
We also need to acknowledge the fact that a 16-year cycle high did occur during the central time 
band of this aspect in the past, and did so with price moving in a parabolic-like manner. Something 
similar is occurring this time around with Gold having exploded to a high (so far) on October 20, 
2025. This is also in the central time band of Saturn, forming a waning sextile to Uranus. While our 
bias is for new highs in Gold during 2026, the possibility that another 16-year high could be in by 
January 19, 2026, is certainly plausible too.
As we move into February, Saturn will form a conjunction with Neptune on the World Point of 
0° Aries. Neptune in Aries could usher in another inflationary wave to wash over the markets, which 
could propel commodity markets (like metals) higher. Gold also has shown to like Neptune and per-
forms favorably when aspects involving Neptune are highlighted. Being that the conjunction between 
Saturn and Neptune is the middle of the three big aspects Saturn is forming to outer planets early in 
2026, makes it a favored time to see a 7.8-year crest within 5 months of February 2026. 
It should also be noted that the last time Saturn entered the sign of Aries was in April 1996. A 7.8-
year crest occurred 2 months prior in February of that year. Might something similar happen when 
Saturn re-enters Aries on February 13, 2026? 
In March, Saturn will form a waxing sextile to Pluto on March 28. The last time this aspect was 
in effect was 1989–1990. At that time, there were three passages that took place, with the third one 
coinciding with a somewhat rare 47-month high within 8 days. Recall that a 7.8-year cycle can break 
down into two 47-month cycle phases. This sets a precedent that a phase of the 7.8-year cycle has 
peaked with this aspect in the past, so it’s possible the top of the second 31-month cycle could be 
around April +/- 1 month. 
## Page 125

121
CONCLUSION
Last year’s Forecast 2025 book concluded, “Gold is due for a 31-month cycle crest and trough 
in 2025. Once the crest of the 31-month cycle forms, Gold could fall 10–20% to a 31-month cycle 
low that is due anytime during 2025. Ideally, this low forms in the latter half of the year between July 
2025 and December 2025.” As we close out 2025 and turn the calendar to 2026, Gold is following 
this script. Gold formed its 31-month cycle crest in October and is now immersed in a correction to a 
31-month cycle bottom. This bottom is ideally due by the end of December 2025, but may extend into 
January 2026. The price target for this low is quite wide at $2680–$3336. Being that Gold has been 
so bullish (as it should be in the first phase of a new 7.8-year cycle), Gold may not drop as far as we 
might expect. Therefore, a more bullish price target for a low might be $3300–$3600.
Once the 31-month low forms, we expect Gold to rally to new all-time highs in 2026. Determin-
ing a price target for the next 31-month cycle crest is difficult without knowing exactly where the 
bottom will form, but if it comes in around $3500, Gold could hit $5225 +/- 425 or even $6285 +/- 
550. However, exceeding the October 20 high of $4398 will need to happen first. Gold likes to form 
double tops and double bottoms, so there is certainly a risk that the high for Gold in 2026 occurs not 
far from $4400. This would be the most bearish outcome for Gold in 2026. In either case, one of the 
most likely times for this high to form is February 2026 +/- 5 months.
In the off chance that Gold satisfies the criteria laid out for a 47-month cycle crest forming 
instead in 2026, Gold could see an impressive decline into the second half of the year.

 SILVER IN 2026
by Pouyan Zolfagharnia, MMA Analyst
REVIEW
Silver has rallied nearly 161% from the October 2023 four-year low of 20.85. In last year’s 
Forecast 2025 book, I stated: “There are two key factors that can drive precious metals to rally: high 
inflation and geopolitical risk. With the case of Silver, demand for the application of Silver in modern 
technologies such as solar panels can also boost prices as we head into a world looking for alterna-
tive sources of energy. As described in the earlier chapters, all these themes will be triggered at the 
Aries Vortex (Feb 2026), which could provide the perfect storm for Silver to rally to a new ATH of 
53.06 +/– 5.27.” 
At the time of this writing, Silver has rallied to a new all-time high (ATH) of 54.42 on November 
13, 2025. My bias is that the price target provided in last year’s report will hold, and that we should 
see a sharp decline in the price of Silver as we approach the Saturn–Neptune conjunction, in time 
for the 26-month half-cycle to the final 4-year cycle within the longer-term 9.25-year and 18.5-year 
cycles.

THE 18.5-YEAR CYCLE IN SILVER AND ITS PHASES
The basic long-term cycle in Silver is 18.5 years, with a range of 15–22 years. The previous 
instance of this cycle was the double-bottom low of 1991–1993, when Silver fell to $3.51/ounce 
(February 1991 and February 1993) after its all-time high of $50.00/ounce in January 1980. The 
low of February 1991 occurred 19 years and three months after the prior 18.5-year cycle trough of 
November 1971. The next (and most recent) occurrence of this long-term cycle was in October 2008. 
That was 17 years and eight months later, as Silver fell from its crest of 21.44 in March 2008 to a 
low of 8.40 in October 2008, just as Saturn began its five-passage opposition to Uranus that lasted 
through mid-2010. This decline then led to a retest of the all-time high when Silver soared to 49.82 
in April 2011. The next 18.5-year cycle is therefore due in 2027 +/– 3.5 years. In January 2026, we 
will be entering the 17th year and third month of the current cycle, which places us well within the 
orb of the 18.5-year cycle.
THE 9.25-YEAR HALF-CYCLE
Silver completed a decline to its 9.25-year half-cycle low in March 2020 when it fell to 11.64, a 
drop of nearly 77% from the April 2011 high. That low occurred 11 years and five months into the 
cycle that began in October 2008. The 9.25-year cycles are usually 7–11 years in length. When we 
## Page 127

123
see cases of cyclical expansion, this is usually followed by a cyclical contraction that restores equi-
librium to the larger cycle. I expect the current 9.25-year cycle to contract closer to seven years, due 
in December 2027 +/– 14 months.
THE 6-YEAR CYCLE
The 18.5-year cycle can also break down into three 6-year cycle phases, with a range of 5–7 
years. As shown in the chart above, the first phase was bullish and ended in December 2014 at 14.16, 
which was six years and two months after the 18.5-year cycle commenced. The second phase was 
bearish and ended with the March 2020 low, five years and three months later. This would mean we 
are now in the third and final 6-year cyclical phase, which is expected to complete the longer 18.5-
year cycle in March 2026 +/– 12 months. The overlap with the contracted 9.25-year cycle discussed 
above is October 2026 to March 2027, which is the ideal time for the low.
Therefore, 2026 will begin the 18th year of the longer-term 18.5-year cycle and the sixth year of 
its second 7- to 11-year half-cycle. The 18.5-year cycle low is due anytime in the next four and a half 
years. The 9.25-year cycle low is due over the next four years. These two cycles are most likely to 
bottom in their overlap, which is 2027–2030. This is also around the same time that the stock market 
is due to bottom, correlating with the lunar node transiting through Aquarius and Capricorn. 
On the other hand, we may be commencing the sixth year of the third and final 6-year phase of the 
18.5-year cycle. The overlap range for this outlook would be slightly earlier, in 2025–2027. Therefore, 
2027 appears to be the year in which all the cycles overlap. We also have the conjunction of the lunar 
node and Pluto taking place in that year. The current 18.5-year cycle commenced with the North Node 
in Aquarius. The North Node will once again enter Aquarius from August 2026 until March 2028.
Last year, I noted: “The crest of the second 9.25-year cycle is most likely still forming, as we 
continue to record higher highs. At the time of writing this report, prices reached 35.07 in October 
2024. It is also possible that we are in the third and final 6-year phase. We know that these cycles can 
be very explosive. Therefore, it remains unclear whether we can take out the 18.5-year [cycle] crest, 
which was 49.82 in April 2011. If we do, the nominal price target would be 53.06 +/- 5.27.” 
## Page 128

124
We have now satisfied this price target, and if the high of 54.42 holds, I would expect a sharp 
decline in Silver, as we are late in the longer-term cycles. Silver is far more volatile than Gold, and it 
tends to spike up and fall back down very quickly. Silver is currently leading the rally, along with a 
case of bearish intermarket divergence: Gold formed its crest in October, while Silver has just made a 
new ATH. This is suggestive of long-term crest formation. This is also accompanied by bearish oscil-
lator divergence in the CCI in the daily, weekly, and monthly time frames. 
As there is a chance that the 18.5-year cycle trough may form next year, there is a likelihood that 
the long-term crest may have formed at 54.42 or may form very soon within the price target of 
53.06 +/– 5.27. If the crest has formed at 54.42, the Fibonacci price target for the 18.5-year cycle 
trough is 31.41 +/– 5.43. The mid-cycle pause price target suggests a steeper decline to 16.24 +/– 
4.51, which would be a decline of roughly 70%. Historical precedence from the prior two instances 
of the 18.5-year cycle—since Silver began trading on the open market in the 1970s—has shown 
declines of 93% and 61% from the crest. While we do not have sufficient data to draw from, the 
second decline was within range of a 61.8% Fibonacci correction. Therefore, I would look to start 
building long-term positions in the 26.00–31.50 range, while also noting strong support in the 
34.50–35.70 and 28.70–31.10 regions. Please note that if the high of 54.42 is taken out, it will 
invalidate these targets.
The broader outlook, marked by the risks of inflation and ongoing geopolitical tensions, offers 
little support for a pronounced decline in Silver prices. Yet it is important to remember that Silver has 
historically entered bearish phases during periods of financial upheaval. The troughs witnessed dur-
ing the 2008 financial crisis and the 2020 pandemic lockdown serve as clear examples. Consequently, 
it is plausible that a more extensive financial crisis will ultimately underpin the long-term bearish 
trend that culminates in the 18.5-year cycle trough.
THE INTERMEDIATE-TERM CYCLES REVISITED
The 18.5-year cycle will either break down into two 9.25-year half-cycles, three 6-year phases, or 
a combination of the two. From the low of October 2008, the first 9.25-year cycle formed in March 
2020, 11 years and five months into the cycle. The first 9.25-year phases of the prior two 18.5-year 
cycles were also longer in length and were followed by shorter second-phase cycles. They were 
both just under 11 years in length in the first phase and were followed by shorter 7- to 9-year cycles. 
Therefore, if the next 9.25-year cycle is also shorter, it will be due in December 2027 +/– 14 months, 
as described above.
The 9.25-year cycle tends to break down into the 4-year half-cycle (48-month cycle), as well as 
a 26-month (111-week) half-cycle, which is also often exhibited. Therefore, we are in the final 4-year 
phase of the greater 9.25-year and 18.5-year cycles, which commenced in October 2023 at 20.85. 
At the time of writing in early November 2025, we are in the 25th month of the new 26-month 
cycle, which has turned parabolic. The 26-month half-cycle within the greater 4-year cycle has a 
range of July 2025 to May 2026. It is likely to form within a three-month orb of the Saturn–Neptune 
conjunction, testing the 56-week moving average. If the high of 54.42 holds as the 26-month cycle 
crest, the price target for the trough is 37.64 +/– 3.97. Therefore, my bias is that the 26-month cycle 
trough has not formed as of this writing. Once it does, I expect a corrective rally, but my bias is that 
it will not take out the high that is forming in November 2025. 
## Page 129

125
While we are clearly in a bullish 4-year cycle and still have the second phase of this cycle to play 
out, I would expect the final 26-month cycle to turn bearish as we approach the end of the longer-term 
18.5-year cycle. It is worth pointing out that shorter cycles are susceptible to distortions (contraction 
or expansion) when a longer-term cycle is forming. Therefore, be prepared to start building long 
positions if we begin hitting the 18.5-year cycle price targets before entering the normal range for the 
26-month cycle. 
GEOCOSMICS
The Moon’s North Node has a correlation with forming highs as it transits Aries–Pisces, followed 
by a sharp decline as it transits Aquarius. It began its transit of Aries in July 2023 and will complete 
its transit of Pisces in August 2026. Therefore, the long-term cycle trough is likely to form as the 
Node transits Aquarius from August 2026 until March 2028. Note that this period overlaps with the 
refined date range for the contracted 9.25-year and 18.5-year cycle lows of December 2027 +/– 14 
months. The refined date range is October 2026–March 2028.
As noted last year: “Jupiter, the planet of growth and expansion, will be transiting Cancer, the 
sign associated with Silver, from June 6, 2025, to June 30, 2026. This transit could provide a cata-
lyst for the 9.25-year [cycle] crest or even a new ATH.” I think we are now seeing the full impact 
of this transit, and by the time we approach the Saturn–Neptune conjunction in February 2026 and 
the Jupiter–Pluto opposition in July 2026, Silver is likely to come under bearish pressure. Perhaps 
the 26-month cycle trough will form within the orb of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction, and the cor-
rective rally will unfold under the Jupiter–Pluto opposition, before a major sell-off. However, both 
signatures have historically been bearish for Silver, so perhaps we will get a sharp sell-off into the 
midpoint around April–May. 
A shorter-term astrological correlation to note is the transit of Venus. This signature applies only 
to short-term aggressive trading of the major cycles or phases within the primary cycle. We look for a 
trading-cycle trough to form when Venus is in Libra, which is typically followed by a 15.8% rally as 
## Page 130

126
Venus enters Scorpio. We also look for a trading cycle crest to form when Venus is in Pisces–Aries, 
followed by a 17.8% decline as Venus transits Taurus. 
Venus’s next transit of Pisces and Aries will occur from February 10 to March 30, 2026. Venus’s 
next transit of Libra will take place from August 6 to December 4, 2026 (longer than prior transits, as 
Venus will turn retrograde in Scorpio on October 3 and then station direct in Libra on November 14). 
The Venus retrograde will make it difficult to trade the Libra–Scorpio transit. The last time this occurred 
was in 2018, when Silver made a trough on both transits of Libra. It is also worth noting that the Novem-
ber 14 direct station will coincide with Mercury’s direct station. This also happened in April 2025 and 
resulted in a sharp sell-off and reversal, so we may see a similar pattern in November 2026.
CONCLUSIONS
Last year’s Forecast 2025 book concluded: “The technical and fundamental picture remains 
strong for Silver, which could even record a new ATH at 53.06 +/– 5.27 within 3 months of the Sat-
urn–Neptune conjunction on February 20, 2026, before a sharp sell-off into 2027. As we saw in the 
previous 18.5-year cycle, the crest formed in March 2008, and the cycle culminated 7 months later in 
October after a 61% decline.” At the time of writing this report, Silver has just formed a new ATH 
on November 13 at 54.42. If this were not the 18.5-year cycle crest, I would expect it to form soon 
within the price target provided, and for it to be followed by a sharp move down. 
Of course, we never see a straight move down, and there is an intermediate 26-month cycle low 
due, from which I expect a corrective rally. While it is not my bias, Silver is very volatile, and we may 
see the rally retest the high currently being formed. The final phase of the 18.5-year cycle has turned 
parabolic, so I cannot completely rule this scenario out. However, since we are in the final 26-month, 
4-year, and 9.25-year phases of the 18.5-year cycle, the greater probability is that we will see only a 
corrective rally with left translation, as the 26-month cycle turns bearish into 2026–2027.
Therefore, the price target for the 26-month cycle trough is 37.64 +/– 3.97, and it should form 
between July 2025 and May 2026. Once the trough has formed, I would expect a 38.2% to 61.8% 
rally to the 26-month cycle crest two to five months later. I cannot provide a price target for this 
rally until the 26-month cycle trough has formed. From there, I would expect a two- or three-phased 
decline into the 18.5-year cycle trough at either 31.41 +/– 5.43 or a more severe decline toward 16.24 
+/– 4.51 at any point over the next three years.

 T-NOTES LINING UP FOR A 6-YEAR CYCLE CREST IN 2026
by Gianni Di Poce, MMA Analyst
T-Notes Cycles
Start/Progress as of 1/1/26
Next Due
18-year
October 2018, 8 years
2033–2039
6-year
October 2023, 3 years
2028–2030
29-month
October 2023, 27 months
August 2025–October 2026
50-week
January 2025, 51 weeks
October 2025–April 2026
REVIEW
T-Notes hit their lows of the year early in 2025, on January 13 at 107/06. This was a 50-week 
cycle low and set the stage for rising prices for the remainder of the year. The low was also significant 
because it confirmed the October 2023 low at 105/15.5 as the 6-year cycle bottom. As of this writing 
in November 2025, T-Notes are making new highs for the year above 114/00. However, prices have 
not taken out the 2024 high of 115/23.5 from September of that year. Thus, 2025 could turn out to be 
an “inside year” for T-Notes, in which the previous year’s high and low are not surpassed.
The conclusion section of Forecast 2025 stated, “Our preferred outlook for 2025 is centered 
around a 6-year cycle trough being complete in October 2023. The 6-year cycle is still in its first 
29-month phase, but since the greater 18-year cycle has turned bearish, there is a strong chance 
that the rally in T-Notes from the October 2023 low ends this year. Although T-Notes satisfied the 
upside target for 2024 in the 114/25–116/20 range by rallying as high as 115/23.5 on September 11, 
the duration of the rally was not long enough to qualify as a 6-year cycle crest. The sell-off that fol-
lowed from this September 11 crest is due to the 9–15 month cycle coming due, and it calls for a low 
no later than January 2025. This scenario would obviously be nullified if prices took out their low 
from October 2023 at 105/10.5… Assuming T-Notes are in a newer 6-year cycle from October 2023, 
another retest of the 114/25–116/20 range is in the cards for 2025. But it’s also possible that high is 
exceeded, and that T-Notes could rally as high as 122/00–124/00 in that time band between April and 
October 2025. In fact, this upside target is supported by previous rallies in 6-year cycles. However, 
it’s worth noting that most of the historical instances of rallies in 6-year cycles occurred during the 
secular bull market in T-Notes from 1982 to 2020. Thus, the historical cases may not prove to be as 
accurate as they once were, since T-Notes are in a long-term bear market now per the 18-year cycle 
turning bearish.” 
T-Notes still have not tested the 114/25–116/20 range, which is what I want to see before a 6-year 
cycle crest is complete. This means there could be higher prices or lower interest rates in 2026 before 
a continuation of the bearish 18-year cycle takes hold.
The Federal Reserve also paused its rate cuts from December 2024 to September 2025. The 
central bank has resumed its rate cuts, and the market currently expects additional easing to continue 
well into 2026. This provides a macroeconomic backdrop for T-Notes to continue rallying, at least 
until inflationary pressures begin to increase again. Remember that rate cuts mean money printing, 
## Page 132

128
and, at some point, the return of inflation will coincide with another long-term cycle crest in T-Notes. 
Inflation typically leads to higher interest rates, and T-Note prices move inversely to interest rates. In 
other words, inflation is bearish for T-Notes.
THE 18-YEAR CYCLE
2026 marks the eighth year of the 18-year cycle in T-Notes, measured from the October 2018 low 
at 117/13. This long-term cycle typically lasts 15–21 years, so we are not looking for a trough until 
2033–2039, unless there is a case of cyclical contraction. This also implies that interest rates would 
continue to climb for the next 7–13 years at least. 
This is a bearish 18-year cycle because prices took out the low that began the cycle in October 
2018. Additionally, the crest was formed in March 2020, which was only the second year of the cycle. 
When cycle crests occur in the first half of a cycle, the cycle is considered bearish. We expect the low-
est price of the cycle to occur at its end. This bearish 18-year cycle continues to hang over the T-Note 
market and points to additional inflation problems until the long-term cycle bottoms. 
THE 6-YEAR CYCLE
The 18-year cycle breaks down into three 6-year cycles. The newer 6-year cycle scenario was 
confirmed in 2025, as prices never broke below the October 2023 low, and we are now beyond the 
5- to 7-year orb from the October 2018 long-term cycle low. Thus, 2026 will begin the third year of 
the second 6-year cycle phase within the greater 18-year cycle, which is bearish. 
This 6-year cycle is the most important one for 2026 because the odds favor a 6-year cycle crest 
forming this year—especially if it did not already occur in September 2024. My bias is that the 6-year 
cycle crest is not complete yet, because the September 2024 high occurred only 11 months after the 
October 2023 low. Although a bearish 6-year cycle is expected overall, a bullish first phase of the 
cycle is still anticipated. More on this in the next section.
Forecast 2025 stated, “Prices didn’t quite reach our upside objective for a 6-year cycle crest, 
which supports the idea that new highs could yet be on the horizon for 2025. Not to mention, the 
## Page 133

129
historical length of rallies for 6-year cycles in T-Notes has always lasted at least 18 months. This 
means that if October 2023 was truly the 6-year cycle trough, we wouldn’t look for the 6-year cycle 
crest before April 2025. Plus, the phase breakdown of the 6-year cycle suggests that there is still time 
left in this rally in T-Notes, assuming it is a newer 6-year cycle.” 
This supports the idea that a 6-year cycle crest will form in 2026. Remember that bearish cycles 
spend more time declining than advancing, so a 6-year cycle crest beyond 2026 would not align with 
a bearish 6-year cycle. The next 6-year cycle trough is not expected until 2028–2030, so the antici-
pated crest this year sets T-Notes up for another multi-year decline. New lows beneath the October 
2023 low at 105/10.5 are also anticipated for this cycle’s bottom.
THE 29-MONTH CYCLE
The 6-year cycle then breaks down into two or three 29-month cycles. The duration of the 6-year 
cycle determines whether there will be two or three 29-month cycle phases. Most 29-month cycles last 
between 22 and 36 months, and since January 2026 begins the 27th month from October 2023, T-Notes 
are already within the time band for a 29-month cycle trough. It is only the crest that still needs to be 
confirmed. Based on historical metrics, the 29-month cycle low is expected no later than October 2026.
With the 6-year cycle bottom in October 2023, the 29-month cycle was reset as well. Forecast 
2025 stated, “T-Notes are still in their first 29-month phase within the 6-year cycle, and as a rule, the 
first phase of every cycle is bullish. Historically, the majority of 29-month cycles have rallied for at 
least 9–27 months. The September 11, 2024, high would fall into this range for a 29-month cycle high, 
although it would be a bit early from a 6-year cycle standpoint, and, as a rule, the longer-term cycles 
overpower the shorter ones. Plus, given that the first phases are usually bullish, it would be prefer-
able to see it rally at least past the halfway mark of the cycle, say 15–16 months. This would call for 
a high as soon as January or February 2025, but, given the current technical picture of T-Notes, it is 
rather unrealistic. Thus, it would still be ideal for T-Notes to rally into April 2025 or beyond from a 
29-month cycle standpoint.” 
T-Notes never hit a new 29-month cycle high in 2025, although prices are not far from exceeding 
the September 2024 crest at 115/23.5. There is still enough time in the 29-month cycle for new highs 
in 2026, although this supports the idea of a crest forming in the first half of the year.
The 29-month cycle crest is lining up to coincide with the greater 6-year cycle crest. To narrow 
down the timeframe for a high even further, the 29-month cycle is broken down into two or three 
50-week cycles that typically last 9–15 months. T-Notes began 2025 with a 50-week cycle trough on 
January 13, 2025, at 107/06. In theory, a 50-week cycle low could unfold before the start of 2026, but 
if not, then the cycle bottom would be expected no later than April 2026, as the beginning of the year 
corresponds to the 51st week, or 12th month, of this cycle. 
T-Notes are still in the second 50-week cycle phase within the greater 29-month cycle. In theory, 
a third phase could unfold in 2026 that aligns with the greater 29-month and 6-year cycle crests. This 
is a wild card for the cycle scenarios in T-Notes going into 2026.	
GEOCOSMICS
As of this writing in November 2025, the high for T-Notes occurred near several key outer-plan-
etary aspects in April. However, there is still a chance that new highs could form before the calendar 
year ends. Forecast 2025 stated, “Looking ahead into 2025, the most notable observation to be had 
## Page 134

130
is a sign change of every outer planet within the year. Of course, Pluto will already be in Aquarius 
for good, but we’ll see Jupiter ingress into Cancer on June 9, Saturn ingress into Aries on May 24, 
Uranus ingress into Gemini on July 7, and Neptune ingress into Aries on March 30”. 
The analysis went on to state, “But it goes even further than these outer-planetary ingresses. Aside 
from the Jupiter–Saturn square and a square between Jupiter and Neptune on June 18, there are a 
few soft aspects between outer planets that could actually signal comfort, even if temporary, for the 
economy. Saturn is in sextile with Uranus on April 4 and August 11, while Uranus is in sextile with 
Neptune on August 28 and November 20. Interestingly, each of these sextile signatures occurs with the 
respective planets in different signs. The April 4 sextile between Saturn and Uranus will have Saturn 
in Pisces and Uranus in Taurus, while the August 11 sextile will have Saturn in Aries and Uranus in 
Gemini. The August 28 sextile between Uranus and Neptune has Uranus in Gemini and Neptune in 
Aries, but the November 20 sextile has Uranus in Taurus and Neptune in Pisces. This happens because 
of the retrograde motions that are going to take all of these outer planets back into their previous signs, 
except Jupiter and Pluto. Saturn retrogrades back into Pisces on September 1, Uranus retrogrades back 
into Taurus on November 7, and Neptune retrogrades back into Pisces on October 22.” 
It was actually near the sextile between Saturn and Uranus on April 4 that T-Notes completed their 
high of the year. There was also the Jupiter–Saturn square, whose central time band was in effect until 
June 2025. The second of three passages occurred on December 24, 2024, just a couple of weeks before 
the low of the year in T-Notes. It is not my view, however, that either of these highs or lows represented 
significant long-term cycle crests. The January 2025 low was, however, a 50-week trough.
From an outer-planetary standpoint, 2026 is the sequel year to the initial ingresses that occurred in 
2025. Pluto has already been in Aquarius, but 2026 will see Saturn definitively ingress into Aries for 2.5 
years on February 13, Uranus definitively ingresses into Gemini for 7 years on April 25, and Neptune 
ingresses into Aries for 14 years on January 26. Interestingly, 2026 begins with another sextile between 
Saturn and Uranus on January 20. This is the same aspect that coincided with the 50-week bottom in Janu-
ary 2025. It cannot be ruled out that another 50-week cycle trough occurs in either January or February, 
but the primary geocosmic focus for 2026 surrounds the timing of a potential 6-year cycle crest in T-Notes.
Based on the cycle counts discussed in the previous section, the timing for a 6-year cycle crest 
appears to favor the first or second quarter of 2026. It is worth noting that all of the outer-planetary 
ingresses will take place in the first half of 2026, including Jupiter’s ingress into Leo on June 30. 
Outer-planetary ingresses tend to correspond with larger psychological shifts among market partici-
pants, which aligns well with the prospect of a long-term cycle crest in T-Notes. 
There is also a sextile between Saturn and Pluto on March 28. Although sextiles are usually not 
the preferred aspect for marking long-term market reversals, this one could be especially important 
because of the Saturn–Pluto synodic cycle. Remember that the long-term bull market in bonds began 
roughly one year before the Saturn–Pluto conjunction of 1982 and then ended within two months of 
the Saturn–Pluto conjunction of January 2020.
However, there are three outer-planetary aspects taking place in July 2026 that are shaping up 
to be very important for the bond market. The first is the Uranus–Pluto trine on July 18. Then, two 
days later, on July 20, there is an opposition between Jupiter and Pluto. That same day, there is also a 
trine between Jupiter and Neptune. The Uranus–Pluto trine will kick off the central time band of this 
signature, which will remain in effect until May 2028. 
## Page 135

131
The Uranus–Pluto synodic cycle is important for T-Notes as well, because the square signature 
between 2012 and 2015 coincided with “QE-3” from the Fed. Now that another signature is coming 
into effect, could the central bank initiate a new form of unconventional monetary policy? For this to 
occur, some sort of crisis in the bond market would likely need to play out, and, naturally, a long-term 
cycle crest would have to form. Uranus rules innovation, and Pluto rules debt. But both Jupiter and 
Neptune—planets that rule inflation—are involved here as well. Let’s not forget that Neptune in fire 
signs has historically been inflationary, too. 
The combination of the trine between Jupiter and Neptune and the opposition between Jupiter 
and Pluto increases the probability of a massive expansion in inflation expectations. This would be 
bearish for T-Notes and would lead to a rise in interest rates.
But the wild card in this case is the Uranus–Pluto trine. Although it is not my bias that the Fed 
would intervene to stop a rise in interest rates this early in the 6-year cycle, at some point the central 
bank could step in with a surprising program—likely in the form of yield curve control—to stem the 
rise in interest rates. Uranus trine Pluto is the ideal aspect for such an intervention to occur, and it is 
my expectation that this will happen during the central time band between July 2026 and May 2028. 
It is not my view that it will occur in 2026, although it may be possible toward the end of the year if 
inflationary pressures get out of control too quickly.
It is also important to tie in some transits to the Federal Reserve’s natal chart for clues in the 
T-Note market. The natal chart used for this analysis is set for December 23, 1913, at 6:02 p.m. in the 
Capitol Building in Washington, D.C. Forecast 2025 stated, “Note that the third and final Jupiter–
Saturn square will hit the Fed’s natal Pluto at zero degrees Cancer. Jupiter will be conjunct Pluto, 
while Saturn is square Pluto. Pluto is known as the “Four D Planet” (debts, downgrades, defaults, 
and deficits), and it rules debt, so it’s obviously a very important planet for an entity that determines 
the price of that debt via interest rates. Jupiter conjunct Pluto could be one of two things. It could 
signal continued easing on behalf of the Fed, since Jupiter has an affinity towards growth, but it 
could also mean an oversupply of debt. In this scenario, the Fed may actually have to slow down on 
interest rate cuts.” 
Interestingly, the Fed did pause in its rate cuts, but it occurred after the second Jupiter–Saturn 
square rather than the final one in June 2025, when Jupiter was on the Fed’s natal Pluto. The Fed then 
resumed rate cuts with Jupiter near its ascendant in September 2025. Due to Jupiter’s retrograde, two 
more conjunctions will take place to the Fed’s ascendant in Cancer: the first on January 25, 2026, and 
the second on April 24, 2026. 
My view is that rate cuts will continue beyond April 24, at least into Jupiter’s opposition to 
the Fed’s natal Uranus at 5 degrees Aquarius. This will occur after Jupiter ingresses into Leo, and 
it will unfold around the same time that transiting Pluto comes within orb of a conjunction to the 
Fed’s natal Uranus.
This combination of planetary aspects seems to be setting up a showdown over control of the 
Fed. The natal Uranus in Aquarius represents the central bank’s strong sense of independence, and 
it looks to be coming under a rather dramatic (Jupiter) attempt at coercion (Pluto) beginning in the 
second half of 2026. It is worth noting that Jerome Powell’s term as Fed Chair is set to end in May 
2026 as well, although he is scheduled to stay on as a governor until 2028. 
## Page 136

132
This geocosmic setup may also involve Scott Bessent’s natal Saturn at six degrees of Aquarius 
(born August 21, 1962; birth time unknown), which is conjunct the Federal Reserve’s natal Uranus. 
Combined with transiting Pluto conjunct the Fed’s natal Uranus, this suggests that the Treasury Sec-
retary could begin to have a major influence on the Fed’s policy decisions. There have already been 
rumors of Bessent being appointed Fed Chair, but the current law prohibits one person from holding 
both positions at the same time. Regardless, the central bank’s independence appears to be under real 
threat in 2026—and it does not end with these aspects, either.
The conjunction between Saturn and Neptune on February 20, 2026, at zero degrees Aries will 
be conjunct the central bank’s midheaven and square its Sun. This spells an identity crisis and raises 
questions surrounding its authority. Authoritative deception is in play here, potentially arising from 
faulty data being sent its way, which could undermine its policy decisions. This already happened in 
2025, when more than 900,000 jobs magically disappeared, and the Fed realized it was behind the 
curve on cutting rates. Something similar could occur in 2026, but perhaps involving understated 
inflation data that encourages the central bank to continue cutting rates.
CONCLUSION
T-Notes are shaping up for additional upside in 2026 now that the newer 6-year cycle scenario 
from October 2023 has been confirmed. My preferred outlook is for prices to rally into a 6-year cycle 
crest in the 121/00–123/00 range sometime between April and August 2026. Keep in mind that this 
will coincide with a 29-month cycle crest as well. The big question is whether another 50-week cycle 
will begin before the 29-month cycle tops out, as there can be two or three 50-week cycles within a 
29-month cycle, depending on the cycle’s length. 
The highs from 2025, 2024, and 2023 are expected to be exceeded in 2026. Since a 29-month 
cycle trough is due by October, the 6-year cycle crest is not likely to produce an immediate sharp 
pullback. This means that at some point, there will be a strong, tradable bounce in T-Notes in 2026. 
However, a significant secondary lower high beneath the high of the year is a potential scenario in 
the fourth quarter of 2026. 
The geocosmics that begin in 2026—especially the Uranus–Pluto trine—point to a managed-
style decline in the T-Note prices over the coming years. Keep in mind that the time band for a 6-year 
cycle trough begins in 2028 and that the central time band of the Uranus–Pluto trine lasts into May 
2028. Since the greater 18-year cycle is bearish, we expect the 6-year cycle phase to record its lowest 
price at the end of its cycle. This means a drop to 105/00–105/10 should be in order, but that is not in 
the cards for 2026, unless we see an expanded 5- to 7-year cycle that takes prices to new lows. This 
is not our bias, however.
Instead, my preferred scenario is to see T-Notes form a 50-week cycle crest in the 114/25–116/20 
range sometime in January or February, followed by a 50-week cycle trough in February or March. 
Then prices would commence another rally into a 29-month and 6-year crest by August. The target 
is as high as 121/00–123/00. A drop into a 29-month cycle low could then occur, with prices falling 
back into the 114/25–116/20 zone. After that, another rally can occur into year-end, but it will not 
take out the 6-year cycle crest. My expectation is for the 29-month cycle that follows the current one 
to be bearish.
## Page 137

133
The threat against the Fed’s independence may not actually work out as intended. In theory, the 
attempted takeover may begin very late in 2026, after rising rates and inflation start to become a 
problem again. The objective appears to be to artificially peg interest rates below the prevailing rate 
of inflation in order to devalue the debt. Structural issues in the bond market could easily continue 
into the mid-2030s, which lines up with an 18-year cycle bottom. There will also be an opposition 
between Saturn and Pluto around that time, and Neptune will be in the later degrees of Aries. All in 
all, this is a bond market that continues to price in default risk and inflation risk—mainly from gov-
ernments versus private corporations, which may actually prove to offer a safer haven compared with 
government bonds going forward.

 CURRENCY MARKETS IN 2026
Currency markets were very active in 2025. The U.S. Dollar was weak, while the star performer 
was the Swiss Franc. Everyone wanted the safety of the neutral Swiss Franc, even though its central 
bank cut its interest rate to 0% to stop its appreciation. 
The decline in the U.S. Dollar reflected the historical pattern of previous incoming Republican 
administrations in the White House. A lower dollar benefits international trade for U.S. corporations, 
which is also a reason why the Swiss central bank didn’t want its currency to appreciate so much. 
Japan was another reality altogether, as will be discussed in the chapters to follow.

 THE U.S. DOLLAR INDEX (DXY)
by Ulric Aspegren, MMA Analyst
REVIEW  
In mid-November 2024, when the previous yearly U.S. Dollar report was completed, the green-
back was rising from the September 27, 2024, low at 100.15 USD (9). Last year’s Forecast 2025 
book detailed: “The hard nut to crack question is: did the greater cycle that started in 2008 (4) end in 
2021(8) after 12.8 years, or are we 16.6 years into an older 16-year greater cycle that also originated 
in 2008? The former could set up a long-term bullish run for the U.S. Dollar Index, while the latter 
would be very bearish for the greenback, as the 16-year cycle would be ripe to head lower into its 
greater cycle abyss.”
Looking back on the last twelve months, the Dollar succeeded in ascending a respectable 10% 
from the September 2024 low (9) to 110.17 on January 13, 2025 (I), but then ran completely out of 
steam. So far, a total descent of 12.7% for nine long months has followed, resulting in a low on Sep-
tember 17 at 96.21 (10). The greenback has managed to regain 4.30%, reaching 100.36 on November 
5. Could the September 2025 low have been the long-term cycle bottom for the U.S. Dollar Index, or 
is there more bearishness to come? The DXY closed on November 14, 2025, at 99.299 USD.
Preferred Cycle (Start)

THE LONG-TERM CYCLES IN THE U.S. DOLLAR INDEX
As of this writing in mid-November 2025, it is still a challenge to etch out the long-term outlook. 
We got a greater cycle start at the 2008 low (4), at 70.70. If this cycle is still operational, then we are 
17.6 years into it and heading south towards its greater cycle bottom. Historically, this is clearly longer 
than the two previous 13.9- and 15.5-year cycles, which could mean that the Dollar is instead 4 years 
and change into a new, greater cycle that commenced in January 2021, at 89.20 (8). If this is true, then 
the greenback is on a long-term bullish path, on the way towards a greater cycle crest, expected in about 
three years’ time. However, as we only have two samples to compare with, we just cannot forge a reli-
able long-term outlook with such a small sample size. We have to search elsewhere for clues.
THE POLITICAL CYCLE IN THE U.S. DOLLAR
The previous Forecast 2025 book stated: “Under a Democrat administration, the Dollar tends 
to rally into the 16-year cycle crest. Under a Republican, it tends to fall into the 16-year cycle low. 
Hence, the political cycle in the U.S. Dollar does not correspond with a greater cycle trough in 2021 
(8), as the Democrats were in the White House. However, the political cycle does align with a 16-year 
greater cycle crest established in 2022 (H), since the Democrats were still in control of the presi-
dency. Now that the Republicans have overtaken the Oval Office, it would indicate, according to the 
political cycle, that the U.S. Dollar Index is heading towards a 16-year cycle trough. My preferred 
outlook is therefore bearish.” 
## Page 140

136
THE 5.2-YEAR LONG-TERM CYCLE IN THE U.S. DOLLAR
The 16-year cycle splits in the bearish long-term scenario into three 5.2-year cycles. The prices 
are here 4.8 years into the third 5.2-year cycle, which started on January 6, 2021, at 89.20 (8). Both 
the final 5.2-year and the 16-year cycle crests were established together on September 28, 2022, at 
114.78 (H). Time-wise, the future 5.2-year cycle low, which should coincide with the 16-year cycle 
trough, is projected to unfold sometime between March 2025 and March 2027 with its one-year orb. 
Hence, we are now within the bottoming time frame for the long-term cycle trough.
As the expectation is that this final 5.2-year cycle should be bearish, we will use its historical 
bearish price declines to estimate the price target for its forthcoming long-term cycle low. The histori-
cal bearish descents from the previous 5.2-year cycle crests are between 25–48% (using 75% of the 
cases), producing a price target span of 60–87 USD. We will use this span as the overall price target 
range for the 16-year cycle trough.
Consequently, the September 17, 2025, low, at 96.21 (10), appears to be too shallow for a greater 
cycle low. Hence, my bias is that the greenback will continue lower. 
U.S. DOLLAR INDEX Preferred Monthly Chart, as of November 14, 2025
THE 36-MONTH LONG-TERM CYCLE IN THE U.S. DOLLAR
The 5.2-year cycle breaks down most of the time into two 36-month cycles. We are now 28 
months into the second 36-month cycle that started on July 14, 2023, at 99.58 (9). The crest of the 
current 36-month cycle did occur on January 30, 2025, at 110.17 (I). This second 36-month cycle, 
with its 6-month orb, is due to bottom out sometime between January 2026 and January 2027. As this 
final 36-month cycle is anticipated to end simultaneously with the completion of the current 5.2-year 
cycle, we can, via overlapping, concentrate the timing for the forthcoming 16-year cycle trough, to 
January 2026–January 2027 as well.
Historically, prices have dropped 19–23% when the 36-month cycles have been bearish. We can 
therefore estimate the price target range for the upcoming bearish 36-month cycle low to 84–89 USD. 
Hence, by overlapping with the overall price target for the 16-year cycle low, we obtain an 84–87 
USD span as one price area where the upcoming long-term cycle low could occur.
## Page 141

137
Once the 16-year cycle trough has bottomed out, prices are expected to rise to a bullish 36-month 
cycle crest, forecasted to take place after 16 to 32 months, at an increase of 16–29%. 
THE 14-MONTH INTERMEDIATE-TERM CYCLE IN THE U.S. DOLLAR INDEX
The 36-month long-term cycle can be split into either three 45-week (10-month) cycles or two 
14-month cycles, or a combination of both. The best fit at this time is that the first 14-month interme-
diate-term cycle was completed on September 27, 2024, at 100.15, as it was 14 months away from 
the July 2023 low.
The current 36-month cycle should thus be in its second and final 14-month cycle. Last year’s 
report stated: “As we are in a bearish long-term scenario, the expectation is that this second 14-month 
cycle should peak out 1.4 to 3.7 months after the September 2024 low. The bearish historical crest 
data generate a time target range of November 8, 2024–January 17, 2025, for the forthcoming 
14-month cycle top. Price-wise, again using the bearish crest data, we obtain a price target range of 
104.62–110.24, which represents a 4.5–10% rise.” The bearish 14-month cycle crest was established 
on January 13, 2025, at 110.17, which was both within the forecasted time and price target spans. 
My preferred view is that we are 13.5 months into the second 14-month cycle. As the Dollar is 
assumed to be in a bearish long-term scenario, the forecast is that prices should now decline into the 
second 14-month cycle low, projected to occur with its 5.5-month orb, sometime between June 2025 
and April 2026. This 14-month cycle bottom is also anticipated to be a 16-year cycle trough, which nar-
rows the time target to January 2026–January 2027. Hence, via additional overlapping, we can further 
concentrate the timing for the 16-year cycle bottom to January 2026–April 2026. This is a very tight 
time gap for a 16-year cycle trough. Hence, let’s not forget that the greater cycle is always in command, 
and the long-term cycle low could, at least potentially, come in at the latest, by March 2027.
A bearish 14-month cycle low is expected historically to come in at a descent of 10%–22%, 
which computes to 86–99 USD. As a 16-year cycle trough is due to unfold, this decline might be too 
shallow. Nevertheless, we have already estimated a first price target range of 84–87 USD, so we can 
overlap with the 14-month cycle low price objective to further narrow down our target to 86–87 USD. 
When the long-term cycle trough is behind us, the prices should rise to a bullish 14-month cycle crest, 
expected to top out six to eleven months after the low and at an increase of 13–23%. 
GEOCOSMICS
We have the important Saturn–Neptune conjunction in February 2026. As this planetary pair only 
meets once, we will extend the timing by four months on either side of the conjunction, which produces 
a time frame of October 2025–June 2026. This time target range creates a bit of a problem for us, since 
we just got a low on September 17, at 96.22 (10). Although it is slightly off, time-wise there is still a pos-
sibility that the greater cycle trough occurred on this date, as September 2025 is within the time forecast 
for the 5.2-year cycle low. However, the price decline was only 16.2% from the 114.78 top of September 
2022 (H). Consequently, it is more probable that the 16-year cycle trough is still ahead.
Now, we have previously carved out a very narrowed down time target range for the 16-year 
cycle bottom to January–April 2026. Hence, the Saturn–Neptune conjunction does not improve this 
slimmed-down time frame. Nevertheless, I think it is wise to extend the timing for the 16-year cycle 
trough to June 2026, incorporating the later timing portion of this planetary pair conjunction.
## Page 142

138
TECHNICALS
Last year detailed: “The price action for the last fifteen years has been in a channel defined by 
the two parallel lines (see chart) that started from the 2009 crest (D) and from the 2011 trough (5)… 
A solid signal that the long-term bearish scenario is active would occur if the prices would break sus-
tainably below the lower parallel line, right now, in November 2024, at 100.38, and rising about 0.17 
USD per month. “The prices did indeed break below the lower parallel line in April 2025, supporting 
the bearish outlook. If the prices were to overtake this line, right now at 102.85 and rising, it would 
increase the probability that either the 16-year cycle trough took place in 2021(8) or in September 
2025 (10).
The next support area is the long-term line that joins the crests of 2001 (B) and 2017 (F). It is 
currently at 93.85 and falling about 0.09 USD per month. If the prices decline sustainably below this 
significant support line (in place now for 24 years), it will send a second forceful signal that the prices 
are heading to the greater cycle trough. Although the estimated price target for the forthcoming long-
term cycle low suggests prices should head below this line, we must still be on the alert that this line 
could be where the 16-year cycle trough occurs. 
Finally, we have a support line, passing through the lows 4 & 5. It is at this time at 81.57 and 
rising about 0.050 USD per month. If the U.S. Dollar Index falls below the 84–87 level, then this is a 
potential reversal zone for the upcoming 16-year cycle trough. The ideal setup would be if the prices 
could temporarily break below this important support line, cementing the greater cycle low. On the 
other hand, as it is getting very late in the greater cycle, there might not be enough time to reach this 
lowest line.
BIAS
Last year, even though the prices were rising from the September 2024 low (9), my bias was 
bearish for the Dollar, a judgment that was only hanging in the balance on the political cycle. There 
were no other clues. This bearish bias strengthened in April 2025, when the prices broke below the 
lower parallel line.
The final concern is whether the September 17, 2025, low at 96.21 (10) could have been the 
16-year cycle trough. It was within its time target span, but as it was not within the estimated price 
target range, I am biased that the greenback is heading lower and thus that the 16-year cycle trough 
is still ahead.
Nevertheless, if, against my bias, the prices would now instead rise, overtaking, at first, the 
lower parallel line, then the Dollar could be in a long-term bullish trend from a greater cycle trough, 
cemented in January 2021, or even in September 2025. This bullish outlook would be powerfully 
reinforced if the previous 14-month cycle crest, established on January 13, 2025, at 110.17 (I), is sur-
passed, as it would confirm that a new 14-month cycle is in a bullish trend. However, it is only when 
the September 2022 crest, at 114.78 (H), is overtaken that we would have the confirmation that the 
long-term bullish alternative is active.

 U.S. DOLLAR/YEN
by Gianni Di Poce, MMA Analyst
REVIEW
The Dollar/Yen had an inside year in 2025. The high of the year occurred early in the year, on 
January 10 at 158.87, while the low of the year occurred on April 22, 2025, at 139.86. This was below 
the high of 2024 but above the low of 2024 as well. Throughout most of the year, the Bank of Japan 
(BOJ) allowed interest rates on Japanese government bonds (JGBs) to rise. This caused some weak-
ness in the Dollar/Yen exchange rate, but with the election of Sanae Takaichi in 2025, markets are 
starting to price in a return to “Abenomics” policies. These economic policies centered on weakening 
the Japanese Yen in order to manage the country’s debt load. This creates a backdrop for potential 
strength in the Dollar/Yen in 2025, and it is supported by the long-term cycle situation as well.
Last year’s Conclusion section stated, “The weight of the evidence of the Dollar/Yen being in a 
new 4.125-year cycle is very compelling. The biggest question for the Dollar/Yen now, given its late-
ness of the 16.5-year cycle, is whether it can go on to make new cycle and multi-decade highs. Given 
the geocosmic backdrop, our bias is that USD/JPY will retest the 164.00 +/- 2.00 zone and probably 
rally as high as 175.00–177.00. It cannot entirely be ruled out that a 16.5-year cycle crest forms in 
2025 in this zone of 175.00–177.00, but this is not our bias. On the contrary, the geocosmics of 2025 
suggest we’re only getting a preview, due to retrograde motions, of a more profound crisis to come in 
the Dollar/Yen in 2026. Eventually, we could see the Dollar/Yen rally as high as 220.00–225.00, but 
probably not in 2025. This may coincide with the greater long-term 16.5-year cycle.” 
While the Dollar/Yen did not rally up to the target of 175.00–177.00, it held firmly in the 139.00 
+/– 2.00 zone, essentially completing a double bottom to the September 2024 low. This low occurred 
seven months later, and it is not uncommon to see retests of important long-term cycle bottoms 6–22 
months later. It will also be a matter of whether the Bank of Japan reverts to a more accommodative 
monetary policy and stops allowing yields on JGBs to rise. There may be a final attempt at lowering 
yields with the new administration in power.
THE LONG-TERM CYCLES IN THE DOLLAR/YEN
The longest cycle to watch in the Dollar/Yen is 16.5 years. The prior low was on October 31, 
2011, at 75.55, and 2026 starts the 15th year of the cycle. This long-term cycle points to a low around 
August 2028 +/– 3.5 years, so a low is due at any time. But first, the crest for this long-term cycle 
must be confirmed. As it stands, the crest from July 2024 at 161.99 is holding, but there is still a pos-
sibility that USD/JPY can rally one final time before reversing lower.
Historically, the 16.5-year cycle broke down into phases lasting 5.5 years, or 55–77 months. 
However, in this cycle, a two-phase pattern composed of two 8.25-year cycles appears to have taken 
hold. An 8.25-year cycle trough unfolded in March 2020, making 2026 the sixth year in the 8.25-year 
cycle. This cycle is calling for a low between 2027 and 2029, so in theory, USD/JPY could still hit 
a new cycle high this year before beginning a drop into an 8.25-year cycle low. This 8.25-year cycle 
crest would form together with the 16.5-year cycle crest.

There is, however, a slim chance that a 16.5-year cycle bottom occurred in April 2025 with the low
