months, and from the October 2011 low, the June 2016 low was 56 months. If the secondary low of Janu-
ary 2021 is considered with respect to the initial March 2020 low, it occurred 55 months from June 2016. 
Finally, the April 2025 low would be 51 months from January 2021, which is a bit short for a 5.5-year 
cycle trough; however, with a potential 16.5-year cycle bottom looming, it is not uncommon for shorter 
cycles to contract. This scenario is not a high-probability one, but it exists nonetheless. It represents the 
most bullish scenario for USD/JPY, as 2026 could start the first year of a new 16.5-year cycle.
The 8.25-year cycle is then broken down into two 4.125-year cycle phases. The first 4.125-year 
cycle low within the 8.25-year cycle occurred on September 16, 2024, at 139.56. Forecast 2025 
stated, “It’s now the final 4.125-year cycle phase within the greater 8.25-year cycle phase, and we’re 
in the second 8.25-year cycle phase within the greater 16.5-year cycle. Thus, we expect this 4.125-
year cycle crest to coincide with the 16.5-year cycle crest too. A rally as high as 175.00-177.00 can-
not be ruled out in 2025. Our bias is for the 164.00 +/- 2.00 zone to be tested, and then, eventually, 
exceeded given the new 4.125-year cycle.” 
It did not rally up to 175.00–177.00 in 2025, but this upside objective remains on the table for 
2026 and beyond. The year 2026 will mark only the second year in the second and final 4.125-year 
cycle. This cycle’s crest will coincide with the greater 8.25-year and 16.5-year cycle crests.
THE INTERMEDIATE-TERM CYCLES IN THE DOLLAR/YEN
The 4.125-year cycle breaks down further into either two 22.5-month cycle phases or three 
17-month cycle phases. The 22.5-month cycle represents not only a half-cycle phase of the 4.125-
year cycle, but also one of the three phases of the 5.5-year cycle. The 4.125-year cycle that bottomed 
in September 2024 broke down into a three-phase pattern of 17-month phases. Forecast 2025 stated, 
“The question now is whether this final 4.125-year cycle phase to the greater 8.25-year cycle will 
break down into two 22.5-month or three 17-month cycles. It is still too early to tell, but January 2025 
will begin the 4th month in this new intermediate-term cycle. Since it’s the first phase of a new 4.125-
year cycle, we anticipate it to be bullish and rally into June or July at least.” 
So far, the high of this first phase of the 4.125-year cycle occurred on January 10, 2025, at 158.87. 
Thus, my expectation is for new cycle highs to follow in 2026, although it is not yet certain what the 
phase breakdown of this cycle will be. January 2026 will start the 16th month from the September 
2024 low, and so if there is going to be a 17-month cycle phase, then a crest could be anticipated 
in the first quarter of 2026 at the latest. A low would be expected no later than April or May 2026. 
However, if there are going to be two 22.5-month cycle phases, USD/JPY could easily rally into the 
back half of 2026. A 22.5-month cycle trough would be due by December 2026, though. Even so, the 
intermediate-term cycles point to more upside for USD/JPY throughout the majority of 2026.
## Page 145

141
GEOCOSMICS
There are a plethora of geocosmic setups that continue to warn of problems for the Japanese 
Yen in 2026. In other words, the outlook favors significantly more upside in 2026 and beyond. In all 
likelihood, the crest will be very climactic. The geocosmics in play for 2026 point to a resurgence 
in inflationary pressures, and the setup is shaping up to be bullish for USD/JPY. It begins with the 
conjunction between Saturn and Neptune at zero degrees Aries on February 20, 2026. Throughout 
2025, the loose conjunction between these two planets kept a lid on inflation. Still, as they begin 
to separate in 2026, the restrictive forces of Saturn may no longer serve to contain the inflationary 
nature of Neptune in a fire sign. 
Then there is a series of aspects in July and August that could prove pivotal for debt markets, 
which are directly connected to currency markets. It begins with the trine between Uranus and 
Pluto, an aspect that will remain in effect into 2028. The central time band begins on July 18, 
and then two days later, there is a trine between Jupiter and Neptune, and an opposition between 
Jupiter and Pluto (both on July 20). With Pluto involved here, debt markets must be considered, 
as Pluto rules debt. With Jupiter and Neptune involved, inflation must be considered, as they co-
rule this monetary phenomenon. There is another exact hit of Uranus trine Pluto toward the end 
of 2026 as well, on November 26. Each of these exact trines should be considered “hot spots” for 
a potential intervention in either debt or currency markets, and the Bank of Japan is well known 
for doing this.
Speaking of Japan’s central bank, these outer-planetary transits should be considered in 
terms of aspects to its natal chart. The central bank’s official website states that it was estab-
lished on October 10, 1882, but the birth time is not provided, so we can only analyze aspects. 
Forecast 2025 stated, “For 2025, there are a few key transits that could compound the Bank of 
Japan’s woes. On the top of the list is Uranus ingressing into Gemini on July 7. This is because 
Uranus will move into orb of an opposition with the BOJ’s natal Venus at 2 degrees Sagittarius. 
Granted, there won’t be an exact aspect, as Uranus only makes it to the first degree of Gemini 
before retrograding back into Taurus on November 7. But still, Uranus opposite Venus is a 
## Page 146

142
classical transit for currency collapse or monetary shocks. However, around the same time, Nep-
tune ingressing into Aries will form a trine to the BOJ’s natal Venus. Thus, the combined forces 
of Uranus and Neptune will be influencing Venus at the same time. Neptune may counteract some 
of the shock associated with Uranus and provide an illusion that all is under control, or it may 
lead to hysteria surrounding the collapse of the Japanese Yen. Keep in mind that it’s in the first 
phase of a long-term cycle, which is usually when a market is at its most bullish. It’s unlikely the 
crest of the 4.125-year cycle will occur in 2025, but rather, when the exact aspects to Venus take 
place in 2026.” 
Uranus makes its definitive ingress into Gemini on April 25, and by late June, there will finally be 
an exact opposition to the Bank of Japan’s natal Venus. Thus, I am looking for an acceleration to the 
upside in the value of the Dollar against the Yen throughout the summer of 2026. It is also worth not-
ing that before this final ingress into Gemini takes place, Uranus will be conjunct the natal Pluto of the 
Bank of Japan. 
The central bank allowed interest rates on Japanese government bonds to rise throughout much 
of 2025, and this led to some strength in the Japanese Yen and weakness in the Dollar/Yen exchange 
rate. However, this policy is likely to be abandoned once Uranus moves away from Pluto in late Tau-
rus. This would be consistent with a return to Abenomics-style policies in Japan, which are centered 
around weakness in the Japanese Yen and, therefore, a higher USD/JPY exchange rate.
There are other transits to consider in the BOJ’s natal chart. Pluto forms an exact square with the 
Bank of Japan’s natal Mars in Scorpio starting in June–July of 2026. Although Mars rules Scorpio, 
Mars square Pluto is a classic signature of conflict. Pluto rules debt and manipulations. Forecast 
2025 stated, “The Bank of Japan may literally be fighting (Mars) to keep their bonds (Pluto) from 
crashing, but in doing so, may lose complete control over the Yen’s value. It’s unlikely that this 
conflict will culminate in 2025, but by the end of the year, it will become very obvious that it’s a 
serious issue.” As of this writing, the Dollar/Yen has not reached this crisis point, but the exact 
square between Pluto and Mars still has not occurred. There are stronger odds of this happening in 
2026 compared with 2025.
CONCLUSION
2026 will start only the second year in the second and final 4.125-year cycle phase within the 
greater 8.25-year cycle. The Dollar/Yen is in the second and final 8.25-year cycle phase within 
the greater 16.5-year cycle, of which 2026 starts the 15th year. Thus, the Dollar/Yen is in the late 
stages of multiple long-term cycles, but final phases can go parabolic and take markets to unthink-
able highs. The geocosmic backdrop is present in 2026 for a meteoric rise in the Dollar/Yen to 
occur, between Uranus’s opposition to the Bank of Japan’s Venus and Pluto’s square to the Bank 
of Japan’s Mars.
My bias is that USD/JPY will retest the 164.00 +/– 2.00 zone early on in 2026 and, in all likeli-
hood, rally as high as 175.00–177.00 at some point during the year. If it cannot test, and preferably 
exceed, the 164.00 +/– 2.00 zone by June, it may be the case that the 16.5-year cycle already formed 
its crest back in 2024, although this is not my preferred outlook. In fact, given the geocosmic back-
drop in the coming years, I could see the Dollar/Yen surge as high as 220.00–225.00, but probably not 
in 2026. This would likely coincide with the greater long-term 16.5-year cycle.
## Page 147

143
The most important cycle to watch for in terms of a crest and a reversal back lower in the Dollar/
Yen in 2026 is the 17-month or 22.5-month cycle. It is still unclear whether the 4.125-year cycle is 
breaking down into a two- or three-phase pattern. A 17-month cycle bottom is most likely by the first 
quarter of 2026, and it is likely to hold above 150.00–152.00. If this level were to break, it would 
increase the odds that the longer-term cycles are topping out. A break below 140.00–142.00 in 2026 
would confirm that the 16.5-year cycle crest has peaked and that the Dollar/Yen could drop as low as 
128.00–130.00, but this is not in my preferred playbook for 2026, especially given the signatures in 
the Bank of Japan’s chart and the inflationary mundane backdrop. Overall, 2026 appears to be a very 
bullish year for the Dollar/Yen as all of the factors are weighed.

 THE EURO
by Ulric Aspegren, MMA Analyst
REVIEW
In mid-November 2024, when the Euro report for the upcoming Forecast 2026 book was com-
pleted, the Euro was in freefall. The prices had managed previously to establish a peak at 1.127 USD 
in July 2023 (E), after rising 18% from an important trough at 0.953 USD in September 2022 (5). 
The prices tried to surpass this July 2023 crest, but stalled at 1.121 in September 2024, just below the 
tip of a massive triangle pattern. The situation did not look promising for the Euro, as it had already 
declined 5% from its September 2024 top. At the time, we were in the 25th month since the Septem-
ber 2022 bottom, and the question was: will the bearish trend endure, or is there hope for the bulls?
Last year’s forecast detailed that the ongoing descent was a normal bullish correction to a 
24-month cycle low, which was due to unfold sometime between April 2024 and March 2025. The 
prices kept falling, but finally reversed in the 28th month, on February 3, 2025, at 1.014 (6). A 
24-month cycle trough was thus cemented within the time target, following an overall 10% decline 
from the 24-month cycle crest in July 2023 (E).
As forecasted, the prices have since been in a bullish trend, rallying 17.5% so far to 1.1918 as of 
September 25, 2025. However, is this rally a sustainable affair, or is it just a transitory push-up from 
an intermediate-term cycle low before the Euro heads south again? The Euro closed on November 
14, 2025, at 1.162.

THE LONG-TERM CYCLES IN THE EURO
My favored view is that a Euro greater cycle trough took place on September 28, 2022, at 0.954 
USD (5). The prior greater cycle started in October 2000 (1) and was active for close to 22 years. We 
only have one previous greater cycle to compare with, which began in February 1985. It was opera-
tional for 16 years, as it ended in October 2000. Hence, it is possible that the greater cycle is a 19-year 
cycle, with a 3-year orb. However, my bias is that it is a 16-year cycle and that the previous 22-year 
cycle was a distorted greater cycle and thus an outlier. Time will have to tell.
Assuming the 16-year cycle is the greater cycle, it should normally divide into two 8.4-year cycles. 
In its turn, the 8.4-year cycle has always split into two 4-year cycles. Hence, the assumed greater 16-year 
cycle should now be in its third year and a few months, off the September 2022 trough (5). This is the 
same for the 8.4-year and the 4-year cycles, as all three long-term cycles began at the same low (5). 
The current 4-year cycle is forecast to top out sometime between August 2025 and November 
2026, at 1.313–1.584, an increase of 38%–66%. Once the prices have peaked out, they should head

south to the first 4-year cycle low, anticipated in the time frame December 2025–October 2027, at a

EURO Preferred Monthly Chart, as of November 14, 2025.
THE 24-MONTH INTERMEDIATE-TERM CYCLE IN THE EURO
My preferred outlook is that the 4-year cycle is separating into two 24-month intermediate-term 
cycles. Last year’s report stated: “We should thus be twenty-five months into this first intermediate-
term cycle that began at the September 2022 low. As it is getting late in the cycle to make a higher 
high, my favored view is that the 24-month cycle crest was already established in July 2023 at 1.127 
USD. If this is correct, then the Euro is on its way towards a 24-month cycle bottom, estimated to 
occur with its 6-month orb, sometime between April 2024 and March 2025.”
Moreover, “The historical 6–20% bullish declines of the 24-month cycles generate a price target 
span of 0.897–1.056. The 38.2–61.8% retracement from the 1.127 crest to the 0.953 low produces a 
price objective range of 1.019–1.061. The overlap creates 1.019–1.056, as the most probable price 
target range for the forthcoming 24-month cycle low.”
The 24-month cycle low was established on February 3, 2025, at 1.014 (6). This bottom occurred 
after an acceptable twenty-eight months from the September 2022 low and was within the set time 
target. The bottom was also within the historical price target span, but manifested slightly below the 
61.8% retracement price level.
Further, last year’s report stated: “Once the 24-month cycle low is in place, the prices are expected 
to rise within this second and current 24-month cycle to the 4-year cycle crest. This crest, already 
forecasted earlier, is anticipated to unfold sometime between August 2025 and November 2026, at 
1.313–1.584 USD.”
As the prices within this second 24-month cycle have overtaken the previous 24-month cycle 
crest of July 2023, at 1.127 (E), it confirms that the current 24-month cycle is in a bullish trend. The 
forthcoming 24-month cycle crest is anticipated to manifest sometime between March and November 
2026, at 1.199–1.471 (an increase of 18–45%). When we overlap the objectives of the 4-year and the 
24-month cycle crests, we obtain March–November 2026 and 1.313–1.471 as the most probable time 
and price targets for the 4-year cycle peak.
## Page 150

146
So far, the Euro has risen 17.5% from the February 3, 2025, low (6), establishing a yearly high 
on September 17, 2025 at 1.1918. We actually have to go back to the end of June 2021 to reach a 
higher price level. 
Once the 4-year cycle crest is in place, the prices are expected to decline to the 4-year cycle 
trough, projected to take place sometime between December 2025 and October 2027. We can narrow 
down this time target range with the time objective for the second 24-month cycle low, estimated to 
occur with its 6-month orb, in the time frame August 2026–August 2027. 
The 4-year cycle low should manifest at historical price declines of 14.8–25.8%. You may over-
lap this range with the 38.2–61.8% retracement from the newly formed 4-year cycle crest to the 0.953 
low of September 2022 (5), to obtain the most probable price target span for the 4-year cycle bottom.
GEOCOSMICS
The current 4-year cycle is expected to peak out sometime in the concentrated time band of 
March–November 2026. We have the important Saturn–Neptune conjunction in February 2026. As 
this planetary pair connects only once, we will extend the timing by four months on either side of the 
conjunction, which generates a time period of October 2025–June 2026. Via overlapping, we acquire 
March–June 2026, which is the most probable timing for the 4-year cycle crest. As already seen, the 
4-year cycle low is then expected to cement, at the latest, by August 2027.
TECHNICALS
As you can see on the chart, the prices have managed since last year’s report to surpass a sub-
stantial resistance line, which joins the 2001 and the 2017 lows. As long as prices can stay above this 
now important support line, the bulls are in control.
If we look to the future, we can see that the line that crosses through the 2010 low (3) and the 
2018 crest (D) is at about 1.334 in March 2026, which is at the beginning of the narrowed-down time 
target range and at the lower edge of the price target span for the 4-year cycle crest. This area could 
be the area where the 4-year long-term cycle peaks out.
BIAS
My bias is that the Euro will remain in a long-term bullish trend until at least the upcoming 4-year 
cycle crest, which is due to unfold sometime in the narrowed-down time frame of March–June 2026. 
We should then get a correction down to the 4-year cycle trough, expected, at the latest, by August 
2027. However, once the 4-year cycle bottom is cemented, the prices should, if history repeats itself, 
continue higher within the next 4-year cycle to a combined 8 and 16-year cycle crest. However, we 
must be on the alert that the 16-year cycle peak could already manifest at this forthcoming 4-year 
cycle top (anticipated sometime between March–June 2026).
If, against my bias, the prices were now to decline below the 1.014 low of February 2025 (6), 
then the current 24-month cycle would turn into a bearish trend, confirming that the 24-month cycle 
crest is behind us. The lowest price of this ongoing intermediate-term cycle will be at its very end, 
sometime between August 2026 and August 2027. Nevertheless, we would only have the confirma-
tion that the whole 16-year cycle has turned bearish if the 0.953 low of September 2022 (5) is broken. 
If this were to occur, then we might even need to revise the whole long-term chart labeling for the 
Euro, where the current 16-year cycle would more likely have started in January 2017.

 THE SWISS FRANC
by Gianni Di Poce, MMA Analyst
REVIEW 
The Swiss Franc in 2025 was exceptionally strong as it rallied to its highest level since 2011. 
The high of the year was on September 17, 2025, at 1.2904, and the low of the year was on February 
3, 2025, at 1.0923. Once again, the Swiss Franc was one of the strongest-performing fiat currencies 
of 2025, and that’s even with the Swiss National Bank (SNB) cutting rates back down to zero. This 
clearly was not enough to reduce demand for this safe-haven currency. In a world filled with geopo-
litical turmoil, the neutrality of Switzerland has been very appealing to investors. 
But perhaps the biggest development of 2025 was the reset of an 8.25-year cycle. The big ques-
tion, however, is whether this cycle low occurred in May 2024 at 1.0899 or in February 2025 at 
1.0923. Note how this February 2025 low occurred in the 6–22 month secondary low window that 
often occurs at long-term cycle bottoms. Forecast 2025’s conclusion section stated, “If the Swiss 
Franc is in a newer 8.25-year cycle from May 2024, then a rally as high as 1.2750 +/–.0150 cannot 
be ruled out. The biggest thing is that we expect either a high above the high of 2024 at 1.2036 or a 
low below the low of 2024 at 1.0900.” This long-term cyclical reset could prove to be a major tail-
wind for the Swiss Franc in the coming years, and points to higher prices.

THE LONG-TERM CYCLES IN THE SWISS FRANC
The Swiss Franc’s longest cycle is 16.5 years. While this cycle has been shown to fit well for this 
currency, there have only been two previous occurrences, which means it doesn’t have the strongest 
statistical reliability. Nonetheless, previous lows occurred in February 1985, July 2001, and then 
again in December 2016. Note that although there are three lows, they make up only two cycles, 
since they are measured low-to-low. The July 2001 bottom was at 0.5492, and the December 2016 
low occurred at 0.9669. This means the next 16.5-year cycle trough in the Swiss Franc is due in 2032 
+/– 3 years. But perhaps the most exciting development with respect to the 16.5-year cycle is how 
prices hit a new cycle high in 2025. This high in the 9th year is a strong signal that this is a bullish 
16.5-year cycle. Forecast 2025 stated, “… ample time remains for new highs in this currency. Not 
to mention, a Republican president will be in the White House starting in 2025, and historically, 
this corresponds with a weaker Dollar, which means that the Swiss Franc could yet make new cycle 
highs.” And indeed, new highs followed.
The 16.5-year cycle typically breaks down into two 8.25-year cycles. Historically, this has mani-
fested as a two-phase pattern, with each phase lasting approximately 8.25 years. However, the current 
16.5-year cycle may not be breaking down accordingly this time. It could be exhibiting three 5.5-year 
## Page 152

148
cycles, too, but this is not our bias. The previous 8.25-year cycle lows were in July 2001 (100 months 
from March 1993), November 2008 (88 months from July 2001), and December 2016 (96 months 
from November 2008). The 8.25-year cycle has historically shown a range of 88–100 months. 
Given this range, there are two possible scenarios for an 8.25-year cycle trough. The February 
2025 low would have been 98 months from the December 2016 low, but then there’s also the May 
1, 2024, low, which was 89 months from December 2016. Either way, there is strong evidence that 
a long-term cyclical reset took place in the Swiss Franc. In January 2026 will either enter the 11th 
month in a slightly newer 8.25-year cycle in the Swiss Franc from the February 2025 low, or it will 
begin the 20th month from the May 2024 low. Under the February 2025 labeling, the next 8.25-year 
cycle low wouldn’t be due until June 2032–June 2033. Note how this overlaps with the time band 
for the greater 16.5-year cycle. This is to be expected as it’s in the second 8.25-year cycle phase 
within the 16.5-year cycle. Under the May 2024 labeling, the low wouldn’t be due until September 
2031-September 2032.
Next, the possibility of a 5.5-year cycle must be addressed. To be clear, there haven’t been any 
instances of a 5.5-year cycle going back to 1985. However, cycles are known to break down into 
smaller phases that are divided by two or three of the greater cycle length. Plus, 5.5-year cycles are 
observed in other currency markets. In this scenario, November 2022 would have been a 5.5-year 
cycle bottom. January 2026 would begin the 38th month from November 2022, or the 4th year, and 
there would still be time for new highs, although a crest could easily form in 2026. This is only the 
second 5.5-year cycle phase within the greater 16.5-year cycle, and a low would be due between May 
2027 and May 2029. The 5.5-year cycle phase to follow out of such a low could easily be bearish 
since the 16.5-year cycle would be very late then, but it’s too soon to know for sure.
The other long-term factor to consider in the Swiss Franc is the two-phase pattern to the 8.25-
year cycle, which is made up of two 4-year cycles. The 4-year cycle would have reset with the 8.25-
year cycle, which means that the Swiss Franc is now in the first 4-year cycle phase in this newer 
8.25-year cycle. 2026 would either begin the 1st or 2nd year of this 4-year cycle phase, depending on 
## Page 153

149
whether the greater 8.25-year cycle bottomed in May 2024 or February 2025. Note that the previous 
4-year cycle exhibited a case of contraction, as the prior low was in November 2022. But such cases 
of contraction are not uncommon when longer cycles come due, as the 8.25-year cycle overpowers 
the 4-year cycle. It’s still early enough in this 4-year cycle for the Swiss Franc to climb to new highs, 
and in all likelihood, into the 1.3200 +/– .0200 zone at least.
GEOCOSMICS
From a mundane astrological standpoint, one of the risks for the Swiss Franc in 2026 is that the 
Swiss National Bank may struggle to keep interest rates low if inflation resurges. Between Neptune 
making its definitive ingress into Aries starting on January 26, 2026, and Jupiter’s eventual ingress 
into Leo on June 30, and the subsequent trine between the two planets on July 20, there’s a real threat 
of another inflationary wave in 2026. However, this may turn out to be bullish for the Swiss Franc, 
because it would eventually force the Swiss National Bank to raise interest rates again. Keep in mind 
that rates have been cut back to zero in Switzerland, and this hasn’t been enough to stem the rise in 
the Swiss Franc. It’s not my bias that the Swiss National Bank hikes in 2026, but if they were to begin 
considering rate hikes again, it probably wouldn’t be before the Jupiter–Pluto opposition of August 31. 
Transits to the Swiss National Bank’s natal chart can also be considered. The central bank was 
established on June 19, 1906, by the National Bank Act, but it didn’t start operating until June 16, 
1907. There is no birthtime available, but outer planetary aspects can still be analyzed. The location 
of this chart is Zurich, Switzerland. Forecast 2025 stated, “The first planetary placement that stands 
out is the SNB’s natal Venus at 29 degrees of Taurus. Not only is the 29th degree of a sign considered 
to be karmically potent, but Venus also rules currencies. It’s no surprise that the Swiss Franc is one 
of the strongest currencies from a historical standpoint, with Venus in Taurus, a sign she rules. But 
in 2025 and into 2026, we will see Uranus transit over this degree on multiple occasions. Uranus 
will go retrograde and direct within the orb of Venus as well. Transiting Uranus conjunct Venus is a 
classical currency boom or bust signature. Thus, we have the geocosmic catalyst here for the Swiss 
Franc to potentially collapse as low as 1.0200 +/– 0.0100 in 2025 for an 8.25-year cycle low. A 
sharp rally would likely follow given the nature of this transit. But in the event it’s a newer 8.25-year 
cycle from May 1, 2024, we could see the Swiss Franc explode higher in value, and potentially rally 
as high as 1.2750 +/– .0150 in 2025. This scenario is supported by the political cycle as well. Ura-
nus will hit the 29-degree mark of Taurus in June 2025, which is a bit late given the 88–100-month 
cycle range of the Swiss Franc’s 8.25-year cycle. If the low is complete below, then it could coincide 
with a surge higher.” The newer 8.25-year cycle scenario was in play, and indeed, the Swiss Franc 
exploded higher just above the upside target of 1.2750 +/– .0150 last year. The high of the year was 
in September 2025 at 1.2904.
Looking ahead into 2026, there are a few notable transits that stand out in the SNB’s natal chart. 
First, there will be both Saturn and Jupiter returns for the central bank. The Saturn return is very early 
in the year, January 13. The Jupiter return occurs a couple of times due to retrograde motions on 
February 15 and April 3. If anything, these conjunctions will serve to further reinforce the value of 
the Swiss Franc for the first few months of 2026. There will even be another conjunction with transit-
ing Uranus over the Swiss Franc’s natal Venus on April 23. This may serve to coincide with another 
notable surge in the value of the Swiss Franc +/- 1 month.
However, the prospect for volatility in the Swiss Franc starts to increase starting in May, as there 
will be a T-square between Saturn, Uranus, and Neptune. Transiting Saturn will be at the apex, as 
## Page 154

150
Uranus and Neptune are in opposition in the SNB’s natal chart, in Capricorn and Cancer, respectively. 
Due to retrograde motions, there will be another passage of this T-square in late September and early 
October. Thus, the Swiss Franc may experience a period of sharp volatility between late May and 
early October. It could start as an initial spike to the upside, followed by a sharp drop to the downside, 
or vice versa, but this seems to be the hot spot for the currency in 2026. Remember that if the mar-
ket sniffs out that the SNB is going to eventually start raising rates again, it could lead to a flood of 
money rushing into this safe-haven currency. It’s also worth pointing out that the Uranus–Pluto trine, 
which is the feature signature of 2026 and beyond, does not aspect the Swiss National Bank chart at 
all throughout this year. If anything, this may prove to provide some extra stability, which is highly 
sought after in this current market environment. 
CONCLUSIONS
There are still questions as to whether the Swiss Franc is breaking down into a two-phase, a 
three-phase, or even a combination pattern when it comes to the 16.5-year cycle. As of this writ-
ing in November 2025, my bias is increasingly that a combination pattern with both 8.25-year and 
5.5-year cycle phases is playing out. The breakout to new multi-year highs in 2025 confirmed that 
an 8.25-year cycle bottomed either in May 2024 or February 2025 (the latter can be considered a 
double-bottom, or secondary low). The Swiss Franc is still early enough in the 8.25-year cycle for 
the currency to exceed the 2025 highs in 2026. However, it’s not as probable that a sustained surge 
similar to what was witnessed in 2025 will play out in 2026.
The 5.5-year cycle is still early enough to carry the Swiss Franc to new multi-year highs as well. 
Ideally, a rally up to the 1.3900–1.4000 zone can occur before the longer-term 16.5-year cycle tops 
out, and while this is the best-case scenario for the Swiss Franc in 2026, it’s not the likeliest one. 
Instead, a rally up to the 1.3400–1.3600 area is the preferred target for 2026. My bias is that the Swiss 
Franc won’t see lower prices than 1.2200–1.2300 in 2026 either. In other words, new highs above 
the 2025 highs are on the table, but new lows below the 2025 lows are not (that would be quite the 
reversal back lower). In fact, the sooner the Swiss Franc breaks above 1.2600–1.2700, the sooner that 
becomes the new floor, or the new support zone in this currency. It’s shaping up to be another strong 
year for the Swiss Franc in 2026. 
In summary, position traders may buy the Swiss Franc as long as it remains above 1.1950 on a 
closing basis.

 BITCOIN IN 2026
by Raymond Merriman
“Never sell your Bitcoin,” 
—President Donald Trump, “Full Text of Trump’s Speech at the Bitcoin Conference,” 
The Block Beats, July 27, 2024.
“It ain’t what you don’t know that gets you into trouble. It’s what you know for sure that just 
ain’t so.” 
—Mark Twain, as posted on “X” by @SilverSurfer23 (Melbourne, Australia).
REVIEW AND PREVIEW
Bitcoin had quite a year in 2025. It started with a new all-time high of 109,071 on January 26. It 
then fell to a yearly low of 74,445 on April 7–9, a loss of 31.7%. Next, it rallied to yet another new 
all-time high (ATH) on October 6, 2025, at 126,223, which was a double top to an earlier ATH of 
124,480 made on August 14, 2025.
The behavior of Bitcoin (BTC) during the year fit the two special updates I issued during the 
year. The first was issued on May 5 as BTC was trading around 94,000. It called for an all-time high 
to take place around October 2025, +/– 1 month, based on the history of the halving cycle, where new 
ATHs tend to happen 16–18 months later. The halving event took place in April 2024. The high was 
thus due August–October. The forecast was moved up one month, to September–November, based 
on the phasing of shorter-term cycles and geocosmic studies. The price target given for the high was 
up to 150,000–158,000.
After the 124,480 new ATH on August 14 and a pullback to the 105,000 area on September 1, a 
special webinar was conducted on September 14, where my outlook on Bitcoin was revised. Although 
150,000 was still a possible target, it was getting late in the time band for a new ATH, ideally due in 
October now. Traders needed to be alert to a possible double top this late in the cycle, where BTC 
could test and even slightly exceed the 124,480 ATH on August 14, and that is what happened. On 
October 6, 2025, the yearly high in BTC, as of this writing, was recorded at 126,223. 
The combination of cycles studies, geocosmics, and chart patterns worked out extremely well. 
Since that time, and as of this writing in early November, BTC has declined by over 20% and below 
100,000.
Based on these same cycle studies reported in the special update and webinar of May and Sep-
tember 2025, the outlook now calls for a decline of 70–90% in BTC by the end of 2026. A new ATH 
in the first quarter of 2026 would alter or delay this bearish outlook for 2026.

CYCLES
There is not a lot of historical data on Bitcoin to derive any strong long-term cycles. Hence, Mark 
Twain’s adage about “It ain’t what you don’t know that gets you into trouble. It’s what you know 
for sure that just ain’t so,” applies here. We don’t have enough data to have high confidence in the 
longer-term cycles related to Bitcoin. It’s only been around for 17 years.
Early indications, however, suggest the possibility that a 4–year cycle may apply to BTC. 
The all-time low was $0.01 (one cent) on October 8, 2010. After rising to a high of $1242 on 
November 29, 2013, BTC fell 88.5% to a low of $142 on January 14, 2015. This was 51 months fol-
lowing the all-time low of .01 in October 2010. 
From there, the second 4-year cycle began. BTC soared to a new all-time high of $19,458 on 
December 18, 2017. But then it collapsed to a low of $3122 on December 15, 2018. This was 47 
months after the previous low and represented a loss of 83.9%. 
The third instance ended with the low of November 21, 2022, which was 49 months after the 
prior low. Thus, we have three instances where a possible 4-year cycle bottomed between 47 and 51 
## Page 157

153
months. Allowing a normal range of 1/6 of the median cycle length would suggest a 4-year cycle 
with an orb of eight months. Measured from November 21, 2022, the next 4-year cycle would be 
due November 2026 +/– 8 months, or March 2026 to July 2027. If it happens in the 47–51 month 
intervals of the first three cases, it would next be due October 2026 to February 2027.
Cycles usually subdivide into phases that are either 1/2 or 1/3 the length of the greater cycle. In 
many cases, both a 2- and 3-phase cycle may be present in the greater cycle, forming a “combina-
tion” pattern. The current 4-year BTC cycle is unfolding in a combination pattern, with lows at both 
the ½ and 1/3 intervals. Thus, we see both a 16-month and a 24-month sub-cycle within the greater 
4-year cycle.
The first 24-month half-cycle occurred on August 5, 2024, at 49,445. It was 21 months following 
the 4-year cycle on November 21, 2022. With a range of four months, it is next due between April 2026 
and December 2026. Note that it will overlap the 4-year cycle which is also due during this time.
Two of the three-phase sub-cycles have also taken place, on January 23, 2024, and April 7, 2025. 
The third one will coincide with the 4-year cycle. With a range of 13–19 months, it is ideally due 
from May to November 2026, again overlapping with the 4-year cycle, as well as the next 24-month 
cycle. In fact, if the 4-year cycle again unfolds at the 47–51-month interval, all of these cycles would 
overlap October to November 2026. With such a short history in BTC, however, it might be wise to 
consider the orb to be a bit wider.
Lately, BTC has also been exhibiting an 8–13 month cycle. There could be two of these within 
the 16-month cycle, and in some cases, it may even coincide with the 16-month cycle if it happens 
in a 13-month period. Within the 24-month cycle, it could unfold two or three times. If this sub-cycle 
is valid, then April 7, 2025, started its second phase of the 24-month cycle, and first phase of the 
16-month cycle. Its next low is thus due December 2025 to May 2026. The one after that would 
coincide with three longer cycles: the 16-month, 24-month, and 4-year cycles. 
PRICE TARGETS
When several cycles converge to bottom simultaneously, then the magnitude of the decline is 
typically steep. It is magnified over what would be expected for a low in the shorter-term cycles. 
Hence, my forecast is for a 70–90% decline from the all-time high of 2025 to the 4-year cycle low 
due in late 2026. It is consistent with the declines from the three prior 4-year cycle highs to lows. In 
other financial markets, such “crashes” are usually 77–93% selloffs from the cycle’s highs. Bitcoin 
has so far fallen into this category, too.
Short-term, the second 10.5-month cycle trough due December 2025–May 2026 has a measured 
price target of 100,335 +/– 6110, or 94,225–106,445. It’s already traded down to 90,000 as of this 
writing in early November 2025 and could be lower by the time the book comes out.  But that 10.5-
month low is due. 
If the longer–term 4-year cycle is to exert its dominance, however, BTC could fall further into its 
next 10.5-month cycle trough. A break below the 16-month moving average (MA) would be the first 
signal. That MA is around 94,000 as this is being written, which is also near the low end of the down-
side price target given above. A break below the 24-month MA, around 82,000 as of mid-November, 
would be a stronger indication that the 4-year cycle has topped out. If these levels are broken, then 
the 4-year cycle crest is in, and a 77–93% decline would give a downside price target of 8835–29,050 
## Page 158

154
for the 4-year cycle trough, due late 2026. However, it should also be pointed out that no 4-year cycle 
bottom has yet to break below a previous 4-year cycle crest. The last confirmed 4-year cycle crest was 
68,999 in November 2021. Measured off the high of 2025, that would represent a decline of 45%, far 
short of declines to previous 4-year cycle troughs of over 78%.
Until major support at 75,000–85,000 is broken, however, the bullish case cannot be completely 
dismissed. The last 10.5-month cycle low in April was 74,445. Technically, BTC is not confirmed 
bearish by MMA methodology until it closes below there, assuming there is not a new high first. If 
the market is to be bullish, and support holds above 75,000–85,000, then the next rally would make 
a new ATH. An estimate of that next high would be 145,000 +/– 900.
In the meantime, if the bearish phase of the 4-year cycle has started, then the rally to the crest of 
the next 10.5-month cycle would be corrective and not make a new all-time high. Resistance for such 
a corrective rally would normally be about 110,000 +/– 4000. But with Bitcoin, rallies (and declines) 
can exceed normal measurements. A rally back to 122,000–125,000 would create an interesting head 
and shoulders chart formation with a neckline around 90,000–95,000. Closing below that would put 
BTC on track for another leg down to 60,000–65,000. And it still wouldn’t be enough for the projec-
tion to the final 4-year cycle trough.
GEOCOSMIC CYCLES
Once again, there is just not enough history to conduct formal studies to identify high-frequency 
correlations between geocosmic cycles and cycles in Bitcoin prices. We can only speculate based on 
basic astrological principles as they might relate to new digital currencies. The assumption is that 
Uranus will be a key geocosmic factor, for it is associated with newness, disruption, and sudden 
changes. Given that world currencies are in a transition phase, moving from paper currencies, backed 
by goodwill and faith of various world governments, to a decentralized digital means of exchange, 
the principles of Uranus appear to apply. And that brings us back to the observation of Uranus as 
an indicator of boom-bust behavior related to the sectors of the economy associated with the sign it 
transits through. 
## Page 159

155
Uranus spends approximately seven years in a sign. It crossed from Taurus into Gemini on July 
7, 2025, through November 8, 2025. It returned back to Taurus, where it remains until April 25, 2026, 
after which it will spend the next six years in Gemini. As Taurus rules money and currency, last year’s 
book suggested, “Bitcoin could experience another large decline nearby to the period when Uranus 
ingresses into Gemini, July 2025–April 2026.” Indeed, Bitcoin made its all-time high in this period 
so far, on October 6, 2025. Then, “This outlook assumes that Bitcoin will exhibit a boom/bust pat-
tern in both Taurus and Gemini. Why? Well, Taurus makes sense because it represents currencies, 
and Bitcoin is a digital currency. Gemini makes sense too, because Bitcoin relies on the blockchain 
technology, which plays a crucial role in maintaining a secure and decentralized record of transac-
tions in digital currencies. There are apt to be many new novel applications and innovations related 
to blockchain use, and this too can greatly affect the price of Bitcoin.” Thus, we expect Bitcoin to 
fall sharply into a 4-year cycle low in the early part of Uranus transiting Gemini, followed by another 
new all-time high within the next 2–4 years.
Last year’s book also focused on the Venus retrograde cycle. It stated, “Another geocosmic fac-
tor to consider is Venus retrograde, March 1–April 12. Since Venus rules currencies, and Bitcoin is 
a digital currency, a reversal from an intermediate-term–term cycle high could take place here. If 
Bitcoin continues its rally into 2025, we could see the crest of the 11- and 16-month cycles January–
March, and then the decline into the low of those cycles within two months of June 2025.” BTC did 
make an all-time high in January 2025, followed by a sharp 31.7% decline into April 7–9, which was 
within two months of June 2025, and while Venus was retrograde. Venus will next turn retrograde 
October 3–November 13, 2026, right in the period when we anticipate the 4-year cycle trough. 
CONCLUSIONS
My outlook on Bitcoin in 2026 is quite simple:
The 4-year cycle crest is in, as of October 2025.
Bitcoin is now in the process of a 73–93% decline into its 4-year cycle trough due April 2026–
August 2027, and especially October 2026–February 2027.
The price target for the low is 8835–29,050.
The outlook will be revised if BTC closes above 127,000.
Investors are advised to buy Bitcoin on a break below 30,000 after April 2026, and especially if 
it happens in October 2026–February 2027.
For further guidance on Bitcoin through 2026, readers are encouraged to subscribe to MMA’s 
daily and weekly Bitcoin reports, which are available at www.mmacycles.com. A new monthly MMA 
Crypto Report is scheduled to begin by March 2026.

 CRUDE OIL IN 2026
by Pouyan Zolfagharnia, MMA Analyst
REVIEW
The water sign of Pisces is commonly associated with Crude Oil, which is ruled over by Neptune 
and Jupiter. The 2022 high for Crude Oil was 130.50 on March 7 and occurred while the Sun trans-
lated the Jupiter–Neptune conjunction in Pisces. This was a significant geocosmic signature relating 
to Crude Oil and may remain as the 12-year crest. Yet it is still early in the cycle, and for the time 
being, it remains as the 4-year crest.
Saturn, the planet of restrictions and contraction, was next to enter Pisces a year later, in March 
2023, and will remain there until February 13, 2026, shortly before the Saturn–Neptune conjunction 
a week later. Crude Oil fell to the 4-year trough in May 2023, a double bottom to the initial low of 
March as Saturn entered Pisces. We have seen numerous Saturnian ‘restrictions’ and ‘limits’ imposed 
on this market, from the price cap and sanctions on the sale of Russian Crude Oil to the Saudi pro-
duction cuts as OPEC+ tried to manage supply. Saturn’s impact can be seen directly on the prices of 
Crude Oil, which has been trapped under a steep trendline since the high of March 2022. 
In 2025, the Saturn–Neptune conjunction was within a 1° orb, and we saw the current 4-year 
cycle turn bearish by taking out the low that commenced the cycle. As we enter the new year and in 
the orb of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction, we are seeing the 22-month moving average (MA) drop-
ping below the slower 72-month MA. With prices under the two MAs, this will downgrade the trend 
to bearish for the first time since the 2020 pandemic low.
As noted in Forecast 2025, “With Saturn exiting the sign of Pisces and entering the confronta-
tional sign of Aries. With numerous geocosmic signatures pointing to 2025–2026 as a period of tense 
geopolitical activity, it is worth mentioning that this asset is often used as a barometer for geopolitical 
## Page 162

158
risk, translating it as higher Crude Prices.” During Saturn’s brief ingress into Aries between May and 
September 2025, we saw the breakout of the 12-day war between Iran and Israel. This sent Crude Oil 
rallying over 42%. I believe this was a prelude for further geopolitical turmoil that is likely to follow 
with Saturn’s entry into Aries over the next three years. If you refer to the chapter on Jupiter’s transit 
of Leo, you will see that the Middle East has experienced geopolitical instability and tension during 
each of these transits, including the Iraq wars of 1990 and 2003. During the 2003 transit, Mossad 
agents leaked information on the Iranian nuclear program. In the previous transit, we saw the Obama 
administration broker the Iranian nuclear deal. There is a pattern suggestive of tensions reaching a 
boiling point with Iran between June 2026 and July 2027.

THE 12-YEAR CYCLE IN CRUDE OIL AND ITS PHASES
The long-term cyclical analysis in Crude Oil begins with a potential 36-year cycle. The exact 
periodicity of this cycle is unknown because there haven’t been enough occurrences in Crude Oil to 
quantify it to a high degree of statistical probability. The previous 36-year cycle was from April 1986 
until April 2020, which was 34 years. 
The 36-year cycle can be subdivided into either two 18-year cycles with a range of 15–21 years, 
or three 12-year cycles with a range of 10–14 years. Historical analysis suggests that the 12-year 
cycle is more prominent. From the low of April 1986, the next 12-year trough was February of 1999, 
which was 12 years and 10 months. Following that, the next trough was January of 2009, which was 
9 years and 11 months. The final 12-year cycle was April 2020, which was 11 years and 3 months 
later. This means that the next 12-year cycle trough is due 2032 +/– 2 years.
As shown in the chart above, the 12-year cycle has a tendency to break down into three 4-year 
or 44-month cyclical phases, with a range of 36–52 months. Therefore, my preferred outlook is 
that the current 44-month cycle formed on May 4, 2023, at 63.64. The trough formed under the 
22-month MA and even tested the 72-month MA. The next 44-month cyclical trough is due Janu-
ary 2027 +/– 8 months. In January 2026, we will be commencing the 32nd month of the current 
44-month cycle, which has turned bearish by taking out the low that commenced the cycle in April 
of 2025.
There is also a chance that the current 12-year cycle is breaking down into a two-phased cycle of 6 
years (range of 5–7 years). This would mean that the 6-year cycle is due between 2025–2027, preferably 
with Saturn in Pisces and in orb of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction. This is my alternative outlook, but 
it deserves attention because a case can be made that a 6-year half cycle is breaking down further into 
two 3-year half-cycle phases with a range of 30–42 month, similar to the U.S. stock market cycle.
## Page 163

159
Under both scenarios, once the 44-month or 6-year trough has formed, I am expecting a strong 
rally back up to the descending trendline that is joining the July 2008 crest to the March 2022 one (in 
the region of 110–125). Since we are in a bullish 12-year cycle, having taken out the crest of the prior 
cycle, it is perfectly conceivable that Crude Oil may even break through the descending trendline and 
record a new ATH with a $130 +/– 15.35 rally from the 44-month or 6-year cycle trough. 
Whilst this asset has essentially remained dormant with the Saturn transit through Pisces over 
the past 3 years, investors should not take their eyes off Crude Oil’s potential for a significant rally. 
The fundamental picture is mixed; On one hand, an economic recession into 2027 would retain prices 
within the bearish price channel until the end of the 44-month or 6-year cycle. On the other hand, the 
risk of geopolitical tension with oil-producing nations (Russia, Iran, Venezuela, etc.), coupled with 
historical low levels of the U.S. Strategic Petroleum Reserve, suggests that Crude Oil prices are coil-
ing and preparing to erupt. 
THE INTERMEDIATE-TERM CYCLES
The 44-month cycle, in turn, can either break down into two 22-month cycles or three 15-month 
cycles.
My preferred outlook for the intermediate cycle count is that we have had a two-phased 
44-month cycle, with the first 22-month cycle following from the April 2020 low, being December 
2021 at 62.43. The next 22-month cycle contracted to 17 months and culminated with a 44-month 
cycle in May 2023 at 63.64. The current 44-month cycle is also breaking down into two phases, 
with the first phase forming in April 2025 at 55.12. The price target for the 44-month trough is 
51.01 +/– 5.20 at any time between May 2026 and September 2027. This is my preferred outlook 
for the intermediate outlook.
As discussed above, the 12-year cycles may be unfolding in two 6-year phases. Whilst this break-
down is far less prominent, it has occurred in the past, so I am sharing it as an alternative outlook. 
This suggests the 6-year trough is due at any point between 2025 and 2027. It would also suggest that 
the 6-year cycle is either breaking down into three 24-month +/– 4 months phases or two 36-month 
## Page 164

160
+/– 6 months phases. If we are in a 6-year cycle, it would appear to have formed a 36-month half-
cycle phase in May 2023, 37 months into the cycle. In this scenario, January will commence the 32nd 
month of the second 36-month cycle, which has turned bearish. The price target for the 36-month 
trough is 28.17 +/– 7.89 at any time between November 2025 and November 2026. It’s possible it 
doesn’t fall that low, as a break below 55.12 would be a minimum target to meet the criterion.
GEOCOSMICS
As noted in Forecast 2025, “The important geocosmic events relating to Crude Oil during 2025 
will be the fact that Saturn will leave Pisces, and the ingress of both Saturn and Neptune over the 
vernal axis, which will take place numerous times during 2025 to 2026, going out with a bang at the 
Saturn–Neptune conjunction on February 20, 2026. With heavy and restrictive Saturnian energy lift-
ing as early as May 2025, we should see a rally in Crude Oil prices.” We got a preview of what is to 
come, between May and June 2025, with the Iran–Israel 12-day war, which sent Crude Oil rallying 
41.8%. It’s worth noting that Israel did not target any of the Iranian petroleum infrastructure during 
the attacks. However, Iran immediately threatened to block (Saturn) the Strait of Hormuz (Neptune), 
should the war escalate. These concerns remain heightened as we enter 2026.
The seasonal trend for Crude Oil is a slump as the Sun transits Sagittarius. As such, I am looking 
for a buying opportunity from late November to mid-December 2025. From here, I would expect a 
rally at least from late February into early March. For the time being, all rallies will be corrective in 
nature until we break through the descending trendline and bearish price channel in the weekly chart. 
If we see a strong weekly or monthly close above these resistance zones, we could see Crude Oil 
rally all the way into July 2026 +/–1 month. At this point, the Jupiter–Pluto opposition will be in full 
force. In prior instances, this signature has corresponded to crest formations within 3 months of the 
opposition that preceded a sharp sell-off. The high of June 2014 formed 2 months after the final Jupi-
ter–Pluto opposition of April 2014. Crude Oil went on to drop 75.8% in value from the crest. The time 
before that was the high of October 2000, which formed a month after the first passage of the Jupi-
ter–Pluto opposition of September 2000. Crude Oil went on to drop 53.7% in value from that crest.
Historical analysis of the Neptune cycle shows that this planet is inflationary when transiting fire 
signs or the vernal axis. There is also evidence of inflationary spikes occurring at the Saturn–Neptune 
conjunctions. We also have the disruptive planet, Uranus, transiting the transactive sign of Gemini, 
which was always expected to bring about trade disruptions. Whilst we are yet to see the full infla-
tionary impact of Trump’s trade wars, it is also worth noting that Crude Oil is one of the key com-
modities responsible for inflation. The last time Neptune went over the vernal axis was 1861, which 
corresponds to the highest value in WTI (when adjusted for inflation) during the American Civil War. 
Crude Oil tends to form important reversals in close proximity to the retrograde motion of Nep-
tune and Jupiter. Neptune will go retrograde on July 7, 2026, until December 12, 2026. Jupiter will go 
retrograde on November 11, 2025, and will be retrograde until March 10, 2026. It will start its next 
retrograde from December 12, 2026 (same day as Neptune) until April 12, 2027. 
CONCLUSION
Whilst the geocosmic outlook is tense, the cycle studies take precedence and remain bearish. The 
cycle studies dictate a bearish move down into the preferred 44-month trough (May 2026–September 
2027) or the alternative outlook of the 6-year trough (April 2025–April 2027). In the latter case, a 
three-year cycle would be due November 2025–November 2026. This overlap zone could be the hot 
## Page 165

161
zone. The price action will help guide us as to which cycle is forming, since the price target for the 
44-month trough is 51.01 +/– 5.20, whilst the target for the 6-year trough may be the steeper decline 
to 28.17 +/– 7.89.
If the geopolitics flare up before either of these two troughs has formed, we are only going to see 
a corrective rally, which will be followed by a sharp move back down, as seen in 2025. However, if 
geopolitics is aligned with either the 44-month or 6-year low, we are likely to see a spectacular rally 
that has a good chance of recording a new ATH. I would expect this low to be accompanied by bullish 
oscillator divergence in the CCI of the weekly chart. Confirmation for the rally will be a weekly or 
monthly close above the descending trend lines shown in my charts.

 GRAIN MARKETS IN 2026
by Wyatt Fellows, MMA Analyst
REVIEW	
Last year’s Forecast 2025 book left off with: “The bottom line here is that with ample grain 
stocks heading into 2025, and the unknown outcomes of the next administration’s policies toward 
energy and trade, it will probably take a supply reduction event to significantly push grain prices 
higher in 2025. Just such an event is possible with the coming Saturn–Neptune conjunction, but its 
effect on the grain markets may not fully be felt until into 2026.” 
We did not get a major supply-reducing weather event last year, and President Trump decided to 
play another game of chicken with China on trade. This kept the grain markets largely range-bound 
but with a more downward bias in Corn and Wheat. On a positive note, all three major grains retested 
their August 2024 lows to some degree in 2025 and held. This is encouraging price action, and as we 
close out 2025, definite signs of life are emerging that could lead to some nice returns for this com-
plex after years of underperformance relative to other commodities and asset classes.
WEATHER
The main event for the grain markets in 2026 is the conjunction of Saturn (restriction) and Nep-
tune (water) taking place in the sign of Aries (fire) on February 20, 2026. In the past, significant 
highs in the grain markets occurred at the conjunctions and oppositions of these two outer planets, 
and mostly within 15 months of the exact aspect. These highs were usually a result of a significant 
drought taking place over a major grain-producing region of the world, which is a hallmark of Saturn 
in Aries (wildfires, eruptions, droughts). For Wheat, these areas would be China, India, and Russia. 
For Corn, it would be the United States, China, and Brazil. And for Soybeans, Brazil, the United 
States, and Argentina. Any widespread hot and dry conditions or lack of adequate rainfall in these 
parts of the world has the potential to light a fire (pun intended) under Corn, Soybeans, and/or Wheat 
this coming year.
Aiding in the potential for a significant drought to develop somewhere in the world during 2026 
and into 2027 is the fact that three outer planets (Jupiter, Saturn, and Neptune) will be in fire signs 
(Aries and Leo) during much of 2026 before fiery Mars adds to this energy when it enters the sign of 
Leo on September 27, where it will remain until November 25. To follow this alignment, there will 
be an even bigger collection of six planets in fire signs during the spring of 2027, when Venus and 
Mercury will join the party as they transit the sign of Aries during April and May 2027. That is a lot 
of heated energy potential in the sky at one time. On top of this, we will have the disruptive planet 
Uranus entering the air sign of Gemini at the end of April. We could see an increase in high winds or 
destructive storm activity during the 2026 growing season.
During 2026, we will want to pay attention when Mars (and sometimes Venus) is making hard 
aspects with Jupiter, Saturn, and Neptune. As mentioned, these planets will reside in fire signs this 
year and could usher in changes in weather patterns to become more arid, hot, and dry. We should also 
pay attention to when Mars forms hard aspects to Uranus (unpredictable) and Pluto (destructive), as 
severe weather around these times could cause more localized events of crop damage.
## Page 167

163
At the end of the day, weather and climate are fickle creatures. They are a construct of hundreds 
of variables, each continuously affecting the other and constantly changing the outcome. There is a 
reason why local weather forecasters get a bad rap for not being able to accurately predict the weather 
even seven days out—because it’s difficult. All we can do is look at the past and apply those possi-
bilities to the future. For 2026 and into 2027, the heavens are pointing to an elevated risk of adverse 
weather significant enough to affect crop production to a meaningful degree. That does not mean that 
it is going to happen by any means, but it is prudent that we are aware of the possibility.
## Page 168

164
 CORN
REVIEW
Corn peaked for the year at 504.50 in February 2025. This was not shocking, as last year’s Forecast 
2025 stated: “I would look for Corn to at least test 475.00 at some point during 2025 with an eventual 
upside target of 540.00–600.00. A lot will depend on the growing season in North and South America as 
to how long and how high Corn can rally.” Growing conditions were generally good in North and South 
America, so after peaking, Corn spent the next six months falling to a low of 368.75 in August 2025. This 
was 8.25 cents above the August 2024 low of 360.50 and was likely a successful retest of this long-term 
bottom. Since bottoming, Corn has caught a bid, retracing about 50% of the decline off the February high.
Corn Cycles

THE 18-YEAR CYCLE
The longest cycle we measure in Corn is the 18-year cycle. It has a range of 15–21 years and 
last bottomed in April 2020 at 300.25. This low was 20 years after the previous 18-year cycle low 
in August 2000, so it was on time. The year 2026 will begin the sixth year of this current 18-year 
cycle, which is not due to bottom again until 2038 +/– 3 years. The high so far for this current 18-year 
cycle occurred in April 2022 when Corn reached 827.00. This was a gain of 175% from the start of 
the cycle. While impressive, it is still a little short of the average trough-to-peak gains of previous 
18-year cycles, which are 308% when throwing out obvious outliers. 
Because we are still relatively early in this 18-year cycle, there is still plenty of time for Corn to 
mount another substantial rally. In fact, in the last three 18-year cycles, the crest formed beyond the half-
way point of the cycle (right translation) in two of them. In the third case, the high occurred in the first 
half of the cycle, but that high was tested (forming a double top) during the second half. This implies 
that Corn has a good chance of at least revisiting the all-time high of 827.00 at some point in the future. 
While we are using 2020 as the starting year for this current 18-year cycle, I think an alternative 
starting year should be entertained. Since 1912, every 18-year cycle in Corn has bottomed within 0–2 
years (usually 0–1) of Wheat’s 18-year cycle. Wheat’s last 18-year cycle bottomed in 2016, so the 2020 
low in Corn would have been four years later. This does not fit the historical cycle relationship between 
these two grains. However, Corn did have a low in August 2016 when it fell to 301.00. This is extremely 
close to the April 2020 low of 300.25—close enough to be considered a double bottom to the August 
2016 low and not the start of this current 18-year cycle. The implication here is that instead of Corn 
being in the sixth year of its 18-year cycle, 2026 would be the 10th year measured from the August 2016 
low. The magnitude of the decline from the 2022 high would argue that this labeling might be a better 
fit. In fact, as time goes by, this is more and more becoming my preferred bias.
## Page 169

165
THE 9-YEAR CYCLE
The 18-year cycle traditionally breaks down into two 9-year cycle phases. The 18-year cycle can 
also break down into a three-phase pattern of 6-year cycles, but these can be hard to distinguish from 
the 4.6-year half-cycle to the 9-year cycle. Depending on the correct starting year for the 18-year 
cycle (this would also be the starting year for the 9-year cycle, as shorter cycles reset when longer 
cycles culminate), 2026 will either begin the sixth year of the first 9-year cycle phase measured off 
the April 2020 bottom or the second year of the second 9-year cycle phase measured off the August 
2024 bottom. My bias at the moment lies with the latter.
If my bias is correct and we are indeed two years into the second and final 9-year cycle phase, 
then there are historical criteria to watch out for. First, these second 9-year phases rally for only 
2–4 years before topping out. This makes 2026 an early candidate for a 9-year cycle crest to form. 
Second, the percentage gains in this crest have ranged from 119% to 193%. A 119% gain from the 
360.50 low would equate to about 790.00. Reaching this price target would satisfy the third cri-
terion of Corn, at least testing and even exceeding the crest that occurred in the first 9-year cycle 
phase (827.00 in this case). 
To be fair, this would be a substantial move if it were to all occur in 2026, so this may be some-
thing that we will need to revisit in Forecast 2027. However, the move higher has to start somewhere, 
so we may see a nice surge in Corn prices this year with the geocosmic and fundamental backdrop 
in play.
THE 4.6-YEAR AND 33-MONTH CYCLES
If the 9-year cycle is breaking down in a three-phase pattern, it typically consists of three 
33-month cycles. If the 9-year cycle is breaking down into a two-phase pattern, then we usually see 
two 4.6-year cycles (55 months) form. The orb of this 55-month cycle is a little wide at 14 months, 
but that is what you get when analyzing a commodity largely dictated by the weather. In the last few 
instances, the 9-year cycle has been showing a preference for deploying in a two-phase pattern, so we 
will go with the idea that this is going to continue in the current cycle. 
## Page 170

166
If we assume the 18- and 9-year cycles bottomed in 2016, then the April 2020 low would have 
occurred 44 months later and in the time band for a 55-month bottom to form. Measuring from the 
April 2020 low, the August 2024 bottom was 52 months later—again, right on time for a 55-month 
low, and since it was the second 55-month cycle phase, August 2024 was probably a 9-year low as 
well. After an initial rally to the 27-month (half the length of the 55-month cycle) moving average, 
Corn came back to test the 2024 low in August 2025. This is tracing out a similar pattern seen at pre-
vious 9-year lows (the 2008–2009 bottom) and bodes well for the price of Corn in 2026 and onward 
should it continue.
I will be watching for Corn to start closing above the 27-month moving average in 2026, fol-
lowed by the 18-month moving average climbing above the 27-month. This has been a strong signal 
that Corn has indeed formed at least a 4.6-year low. As of this writing in early November, those 
moving averages are sitting around 427.00 and 437.00, and Corn is now poking above the 27-month 
moving average. 
The smallest percentage gain of 55-month cycles has been 30%, but this was in a bearish cycle. 
In bullish first-phase cycles (which I think we are in), the smallest gain has been 54%, while the 
largest was 311%. A 54% rise from the 360.50 low in August 2024 equates to 555.00. Therefore, I 
think 555.00 +/– 25.00 is a reasonable price target for Corn to reach this year. If we do see a drought 
pattern develop over a major corn-producing region of the world, as the Saturn–Neptune conjunction 
suggests is possible, then 601.00 +/– 29.00 becomes a valid price target. 
GEOCOSMICS
Two major geocosmic signatures in 2026 could significantly influence the Corn market. The 
first is the Saturn–Neptune conjunction occurring on February 20, 2026. Like other grains, both 
Saturn–Neptune conjunctions and oppositions have coincided with peaks in grain markets. Since 
1950, there have been two conjunctions and two oppositions. In these previous instances, Corn 
has formed an important crest (18- and 9-year crests) within 8–15 months of the exact aspect. 
Measuring from February 2026, eight months takes us to October 2026, while 15 months takes 
us to July 2027.
The second major aspect for Corn is Jupiter forming a waxing trine to Saturn. In the previous 
three instances of this multi-pass aspect, going back to 1966, Corn has formed significant highs 
during the central time band of this aspect or within four months of the first or last passage. These 
include the 9-year high in August 1966, the 9-year drought high of July 1988, and the June 2008 
9-year high. The central time band of the coming Jupiter–Saturn waxing trine is August 2026–July 
2027. Also, keep in mind that this aspect is occurring with both planets located in fire signs. 
There is a planet/sign combination that has been strongly correlated to crests in the grain 
markets: Ceres transiting the signs of Gemini and Cancer. For those who are unfamiliar, Ceres is 
a dwarf planet that was the goddess of agriculture, grain, and the harvest in Roman mythology. 
Looking back to 1966, Corn has formed at least a 33-month cycle top, or a high followed by at least 
a 20% decline, more than 90% of the time when Ceres was between 5° Gemini and 26° Cancer. 
Ceres enters Gemini in May 2026 and will not exit the sign of Cancer until May 2027 due to its 
retrograde motion.
## Page 171

167
CONCLUSION
Corn looks to have successfully retested its August 2024 low during 2025 and now appears 
poised to muster a rally in 2026 and possibly lasting into 2027. Closing above the 27-month moving 
average on a monthly basis is essential to confirming this bias. If Corn can do that, taking out the Feb-
ruary 2025 high of 504.50 would then set a technical uptrend of higher highs and higher lows. This 
would then open the door for Corn to reach our conservative price target of 551.00 +/– 25.00. Should 
weather become an issue this year, then 601.00 +/– 29.00 is certainly achievable in 2026.
Based on geocosmics, the best time for Corn to reach these targets is in the second half of 
2026—specifically, September +/– 1 month and then November 20 +/– 2 weeks. It should be noted 
that many of the long-term aspects coinciding with a potential crest in Corn are still in effect in the 
first half of 2027. As such, a high that occurs in 2026 might be followed by a significant decline into 
a 33-month cycle low (due November 2026–November 2027) before another rally takes Corn into a 
more important high in early 2027.
## Page 172

168
 W HEAT
REVIEW 
Wheat was by far the weakest of the three grain markets in 2025, but that was not a complete sur-
prise. Last year’s Forecast 2025 book: “For this reason, my bias is that a 36-month cycle low is still 
ahead of us,” and “… Wheat doesn’t have to drop appreciably below the August 2024 low of 493.50 
when this 36-month cycle does form. It could be just a double bottom or a retest of that low.” Wheat 
did just that by hitting 492.25 in August 2025 and is now rallying above critical moving averages as 
we close the book on 2025. 
Wheat Cycles
Start/Progress as of 1/1/26
Next Due
18-year
August 2016, 10th year
2034 +/– 2 yr
9-year
August 2024, 2nd year
2033 +/– 2 yr

THE 18-YEAR CYCLE
The longest cycle we measure in Wheat is the 18-year cycle. It has a range of 16–20 years, mak-
ing it the most reliable long-term cycle of all three grain markets. This 18-year cycle last bottomed in 
August 2016 at 359.50 and is next due to bottom in 2034 +/– 2 years. The year 2026 will begin the 10th 
year of the current cycle. So far, Wheat has satisfied one of the criteria of a bullish cycle by trading 
above the previous 18-year cycle crest of 1272.75 when it reached a high of 1363.50 in March 2022 fol-
lowing Russia’s invasion of Ukraine, which is a major wheat-producing region of the world. The second 
criterion would be making new highs in the second 9-year cycle phase (which we could be in). For the 
current 18-year cycle, the simple Mid-Cycle Price (MCP) target, which represents the midpoint projec-
tion of the cycle’s expected price range, is 1,395.75 +/– 122.25. The 1272.75 high in 2022 is already 
within that range, which raises the question: has this 18-year cycle already topped out?
Looking at the historical data, Wheat’s 18-year cycles tend to form as double tops to each other. 
When considering this, the March 2022 high of 1363.50 could technically be considered a double 
top to the previous 18-year cycle crest of 1272.75, even though it was almost $1 higher. I think this 
adds to the argument that we probably have seen the high in Wheat for the remainder of this decade, 
barring a black swan type of event (nuclear war?).
THE 9-YEAR CYCLE
Wheat’s long-term 18-year cycle predominantly breaks down into two 9-year cycle phases. The 
9-year cycle last bottomed with the 18-year cycle in August 2016. It was next due to bottom in 2025 
+/– 2 years, which makes the August 2024 low of 493.50 and the October 2025 low of 492.25 both 
candidates for this bottom. I have adjusted my bias slightly and now consider August 2024 to be the 
start of this new 9-year cycle due to the fact that it formed within two weeks of the Jupiter–Saturn 
waxing square that took place on August 19, 2024. Generally, longer-term planetary aspects coincide 
with longer-term cycle tops and bottoms. In the case of Wheat, this would line up. October 2025 
would constitute a successful retest or double-bottom chart formation relative to the August 2024 
low, even though it was lower by a little over one penny.
## Page 173

169
If 2024 is indeed the correct starting year for this current 9-year cycle, 2026 will mark the second 
year of the second 9-year cycle phase. This is where it gets interesting. Since 1885 (yes, you read that 
right), six out of eight second-phase 9-year cycles have topped out in years 2–4 following the low. 
Since 1960, all four second 9-year phases have topped in the third year. This puts 2026 and 2027 in 
the crosshairs for when, historically, a 9-year crest could form. 
Further, the gains of these 9-year cycles have ranged from 25% to 437%. If we throw out the 
outliers, we have a more normal range of 43% to 154%. This yields a possible price target for a crest 
of 704.00–1251.00. A normal Fibonacci price target for a corrective high would be 826.00–1031.00 
and overlaps the price target just given. We will therefore use 928.00 +/– 103.00 as a possible target 
for the crest of this 9-year cycle. Based on historical precedent, this crest could even occur this year.
THE 36-MONTH CYCLE
The 9-year cycle typically breaks down into three 36-month cycle phases. This 36-month cycle 
carries an orb of eight months, which makes its range 26–44 months. It last bottomed with the 9-year 
cycle in August 2024. The previous two 36-month cycles bottomed in April 2019 and August 2022 
and were 32 and 40 months long, respectively. The low in August 2024 was only 24 months from 
the August 2022 low, so it was a little short of the normal range for this cycle. This is okay, however, 
because when longer cycles (such as the 9-year cycle) come due, shorter cycles distort about 50% 
of the time. Admittedly, the October 2025 low would be a better fit here time-wise, as it would have 
been 38 months from August 2022. However, the October bottom did not have a major long-term 
aspect associated with it, as the August 2024 low did, which is why I favor it over the more recent 
October 2025 low.
Regardless of the starting point, this will be the first 36-month cycle phase in a new 9-year cycle. 
First phases in any cycle are usually bullish, and this is indeed the case for Wheat. The average gain 
for a 36-month cycle that is beginning a new 9-year cycle is 84%, with a range of 57%–127%. The 
average time it takes to reach this crest is 26 months, with a range of 17–34 months. Using the August 
2024 low of 493.50, a 57% gain would imply a Wheat price of about 775.00, with an 84% gain reach-
ing about 908.00. Notice that this latter price falls into the possible price target for a 9-year crest given 
## Page 174

170
earlier. The 17th month from August 2024 is January 2026, while 26 months is October 2026. Taking 
all this into consideration, I think Wheat has an excellent chance of at least hitting 775.00 this year 
and doing so before October 2026.
While my bias is bullish heading into 2026, it should be noted that the start of this 36-month cycle 
has yet to be fully confirmed. It will take prices closing above the 9- and 18-month moving averages, 
with the 9-month average rising above the 18-month. Currently, those averages are around 525.00 
and 550.00, respectively. Wheat is testing the 18-month moving average at the time of this writing, 
so it would not take much additional strength to achieve initial confirmation. However, until this fully 
happens, any monthly (or even weekly) close below the double-bottom lows around 493.00 going 
forward would signal that the 36-month cycle has not bottomed and would be due by April 2026, 
which would be the 44th month from August 2022. Any new low after April 2026 would require 
revisiting the long-term cycle labeling.
GEOCOSMICS
There are two important geocosmic signatures taking place in 2026 that could influence Wheat 
prices. The first is the Saturn–Neptune conjunction on February 20, 2026. The section on weather 
noted that both Saturn–Neptune conjunctions and oppositions have coincided with peaks in grain 
markets. Since 1950, there have been two conjunctions and two oppositions. In these instances, 
Wheat has formed an important crest within 22 months of the exact aspect. Measuring from February 
2026, 22 months takes us out to December 2027. Because this window is somewhat longer than that 
of the other grain markets surrounding this aspect, it is conceivable that we see either a double-top 
pattern to a high made earlier or a case of bearish intermarket divergence—in which all the grains 
peak in their respective time bands for a meaningful crest, but Wheat makes a marginal new high not 
confirmed by the other grain markets later.
The second important aspect for Wheat is Jupiter forming a waxing trine to Saturn. In the previ-
ous three instances of this multi-pass aspect, going back to 1966, Wheat has formed significant highs 
during the central time band of this aspect. These include the final high in 1966 before a 40% decline 
into an 18-year low, the 18-month high and subsequent low that preceded the sharp move higher dur-
ing the 1988 drought year, the 9-year drought high of July 1988, and the 18-year high that occurred 
in 2008. The central time band of the coming Jupiter–Saturn waxing trine is August 2026–July 2027. 
Also, keep in mind that this aspect is occurring with both planets located in fire signs. 
In addition to the above signatures, Wheat also seems to respond to Jupiter in a waxing trine 
to Neptune. This aspect will be exact on July 20, 2026. In most cases, a tradable low has occurred 
within six weeks of this aspect in the Wheat market. This makes June 20–August 20 a potential bot-
tom in Wheat. This could be a simple primary cycle, but it also falls in the time band when the second 
12-month cycle would be due.
There is yet another planet/sign combination that has strongly correlated with crests in the grain 
markets: Ceres transiting the signs of Gemini and Cancer. For those unfamiliar, Ceres is a dwarf 
planet that was the goddess of agriculture, grain, and the harvest in Roman mythology. Looking back 
to 1966, the high that unfolds has typically been either a 9-year cycle crest or a retracement high fol-
lowed by at least a 30% decline. This has occurred in about 75% of the cases when Ceres was in either 
Gemini or Cancer. Ceres will transit Gemini from May 2026 through May 2027.
## Page 175

171
CONCLUSION
Wheat appears to have secured a double bottom to the August 2024 low in October 2025. If it 
can confirm this by closing above the 18-month moving average (it is close to doing so), and if the 
9-month moving average can cross above the 18-month, then we will assume Wheat is in the first 
36-month cycle phase of a new 9-year cycle. Because this is the first phase—typically the most 
bullish—I think 2026 could be a good year for Wheat prices; however, since this is the second 9-year 
cycle phase, the rally should ultimately prove corrective in nature, possibly similar to what transpired 
following the 2009 low (see monthly chart). Geocosmics indicate that we should look for this high 
within 22 months of the Saturn–Neptune conjunction taking place in February 2026. Using other 
geocosmic signatures, we can narrow this time band to August 2026–May 2027. 
The price target for this crest is ultimately 928.00 +/– 103.00. Whether we can reach that level 
in 2026 remains to be seen, but I do think 700.00–775.00 is a safe objective for this coming year. If 
at any point Wheat experiences a weekly close below 493.50, these upside targets will have to be 
adjusted, as this would signal that Wheat is not in a new 36-month and 9-year cycle. In this case, a 
low would be due by April 2026.
